# Architecture Decision Records

This directory contains the Architecture Decision Records (ADRs) for **My Financial Life**. ADRs capture significant technical and architectural decisions made during the project, including the context that motivated them, the options considered, and the consequences of the decision taken.

---

## What is an ADR?

An Architecture Decision Record is a short document that captures a single architectural decision. Each ADR records:
- **Context** — the situation or problem that required a decision
- **Options considered** — the alternatives evaluated
- **Decision** — what was decided and why
- **Consequences** — the positive outcomes, trade-offs accepted, and ongoing responsibilities

ADRs are written at the time a decision is made and are not retrospective documents. Once accepted, an ADR is not edited to reflect subsequent changes — instead, a new ADR is written that supersedes or amends it.

---

| [ADR-057](ADR-057-automatic-rotating-snapshots.md) | Automatic rotating database snapshots + clean-close checkpoint — closeEvent runs `wal_checkpoint(TRUNCATE)` so the single `.mfl` is self-contained on quit; rotating timestamped copies in a `Snapshots/` folder beside the live DB (on launch, a 30-min in-session timer, and clean close), keep last 10, change-detection skips duplicates; restore = File ▸ Open; extends ADR-016's auto-commit model | 2026-06-12 | Accepted |
| [ADR-058](ADR-058-budget-redesign-envelope-zero-sum-planning.md) | Budget redesign (umbrella) — hybrid envelope/zero-sum/long-term-planning; **per-month allocations** (copy-forward on edit) replace ADR-024's amortized amount+cadence; multiple budgets + scenarios; budget period (default Jan–Dec); 12-month editable matrix (Budget/Actual/Diff by income/expense/transfer) + per-section Unbudgeted rows; soft Unallocated indicator vs the perimeter-account pool; auto-rollover (reallocate by editing); historical-average suggestions; projected burn-down. Migration 0019 (`budget_line` + `budget_allocation`, drop `budget_category`); migration 0020 (`account.credit_limit` + `budget_account.contribution`, R4a); migration 0021 (`budget_goal`, R4b). Supersedes ADR-024/025; keeps perimeter cancellation + nearest-ancestor bucketing + pure `budget_calc`. Phased R1–R4: R1–R4b shipped (R2 rollover/role controls; R3 monthly view + projected burn-down; R4a credit cards as a pool source; R4b pay-down goals — pure `goal_calc`, balance-based progress, a goals strip in both views) + an annual-matrix polish pass (Total column, Net line, collapsible sections, section-header budget totals); R4c = savings goals remaining | 2026-06-13 | Accepted (R1–R4b shipped) |
| [ADR-059](ADR-059-data-library-test-dataset-management.md) | Data Library — visual save/load of whole `.mfl` datasets for juggling test data. New `Library/` folder beside the live db (parallel to ADR-057's `Snapshots/`); **File ▸ Manage Data…** (`Ctrl+Shift+D`) modal lists named saves + snapshots, each with Load / Save current as… / Rename / Delete. **Load takes a fresh working copy** — clones the dataset *onto* the working file (read-only source, temp-and-atomic-replace) so the saved original stays pristine; contrast `File ▸ Open` which makes the picked file itself live. Qt-free `data_library.py`; `_swap_repository` refactored into `_adopt_repository`/`_teardown_repository`; loaded dataset name shown in the title. Fulfils ADR-057's deferred "Restore from snapshot…". No schema change | 2026-06-13 | Accepted |
| [ADR-060](ADR-060-configurable-snapshot-retention-gfs.md) | Configurable grandfather-father-son snapshot retention — replaces ADR-057's flat `keep newest 10` (which a busy day exhausts in hours, losing every older restore point) with a thinning GFS policy: keep *all* within `subdaily_hours`, then *one per day* to `daily_days`, then *one per month* to `monthly_months` (defaults 24h/7d/12mo). Four knobs in the `setting` table per file (`RetentionPolicy` + `load_policy`/`save_policy`, floor-clamped); `prune(db_path, policy, now)` rewritten as the GFS bucketer (`_stamp_of` parses the filename timestamp; non-matching files never deleted). New `SnapshotSettingsDialog` (four spin boxes + live summary) reached via a `Settings…` button on the Data Library Snapshots tab; capture timer re-armed live on change + per-file on adopt. Amends ADR-057; closes its "promote constants to `setting` rows" item. No migration | 2026-06-13 | Accepted |
| [ADR-061](ADR-061-register-search-debounce-and-filter-cost.md) | Register search performance — searching the **All** date window on a big account (13.5k rows) froze on every keystroke. Three view/model-layer fixes: **(a)** debounce the Search box (200 ms single-shot timer; a typing burst → one filter pass); **(b)** precompute each row's lowercased search haystack once (`TransactionTableModel._search_blobs`, refreshed on load + inline edit) so `filterAcceptsRow` is a single substring test (~15 ms → ~2 ms/pass) instead of rebuilding seven fields + two amount formats per row per keystroke; **(c)** coalesce the status-bar refresh via a zero-delay single-shot timer so one filter invalidation walks the visible rows once, not 2–3×. The follow-on to ADR-041's flagged "All is still slow on huge accounts", scoped to search rather than sort. No migration, no Repository change. **Amended 2026-06-14:** `category_name` added to the haystack (Search now matches categories) and the register's Category filter combo removed | 2026-06-14 | Accepted |
| [ADR-062](ADR-062-register-date-amount-filters.md) | Register date-range + amount-range filters — a "Filters ▾" popover (`register_filters_popover.py`) with checkbox-gated date From/To + **signed** amount Min/Max + Clear, applied live; an active-filter dot on the button. Date/amount filtering is proxy-level (in-memory, like Search — ADR-061), so no schema/Repository change. One coupling: a date-From earlier than the loaded "Show" window auto-widens the load via `_effective_since() = min(preset_since, filter_from)` so an early From is reachable. Owner forks (`AskUserQuestion`): separate From/To fields (not a Show "Custom range…"), signed amounts (not magnitude), popover (not a second row/inline). Part of register tidy-up Arc A (A5) | 2026-06-14 | Accepted |
| [ADR-082](ADR-082-date-period-standardisation.md) | Date & period standardisation (launch-plan P1) — one period vocabulary + one date-edit factory. The audit found 3+ preset vocabularies, period-bounds maths duplicated in 4 places (`account_summary.period_bounds`, the register's `_months_before`/`_current_since`, inline `_resolve_bounds` in the Sankey + Investment windows), the label dict copy-pasted into ~10 files, **and a latent bug** — the register computed `6m`/`12m` calendar-accurately while `account_summary` used day-deltas, so `"6m"` meant two different windows. New Qt-free **`mfl_desktop/periods.py`** owns the one `PERIOD_LABELS` registry, the per-context preset SETS (`REGISTER`/`REPORT`/`INVESTMENT`/`SANKEY` — keys unchanged so saved `filters_json` is stable), one `period_bounds(...)` for every key, `months_before`/`period_since`/`fmt_date_range`/`period_label`/`labels_for`/`options_for`; new Qt **`ui/date_widgets.py`** has `make_date_edit` (calendar popup + the `d MMM yyyy` format per P1a) + `make_period_combo`. `account_summary` + `reports/filters` **re-export** the vocab under their historical names (zero importer churn); the register, Sankey + Investment windows drop their inline maths; all ten `_PERIOD_LABELS` dicts removed (8 reuse `account_summary.PERIOD_LABELS`, 2 use the full registry). Deliberate alignment: month/year windows are now **calendar-accurate everywhere** (report `6m`/`1y`/`3y`/`5y` shift 0–3 days off day-deltas — intended). Rejected: one preset set everywhere (sets legitimately differ + breaks persisted keys), hand-syncing the duplication (that drift was the bug). **Verified**: periods unit tests, delegation parity, app import, offscreen filter-dialog + register checks. Follow-up "P1 part B": roll `make_date_edit` across the ~14 `QDateEdit` sites for the one date format. Amends ADR-033/041/056/046/064/066/068 | 2026-06-16 | Accepted |
| [ADR-083](ADR-083-report-drill-down-completion.md) | Report drill-down completion (launch-plan P2) — every report reaches the ledger. The four **dead-end** reports (Sankey, Income & Expense, Investment Returns, Net Worth) become clickable, reusing the shared `TransactionsListWindow` (ADR-034) like Spending/Payee/Category-&-Payee/Account-Summary already do. Adds two `TxnListFilter` dimensions + `DrillDownFilterProxy` filters: **kind** (`for_kind` — Income & Expense; matches `income_expense_series`'s exact predicate: non-transfer, kind's category set, sign by kind, so the drill reconciles with the bar) and **security** (`for_security` — Investment Returns). **Sankey**: `SankeyNode` gains `category_id` (None for Other/balance nodes) → `node_clicked` → `for_category` (+descendants). **Income & Expense**: chart `segment_clicked(kind, bucket_key)` + new pure `income_expense.bucket_bounds(key, mode)` (inverts a bucket key to its calendar span; week per `%W`) → `for_kind`. **Investment Returns**: chart is portfolio-level, so the per-security **table** drills — sid stashed on the row (`_SID_ROLE`), double-click → `for_security`. **Net Worth**: `DonutChild` gains `account_id` → `account_clicked` → window re-emits `account_activated` → `register_window._open_account_summary` (owner fork: the Account Summary page, not the flat register). **Budget already satisfied** — its matrix double-click-drills into `BudgetDrillDownWindow` (a txn-id-set editable register that reconciles exactly with the cell); deliberately kept over the shared window (the perimeter bucketing can't be expressed by the shared filters). Kind/security chips non-removable (defining dimension); account scope mirrors ADR-066 (single→per-account, else cross-account). Owner forks: IE→that month's txns, Net Worth→Account Summary, all in one arc. Known limits (noted, deferred): split fidelity, `include_transfers`, archived categories. **Verified** offscreen on a seeded DB (all five drills + `bucket_bounds` round-trip + donut paint + app import) | 2026-06-18 | Accepted |
| [ADR-084](ADR-084-de-overlap-shared-report-filter-base.md) | Remove overlapping functionality (launch-plan **P3**) — first slice. The de-overlap rule: consolidate divergent *duplicates of the same thing*, never prune distinct *affordances*. **P3a:** the six report filter dialogs (spending / income-expense / payee / category-payee / investment-returns / sankey) were ~40% copy-paste — `_set_combo_to`, `_initial_custom_dates`, `_sync_custom_visibility`, the period-combo + custom-date triad, the granularity list, the transfers tooltip, the all-checked→`[]` normalisation, the OK/Cancel scaffold all re-declared. New **toolkit** base `ui/report_filter_dialog_base.py` (`ReportFilterDialogBase`) offers opt-in builders (`_make_period_combo`/`_make_custom_dates`/`_make_granularity_combo`/`_make_transfers_check`/`_make_top_n_spin`/`_make_accounts_panel`) + shared helpers (`_period_and_custom`/`_checked_or_all`/`_finalise`/`values`) + the statics; each dialog keeps its specials (rollup, securities panel, top-N, category tree). Sankey adopts partially (no period, tuple return). Constructor signatures unchanged; persisted `filters_json` round-trips identically. Audited & kept as legitimate affordances: schedules' 4 entry points, `TransactionsListWindow` nav (transfer-match chips = P3b). Fixed a latent bug — the unified seeder guards `period_bounds`' `None` start for unbounded `max`/`all` (Investment default). Amends ADR-039/046/056/064/066/068. **Verified** headless across all six. P3b/P3c pending | 2026-06-18 | Accepted |
| [ADR-085](ADR-085-cross-source-duplicate-detection.md) | Cross-source, count-aware duplicate detection on import — closes a hole where the same real transaction from a *different* source (OFX FITID vs a Banktivity composite hash vs a feed `transactionId`) carried a different `import_hash` and silently re-imported (a real import duplicated ~46 June rows). The naive "match exists → skip" is rejected: people legitimately spend the same amount at the same payee several times in days. **Count-aware matching** pairs each import row to a *distinct* existing row, each claimed at most once (reuses `transfer_reconcile.greedy_pair`), so 1-in-register absorbs only 1 of N. New pure `import_engine/dedupe.py` (exact signed amount + date ±window hard filters; `score_candidate` orders same-day / same-payee first; strength = same-day-or-payee-overlap → default-skip, else weak → opt-in). Repository `list_dedupe_candidates`; `_classify_and_stage` runs the batch pass; confirm = **merge** a manual placeholder or **skip** an already-imported dup. New `ImportReviewDialog` shown **only when** dupes are flagged (clean imports still silent); feeds auto-confirm strong only. Amends ADR-010/077. **Verified** headless (pure matcher multiplicity/strength/pairing + stage→commit integration + dialog) | 2026-06-19 | Accepted |
| [ADR-086](ADR-086-investment-transaction-categories.md) | User-editable categories on investment transactions, scoped to the cash income/expense actions — they already carry an auto-derived, *locked* `category_id` (Div/ReinvDiv/interest/cap-gain → *Investment income*, else Uncategorised), invisible and uneditable. Owner decisions (`AskUserQuestion`): goal = **reports & budget**; scope = **cash income/expense actions only** (dividends / interest / cap-gains / fees / manual Cash in-out — **not** Buy/Sell/share-transfer/split, which would inject trade amounts into the cashflow reports); editing = **dialog picker + inline column**. New pure `qif_actions.is_categorisable` (+ `CASH_EXPENSE_ACTIONS`) is the safety gate. `InvestmentTransactionDialog` shows a category picker for those actions (income default, edit pre-selects). `COLUMNS_INVEST` gains a Category column, inline-editable **only for categorisable rows** (per-row `flags()`/`setData()` gate; the Category cell's double-click edits inline instead of opening the dialog). **No report/budget change** — kind-based aggregation already does the right thing; restricting which actions can be categorised is the whole mechanism. Amends ADR-043/048. **Verified** headless (classification + model gate + dialog visibility/default/save) | 2026-06-19 | Accepted |
| [ADR-087](ADR-087-home-budget-card-measures-against-available.md) | Home dashboard budget card measures spend against envelope **available** (allocation + rollover), not bare `allocation` — it falsely flagged "over" while the Budget window said "under" for the same month (the card compared spend to the header's *Assigned* figure). `cell.available` matches the ADR-058 envelope model. Amends ADR-075 | 2026-06-20 | Accepted |
| [ADR-088](ADR-088-income-over-time-report.md) | Income Over Time report + category filter on Income & Expense — the income-side mirror of Spending Over Time (strict inflow: `kind='income'` AND `amount>0`), built by generalising `SpendingReportWindow` over a `_Direction` descriptor (`IncomeReportWindow` is a one-attribute subclass); new `income_aggregates` + `IncomeOverTimeFilters` + **migration 0028** (report-type CHECK widen) + menu/catalog/dispatch. **Also amends ADR-064:** a category filter on Income & Expense (`category_ids` clause on `income_expense_series`, picked parents expand to descendants) | 2026-06-20 | Accepted |

| [ADR-094](ADR-094-budget-bills-and-stepped-burndown.md) | Budget bills (scheduled-backed lines) + stepped burn-down — a **bill is a budget line backed by a real `scheduled_txn`** (the schedule owns the date/cadence/amount/account a category-level line lacks). **Migration 0030** adds `budget_line.scheduled_txn_id` (NULL = ordinary envelope; `ON DELETE SET NULL`). The burn-down (`compute_burndown`) becomes **bill-aware + stepped**: ideal is a staircase (each planned bill a step at its due day, discretionary remainder linear); projection = actual + the **unpaid** bills (amount-matched against actuals, overdue→step at today) + the discretionary run-rate on non-bill spend only — so a **paid bill flattens** and weekly/twice-monthly bills contribute one step per in-month occurrence. `burn_down_chart.py` rebuilt as a filled **staircase** (replacing the three thin diagonal dashed lines, 2b). Owner forks: bill setup pulls **existing schedules** into the budget (adjustable); a new bill from a line opens the full **Schedule dialog** (for the paying account); schedule→budget reverse-sync **asks each time**; paid detection = **amount-match**. | [ADR-093](ADR-093-bonds-and-options.md) | Bonds & options as first-class securities — the equity-only engine (qty × price, market value = Σ shares × price, basis = net cash) broke for the two classes the owner trades: **bonds** quote as a **% of par** in par multiples (45 bonds £1,000 par @ 99.618 = £44,828.10, plus coupon/maturity/**accrued interest** — cash but not basis) and **options** trade in **contracts** of a multiplier (×100) priced as a premium/share. Fix expresses both via one per-security **`price_multiplier`** (stock 1; bond face/100; option contract_size) so the engine's `shares × price` is preserved by passing × multiplier at the value sites; descriptive metadata (coupon/maturity/cusip; underlying/strike/expiry/type/size) rides alongside. **Accrued interest** (`txn.accrued_interest`) is in the cash but subtracted back out of basis (buy) and proceeds (sell). **Migration 0029** (security instrument_type + 11 metadata cols + price_multiplier; `txn.accrued_interest`) — all defaulted/nullable, so an equity portfolio is byte-for-byte unchanged. Holdings/value-history/returns engines gain optional `multipliers` + accrued awareness; the 5 callers pass `security_multipliers()`. Dialog: Instrument combo (Stock/Bond/Option) reveals per-class fields + accrued, multiplier-aware tri-field solver; Stock Record shows the metadata. Basic options only (long buy→sell/expire-worthless; no exercise/assignment). Reuses Buy/Sell (no new actions). **Verified** headless (bond basis 44848.10 vs MV 44828.10 with accrued excluded; option ×100; stock unchanged; get/update_security round-trips) + offscreen Qt (dialog create/edit + Stock Record) | 2026-06-21 | Accepted |

| [ADR-099](ADR-099-release-engineering-hygiene.md) | **Release engineering hygiene: pinned desktop deps, build metadata, local crash log + diagnostics export** (backlog item **P6**). The audit found two gaps: the desktop app's dependencies were pinned **nowhere** — the repo-root `requirements.txt` pins the legacy v0.1 FastAPI/Oxigraph web app and doesn't even list PySide6 — while a scan of every top-level and lazy import across `mfl_desktop/` showed the real third-party surface is tiny (PySide6, `cryptography`, `ofxtools`; the FX and price clients use stdlib `urllib`); and there was no logging, no crash handling and no build revision, so an uncaught exception vanished silently and a non-technical user had no way to file a useful report. Decisions: (1) new `requirements-desktop.txt` pinning the three direct runtime deps, leaving the legacy file untouched with a cross-reference header in each; (2) `version.py` gains `build_revision()` reading an optional CI-stamped, gitignored `_build_info.py` and falling back to `"source"` (never shells out to git at runtime), surfaced as a muted "Build …" line in About; (3) `mfl_desktop/diagnostics.py` — the privacy-friendly, **no-telemetry** minimum: `setup_logging()` (rotating `<AppData>/MFL/logs/mfl.log`, idempotent, degrades to console-only on a read-only home), `install_excepthook()` (logs the traceback then shows a best-effort non-fatal dialog saying the data is safe and where the log is; re-entrant-guarded, chains to the previous hook, passes `KeyboardInterrupt` through), and `collect_diagnostics(repo)` / `write_diagnostics(dest, repo)` producing a **PII-light** blob exported via Help ▸ Export Diagnostics… — **nothing is sent anywhere**. Rejected: folding desktop deps into the existing `requirements.txt` (conflates two disjoint stacks); a hosted Sentry-style crash reporter (network dependency + data egress, against the local-first promise); embedding the git SHA by running git at startup (a frozen app has no git); a full transitive lock (deferred to the build scripts). **Verified** import-all across `mfl_desktop` = 135 modules / 0 failures; diagnostics exercised offscreen against a seeded file. Still open under P6: per-OS reproducible build env, PyInstaller specs, the full dependency lock, and a CI matrix. No schema change | 2026-06-21 | Accepted |
| [ADR-100](ADR-100-brand-palette-teal-gold.md) | **Brand palette — re-tone the accent from blue-600 to icon teal, add a gold brand token.** The owner produced hexagonal app-icon badges on a deep petrol-teal field with a gold mark; sampling the artwork gives the brand system (teal `#0e3a44`→`#1f6e78`→`#43a0a8`, gold `#c9a23a`→`#e3c560`, the sunset orange reserved as *MRL's* signature), which made ADR-026's `blue-600 #2563eb` accent off-brand. This **deliberately breaks ADR-076's "light value == the hex it replaced" discipline** (here, changing the look *is* the point); the break is scoped to the accent family, leaving the slate canvas, text ramp and semantic green/red untouched. New **`brand_gold`** token is **not** for text or money (gold-on-white is ~2.3:1) — a contrast-safe graphic accent, first used as the About box's divider rule. Rejected: gold hero/money numbers (contrast + semantic conflict), freezing the chart accent to a teal literal (too dark on the dark surface), re-toning the data blues, branding only the icon. **Verified** `py_compile` clean on 11 touched files; token resolution checked in both themes. | [ADR-104](ADR-104-packaging-scaffold.md) | **Packaging scaffold: PyInstaller spec, per-OS build scripts, CI matrix** — the as-built machinery implementing ADR-078's K0 decision, which had locked the approach but left "no spec/build scripts exist yet." The blocking unknown was which runtime data a frozen build must carry; an audit found exactly **one critical dependency** — the 31 `mfl_desktop/migrations/*.sql` files, loaded via a `__file__`-relative path, so without them bundled *and found* the packaged app applies **zero migrations and every database stays empty**. Decisions: (1) the one code change packaging required — `db/schema.py`'s `_migrations_dir()` returns `<sys._MEIPASS>/mfl_desktop/migrations` when frozen, else the source path; (2) one spec for both targets (`packaging/mfl.spec`, run per-OS since PyInstaller can't cross-compile) → macOS `.app` / Windows folder+exe, bundling the migrations and `assets/icons`, setting the per-OS bundle icon, building windowed, and **excluding the unused legacy web stack** (fastapi/uvicorn/pyoxigraph/rdflib/pydantic); (3) per-OS build scripts that stamp build metadata into the gitignored `_build_info.py` (git SHA + date, surfaced in About/diagnostics per ADR-099), run PyInstaller, and sign/notarize **only when the env vars are set** — so they yield a working *unsigned* build today and become a one-command signed release once the owner holds the certificates (K1/K2); (4) a GitHub Actions macOS+Windows CI matrix that runs the offscreen smokes, builds unsigned, and uploads the artifact on every push; (5) `requirements-build.txt` pinning PyInstaller separately from the runtime deps. Rejected: relying on `__file__` for migrations in the frozen app (PyInstaller doesn't guarantee a real filesystem `__file__`; the explicit `sys._MEIPASS` branch is the documented pattern); Briefcase (ADR-078 already settled PyInstaller); a onefile build (onedir launches faster and is simpler to sign/notarize); a Linux CI smoke job (the targets are macOS + Windows). **Verified** a real macOS build produced `My Financial Life.app` (159 MB) carrying all 31 migrations and 7 icon PNGs; the frozen binary launched headless and applied all 31 migrations from the bundle against a fresh DB, confirming `_MEIPASS` resolution. The Windows path is unrun locally (no Windows host) but symmetric and exercised in CI. | [ADR-105](ADR-105-backlog-usability-round.md) | **Backlog usability round — faster manual entry, report focus, editable drill-downs.** Four independent papercuts from real use, shipped as one round. (1) **Save & New**: `NewTransactionDialog` gains a third button that validates/accepts like Save but sets a flag; the register's handler is refactored so the per-dialog body moves into `_create_one_transaction(default_id)` and `_on_new_transaction` loops on it — so the dialog keeps cycling on the same account, while a plain Save, cancel, error or the Split… branch all stop the loop. (2) **Payee autocomplete in the modal dialog** — an optional `payee_names` list + a `QCompleter` in the same configuration `PayeeTypeaheadDelegate` (ADR-022) and `BulkEditDialog` already use, so all three surfaces behave identically. (3) **Report stays in front**: a report is a non-modal `QMainWindow` parented to the register, so accepting its modal filter dialog returned activation to the top-level parent and **buried the report** — `_on_open_filter` now calls `raise_()` + `activateWindow()` before applying the result; the other five report windows get the same one-liner (same shape, same latent bug). Rejected: reparenting the report to be top-level (the parenting is deliberate — closing the register closes its reports). (4) **Bulk edit in the drill-down**: `TransactionsListWindow` gains the register's edit triggers, the reconciled-edit guard and a `Ctrl+E` / context-menu **Bulk Edit N Transactions…**, reusing `BulkEditDialog` — **scope-limited to payee/category/status/memo** and refusing a transfer-kind category (with a pointer to the main register), because the register's transfer-conversion and split-discard machinery is deeply coupled to its own proxy/model. Rejected: extracting a shared "transaction table behaviours" mixin (cleaner long-term; recorded as the future direction if a third surface needs the verbs). View/dialog layer only — no schema change, no migration | 2026-06-25 | Accepted |
| [ADR-106](ADR-106-payee-category-inference-and-rules-visibility.md) | **Payee→category: history-inferred pre-fill + remembered categories surfaced in Rules** (owner: typing "Scot Rail" in New Transaction left the category *Uncategorised* despite many ScotRail txns filed under *Commuting*, and **Manage ▸ Rules… was empty** despite payees that clearly auto-categorise). Investigation showed neither is a defect but a **design gap**: there are **two independent** auto-categorisation mechanisms — the pattern **rules** the Rules dialog manages (owner has **0**) and the per-payee remembered category (`payee.default_category_id`, ADR-072; owner has **19** of 3,135 payees) — so auto-categorisation runs almost entirely off the mechanism the Rules screen doesn't show. The memory is also **sparse** (only written by the ADR-072 inline prompt or the Payees dialog — imports and bulk edits never record it) and the owner's payees are **fragmented** (`ScotRail`, `ScotRail London`, `SCOTRAIL`, `Scot Rail` are separate records; only one carried the memory; lookup is exact + case-sensitive). New read-only `Repository.most_common_category_for_payee(payee_id)` returns the most-frequent **non-Uncategorised, non-transfer** category across the payee **and its aliases**, ties broken by most recent `posted_date`; the register returns the explicit memory if set, **else** the inferred one. Scope is deliberately the **New Transaction pre-fill only** — it writes no memory (the explicit default stays the source of truth) and leaves the inline edit and the import categoriser explicit-only, so nothing silently bulk-reclassifies. New `list_payee_default_categories()` feeds a **"Remembered payee categories"** section in the Rules dialog with **Edit category…** and **Forget**, making that dialog's stated "whole automation picture in one place" goal actually true. Rejected: case-insensitive/fuzzy name matching (`Scot Rail` vs `ScotRail` are genuinely different records — merging is the real fix, deferred), auto-recording a memory whenever any category is set (owner chose inference — reflects all prior categorisation immediately, never silently writes), extending inference to the importer (would silently reclassify on every import). No schema change, no migration | 2026-06-25 | Accepted |

| [ADR-126](ADR-126-frozen-app-tls-ca-bundle.md) | **Frozen-app TLS trust store — point OpenSSL at certifi's CA bundle** (owner-reported: every price update failed with `CERTIFICATE_VERIFY_FAILED … unable to get local issuer certificate (_ssl.c:1010)` in the packaged macOS `.app`). Root cause: all HTTPS in the app is stdlib `urllib` on the **default** SSL context, and inside a PyInstaller bundle OpenSSL's default CA paths point at the missing *build-machine* prefix while macOS OpenSSL never falls back to the Keychain — so there is no CA to verify against (Windows loads the OS store, hence unaffected). certifi's `cacert.pem` was already in the bundle but nothing pointed at it. Fix: new `mfl_desktop/net_certs.py` `ensure_ca_bundle()` sets **`SSL_CERT_FILE=certifi.where()`** once at the top of `main()`, before any network I/O — one chokepoint covering Tiingo prices, FX, and all bank feeds. Override-safe (never clobbers an existing value), idempotent, exception-safe, no-op in dev / on Windows / when certifi absent. certifi promoted to an explicit pinned desktop dep + `collect_data_files("certifi")` in `mfl.spec` so the bundle is deterministic. Reproduced the exact `_ssl.c:1010` error and verified the fix against `api.tiingo.com`; `test_net_certs.py` 5/5 (base + CI interpreters) | 2026-07-01 | Implemented |

| [ADR-128](ADR-128-consistent-rounded-bar-corners.md) | **Consistent rounded bar corners across report charts** (owner-reported: some Spending Over Time bars have a nice rounded top, others a dated square top, inconsistently). Cause: each chart rounded its **top segment** as a rounded-top path but only when that segment was tall enough (`rect.height() > radius*1.4`) — a thin stacked cap fell back to a square `fillRect`; a per-segment path can't round a cap thinner than the radius. `investment_income` never rounded; the three charts used three different radius formulas. Fix: round the **whole bar** with one shared radius via new `chart_helpers.bar_corner_radius()` + `round_bar_corners()`, which **carves** the corner wedges to the plot-background colour — composes over an already-painted stack without needing segment colours, works at **any** height (thin cap rounds like a tall bar), and stays crisp under antialiasing (a filled arc, not an aliased `setClipPath`). Wired into spending (stacked, top), income_expense (income top / expense bottom), investment_income (top). Removed the two ad-hoc rounding blocks + divergent radius constants + dead `QPainterPath` imports. Horizontal payee chart left as-is. View layer only, no migration. `tests/test_bar_corners.py` 7/7 pixel-level (incl. a height-4 cap); verified across all three reports in light + dark | 2026-07-01 | Implemented |
| [ADR-129](ADR-129-net-expense-refunds-in-reports.md) | **Net-expense definition — reimbursements/refunds reduce spend across the flow reports** (owner-reported: a "Reimbursed" category showed **£1,730.79** on the Spending chart but the drill-down netted to **−£45.04** because reimbursements offset it). Five aggregates defined expense as **strict outflow** (`kind='expense' AND amount<0`, `SUM(-amount)`), silently dropping positive refund lines — so the bar showed gross money-out and couldn't reconcile with its own drill-down, and the report families disagreed. Fix: **net** definition everywhere — every expense line contributes its signed amount (a refund reduces its category), with a category/payee/cell that nets **≤£0 clamped to £0** (a stacked bar can't draw negative). | [ADR-130](ADR-130-transaction-status-lifecycle-and-reconcile.md) | **Transaction status lifecycle (confidence ladder) + status-driven reconciliation + precise OFX matching** (prompted by the June reconcile audit — a £16.17→£13.39 variance caused entirely by *status/selection*, not arithmetic: `pending` 30-June purchases and duplicate entries were reconcilable and got ticked). Replaces today's `Pending/Uncleared/Cleared/Reconciled` (copy-pasted in ~8 UI files + a 0001 `CHECK`) with a lowercase **confidence ladder**: **pending** (spent) → **cleared** (you saw it post) → **matched** (an OFX download matched/added it) → **reconciled** (statement-locked). Mostly a rename (`Uncleared→cleared`, `Cleared→matched`). Reconcile candidate set becomes **`matched`**, with an **optional "include cleared"** toggle (some banks offer no downloads — ADR-050), and `cleared`-in-range shown as a warning; `pending` never eligible; an unconfirmed `cleared` is flagged, never auto-reverted. Adds `bank_posted_date` (keep the spend date) so reconcile date-ranging aligns to the bank and the 22/23-June scramble stops. Import becomes a **reviewable, precise matcher** (amount exact + date window + canonical-payee fuzzy → auto / needs-review [incl. amount-differs → *adopt bank amount*, which would've caught the £13.39] / new-from-bank), reusing the existing FITID/`import_hash` dedup. Centralises the enum into `mfl_desktop/txn_status.py`. **Phased:** (1) status foundation — `txn_status.py` + migration 0033 (rename + `CHECK` rebuild via ADR-032 recipe) + register colours/legend; (2) reconcile-by-confidence (no schema change); (3) `bank_posted_date` (migration 0034) + the import review screen. Phases 1–2 already make the June bugs structurally impossible. **Phase 1 SHIPPED 2026-07-02** — `txn_status.py` (centralised enum + label/key helpers), migration 0033 (rename + `CHECK` rebuild via ADR-032 recipe + `legacy_alter_table` for the `txn_category_line` view), all ~16 modules repointed, combos show labels/store keys, account-summary labels → Confirmed/Unconfirmed; `test_txn_status_ladder.py` 6/6 + suite 23/23. **Phase 2 SHIPPED 2026-07-03** — `list_reconcilable_txns` gated by the ladder (matched always, cleared only with `include_cleared`, **pending never**, resumed ticks preserved); reconcile wizard "Include cleared" checkbox + auto-select + an excluded-cleared warning (`count_cleared_in_period`); `test_reconcile_confidence.py` 4/4 + suite 24/24. **Phase 3 CORE SHIPPED 2026-07-03** — 3a: migration 0034 `bank_posted_date`, download→match flips a hand-entered row `pending`/`cleared`→`matched` + records the bank date, reconcile ranges on `COALESCE(bank_posted_date, posted_date)`; 3b: `dedupe` amount-mismatch tier (payee-gated, ≤20%) → weak `amount_differs` review + "Adopt bank amt" (the £8.99-for-£8.25 fix); `test_import_bank_date.py` 4/4 + `test_import_amount_mismatch.py` 7/7 + suite 26/26. | [ADR-132](ADR-132-launch-dialogs-must-escape-the-splash.md) | **Launch-time dialogs must escape the always-on-top splash** (owner-reported, Windows: when the data file can't be opened at launch the error is *invisible* — behind the splash — so the app looks frozen). Root cause: the ADR-103 splash uses `Qt.WindowStaysOnTopHint`, which on Windows puts it in the OS **topmost z-order band** above every no-parent modal dialog — and all launch dialogs are parentless (no main window yet): the ADR-109 file-recovery prompt, the ADR-125 first-run folder picker + container-fallback warning, and the ADR-099 crash box. Two of those sites were added *after* the splash, so per-site fixes kept rotting. Fix once, centrally: `splash.py` tracks the splash it makes (`_active_splash`) and exposes idempotent **`dismiss_active_splash()`**; every launch-dialog site calls it first (recovery via the injected `dialog_factory` wrapper so `resolve_database` stays window-free/testable; the two ADR-125 sites; and `diagnostics._show_crash_dialog`, which also forces the box topmost as belt-and-suspenders). Happy path unchanged — no dialog fires, splash stays up until `finish(win)`. Rejected: dropping the stay-on-top hint (regresses ADR-103; two-topmost ordering still unreliable), per-dialog topmost+raise (topmost-vs-topmost race), inline `splash.hide()` per site (the pattern that already rotted). | [ADR-145](ADR-145-bare-transfers-no-irr-flow.md) | **Bare share-transfers don't distort the money-weighted return** (owner: SCHD showed −2.2% IRR against +41% total return). All 78 transfers in the data are bare. Net-safe — matched bare pairs already netted to zero; only single-sided bare transfers change (likelier artifacts). | [ADR-148](ADR-148-csv-date-order-inferred-per-column.md) | **Generic-CSV date order is inferred per column, not per row** (owner: a $12,000 MS Joint Brokerage → eTrade transfer dated 2021-05-12 never showed up in Reconcile Transfers). `_parse_generic_date` walked a fixed `strptime` list with `%d/%m/%Y` **before** `%m/%d/%Y` and returned on the first fit, so a US export parsed day-first whenever the day was ≤ 12 — `05/12/2021` became `2021-12-05`, 207 days from its counterpart and outside `find_transfer_pairs`' ±3-day guard. Rows with a day of 13+ failed DMY and landed correctly, making the corruption partial, interleaved, and invisible to the 5-row preview. The row is the wrong unit of decision: `05/12/2021` alone is undecidable, but one `05/14/2021` anywhere in the column proves month-first. Fix: `infer_day_first(samples)` votes on the whole column (field > 12 in position one ⇒ day-first, position two ⇒ month-first; ISO and junk abstain; `None` when never-disambiguating or self-contradictory) and `make_generic_date_parser` binds it into the parser both import call sites and the mapping dialog's preview now use — so preview and commit can no longer disagree. Undecidable columns fall back to day-first (historic behaviour, UK bias) with a log warning; the explicit date-format combo still overrides. Banktivity/QIF/OFX paths were never affected. Data repair: the bug is exactly invertible (`stored_day ≤ 12` ⟺ flipped), verified by reproducing the buggy parse and the correct parse from both source CSVs; 597/2667 rows fixed in (Closed) Amex Gold + 16/151 in MS Joint Brokerage, Standard Life Pension (a UK file) untouched. `test_csv_date_order.py` 15/15. | [ADR-149](ADR-149-home-refresh-defers-widget-destruction.md) | **Home refresh defers widget destruction (mouse-event use-after-free)** (owner: first-ever hard crash — `EXC_BAD_ACCESS` in `QApplication::notify` under `sendMouseEvent`, faulting at `0xffffffffffff11c0`). `QScrollArea::setWidget` deletes the widget it replaces **immediately**, and `HomeView.refresh()` rebuilt the dashboard that way. `RegisterWindow.changeEvent` refreshes Home on ActivationChange while Home is visible (ADR-063/075), so clicking the Bills card → `_on_manage_schedules` → `SchedulesDialog.exec()` (nested loop) → dialog closes → window re-activates → `refresh()` → the clicked `_Card` is freed while Qt still holds a raw pointer to it as the in-flight event receiver; `notify_helper` had already returned, so `notify` dereferenced freed memory as the click unwound. The `super()`-before-`emit()` comments in `_Card`/`_Row`/`_AccordionHeader` claimed safety but are necessary-not-sufficient — the dangling access is in Qt's code *after* our handler returns; comments corrected. Fix: `old = self._scroll.takeWidget()` (relinquish, don't delete) → `setWidget(container)` → `old.deleteLater()`, so the card outlives every frame pointing at it (and, when posted inside a modal's nested loop, outlives that too). Single-point fix: the other four `setWidget` calls are one-time constructor builds. Rejected: deferring the emit per-widget (symptom, 3 sites, leaves the gun loaded); a "not during a mouse event" flag on `changeEvent`; making Schedules non-modal. `test_home_refresh_use_after_free.py` 3/3 — subprocess-and-exit-code, since the regression segfaults rather than asserts (raw pattern still crashes Qt 6.11; real `refresh()` survives real clicks through a modal; old container alive on return, gone after one loop turn). Reverting the fix → 1/3. Full suite 39/39. No schema change | 2026-07-10 | Implemented |
| [ADR-150](ADR-150-net-worth-hero-trend-sparkline.md) | **Net-worth hero carries a 12-month trend sparkline (computed off-thread).** The Home hero (ADR-119) stated one figure in an otherwise empty card — the textbook "big number in a void": no direction, no context. The obvious fill is the 12-month series the Net Worth screen already computes (`net_worth_history.gather_net_worth_history`), but it is **computed-not-stored** (ADR-121) — every account's transactions replayed across each monthly sample and FX-converted at that date — measuring **~400 ms** against the live file versus ~168 ms for *all* the rest of `gather_home_data`. Folding it in would have tripled Home's build time on a surface that rebuilds on every window re-activation (ADR-063/075). So the heavy cards (trend + investment performance) are computed **off the UI thread** on a `QThreadPool` runnable with its own background `Repository` (a sqlite connection can't cross threads), handed back via a queued signal, and **cached against a cheap data signature** so they paint synchronously while the data is unchanged and only recompute when it moves. A new file / <2 months of history returns `None` and the hero is exactly the ADR-119 number-only card — no empty-chart state to design. The sparkline is a fourth hand-rolled chart (ADR-026) and shares the theme-at-paint-time convention, so ADR-076's live toggle repaints it for free; same source as the Net Worth screen, so hero and report can never disagree. No schema change | 2026-07-11 | Implemented (amended 2026-07-11) |
| [ADR-151](ADR-151-import-settlement-window-and-match-review.md) | **Import matching tolerates settlement gaps; net-new rows are reviewable** (owner: a real HSBC import created obvious duplicates and never surfaced them — a £588.38 Capital One payment and an £11.60 M6 toll, both **unique amounts**, each landing 3 days from an existing row). The cross-source matcher (ADR-085) only paired rows within **±2 days**, but posted-vs-cleared drift of 3 days is the *ordinary* case (a Friday authorisation settles Monday; a bank-holiday Monday takes 4). Phase 1 widens the window to **±4 days** and adds a weak **"possible"** tier (`match_duplicates` gains an optional `possible_window_days`, off by default, so existing callers/tests are unchanged); Phase 2 makes the import review show **net-new rows** with a **"Find match"** picker so an unmatched row can be paired by hand. Strong matches default-ticked to merge/skip; weak ones default to *keep*, so review stays low-friction. Investigated and **disproved** the owner's companion observation that existing rows had been "changed to cleared" — both had `bank_posted_date`/`import_batch` NULL and were already cleared; the commit path only writes to an existing row on a *confirmed* match. No migration; already-imported duplicates are untouched (owner declined an automated cleanup) — this only prevents new ones | 2026-07-11 | Implemented |
| [ADR-152](ADR-152-category-sunburst-top-group-and-clickable.md) | **Category & Payee "Where it goes" sunburst is a fixed top→group view, and clickable** (owner: it "isn't quite right"). Two faults. (1) **Wrong levels** — it rendered **group→leaf** while the report's bars/table show the **top-level** category, so the inner ring sat one level *below* the bars and read as a mismatch. It is now fixed at **top→group** *regardless* of the report's Group-by / Roll-up / Top-N / drill — a deliberately stable two-level overview (owner explicitly wanted it fixed, not tracking the roll-up combo, which is what caused the "it keeps changing" confusion). (2) **Inert** — `DonutSegment` gains a `segment_id` and the inner-ring hit now carries it (it was hard-coded `None`), so **both rings** are clickable and open `TransactionsListWindow` via `TxnListFilter.for_category` (descendants included, all payees, honouring the report's period + account scope). Backward-compatible: `segment_id` defaults `None`, so Net Worth's "account type" inner ring stays non-clickable exactly as before. Rejected: inner=top/outer=leaf (explodes into dozens of thin petals) and a new `slice_clicked` signal (reusing `account_clicked`'s int drill id needs no change to Net Worth). **Verified** headless on the live file: 16 top segments with groups nested; clicking top id 12 "Household" and group id 14 "Home and Garden" opens the right filtered windows. No schema change | 2026-07-11 | Implemented |
| [ADR-153](ADR-153-standard-life-pdf-to-qif.md) | **Standard Life pension statements: PDF → QIF, with prices solved from the switches** (Standard Life exports nothing machine-readable for a Group Stakeholder plan; the only artefact is a **PDF** covering 15 Apr 2005 → 9 Jul 2026 — 7 contributions, 37 Lifestyle "phased switches", closing £9,277.99. The account read **£2,263.31**: those 7 contributions, imported earlier from CSV as plain *cash* rows (ADR-148, batch 43) with no fund, units or price — so the pension showed its 2005 contributions and none of 21 years of growth, with no way to fix it by hand.) `tools/standard_life_pdf_to_qif.py` (operator tool, not shipped) emits a QIF the existing investment importer already understands, plus a unit-price CSV. Three obstacles, three findings: **(1) No prices** — insurer-internal funds have no ticker (Tiingo can never price them, the ADR-090 wall) and the statement prints exactly one price per fund, on the closing date. But a Lifestyle switch is not a partial rebalance: it **liquidates the whole plan and rebuys it**, so each switch states the same total twice (`sold_a·Pa + sold_b·Pb = total = bought_a·Pa + bought_b·Pb`) — two equations, two unknowns, solvable on all 37 dates, and *the only source of unit prices in the document*. Independently checkable: solving the closing date yields 123.91p / 116.38p against the statement's separately-published 124.0p / 116.4p (which are never fed in — rounded to 0.1p, they don't reproduce the stated fund values). **(2) Units don't conserve** — a Jul 2023 switch sells 2,202.631 units of `SL Managed P` when the contributions only ever bought 2,012.189. The drift is Standard Life crediting free units (the statement's "Total credits", £513.08): a share-in with no cash leg, emitted as `ShrsIn`, after which the replay lands on the closing units exactly. Their **dates are unrecoverable** (nothing is itemised 2005→2023), so they're booked in one lump at the first switch that reveals them — unit counts exact, **cost basis approximate and any gain/loss indicative**. Accepted: it's a tax-free wrapper, and inventing a schedule would be fabrication dressed as precision. **(3) The 29 Jul 2025 "switch" is a share-class re-designation** (`SL Managed P` → `SLMixAstMgdS7P`, `SL MAMgd2060 P` → `SLMan2060ShS7P`) — emitted `ShrsOut`/`ShrsIn`, which ADR-053 already defines as a custodian move carrying basis across; Sell+Buy would have booked a **phantom ~£8,000 realised gain**, and it's the one switch whose prices *aren't* recoverable (four unknowns, two equations) and needs none, since no cash moves. Guard rail: the tool **refuses to write unless the replay reconciles** against the statement's own investment summary, fund by fund, to the unit (exit 1) — everything else is inference, this is what makes it trustworthy. Its blind spot needed a second guard: under `--since`, the replay starts holding nothing and the credit mechanism will cheerfully fabricate the entire missing opening position *and still reconcile*, doubling the position on import — so selling a fund the replay doesn't hold is a hard error naming the exact `--hold` to pass. Result: the account reads **£9,277.99** (2,992.432 `SLMixAstMgdS7P` + 4,786.346 `SLMan2060ShS7P`, cash £0.00, nothing unpriced), every figure matching the statement to the penny, with 74 unit prices Jul 2023 → Jul 2026 so the funds chart plots the lifestyling period instead of a flat line; applied to the live DB after a `.backup` snapshot (225 rows, txn 39,565 → 39,790 — exactly +225). Writing the QIF against the app's real parser caught a defect that would otherwise have shipped: **QIF dates are US `M/D/Y`** (`qif_parser._parse_qif_date`) — a `D/M/Y` emitter had every row silently dropped, and every day ≤ 12 would have been transposed rather than rejected (same class as ADR-148, from the opposite direction). Rows carry **no provider IDs**, so the importer can't dedupe them: follow-up statements must use `--since` + `--hold`. No schema change | 2026-07-12 | Implemented |
| [ADR-154](ADR-154-reinvest-shows-cash-value.md) | **A reinvested dividend shows its cash value** (owner, editing a real 401(k) row of `23.893205` shares at `25.06`: *"there is no way to see the cash value, which is useful to make sure the other numbers are correct"*). The investment dialog gives Buy/Sell a **Total cost** row — the third leg of the ADR-093 tri-field qty ⇄ price ⇄ total solver — but a reinvest got Quantity and Price and nothing else, because the row genuinely moves no cash (signed impact 0, ADR-043). "No cash impact" is not "no cash value": the statement quotes the distribution as an **amount** (`$598.76`), the file stores it as shares × price, so with no total on screen there was nothing to check the two imported figures against and no way to go the other way. Fix: a new `_solves_total(kind)` predicate (`buy` / `sell` / **`reinvest`**) replaces the four scattered `kind in ("buy", "sell")` guards that gated the solver, so a reinvest gets the same tri-field total, labelled **Dividend amount**, solving in *both* directions — quantity + price fill the amount, and **amount + price back out the quantity**, so you can type the figure off the statement and let the dialog compute the fractional shares. **No commission leg**: `_solve_trade_field` now zeroes the commission term for anything that isn't a Buy/Sell — the Commission row is only *hidden* on a reinvest, not cleared, so a Buy → Reinvest switch with a fee typed would otherwise have folded a phantom `9.99` into the dividend (`_on_action_changed` re-solves on the switch for the same reason). The ADR-093 per-instrument multiplier still applies (a reinvest on a bond or option values correctly), and **the stored row is unchanged** — `_compute_amount` still returns `0.00`, so the field is an entry aid and cross-check, never a cash movement, and nothing downstream of the dialog sees a difference. Rejected: the hint line alone (read-only — checks the numbers but won't enter them); a separate read-only "Cash value" row (a fourth field duplicating a solver leg that already exists); storing the value in `txn.amount` (breaks ADR-043's `balance = SUM(amount)` invariant — a reinvest would spend money the account never spent). `test_investment_reinvest_cash_value.py` 8/8 (the row and its label, both solve directions, the option multiplier, the stale-commission leak, zero cash impact on save, the value seeded on re-open). No schema change | 2026-07-12 | Implemented |
| [ADR-155](ADR-155-sell-to-clear.md) | **Sell to clear — a closing sale lands the position on exactly zero** (owner: "when a security is cleared the holdings should go to zero with no lingering rounding errors"). The diagnosis is sharper than the description and it is *not* rounding drift: `compute_holdings_view` drains FIFO lots with `while remaining > _EPS and queue:`, so a sell bigger than the holding **stops at zero and silently discards the excess** — no exception, a `logger.info` at most. Realised gain is then overstated (unbacked shares sold with no cost matched), and — worse — the *data* went negative where the *engine* went to zero, so the compensating **`ShrsIn` plug** a broker/importer emits to force its own running total back to zero doesn't cancel anything: it **materialises shares out of nothing**. The owner's "fractionals" are that artifact, not slivers he still owns. 12 oversells in the live file (39,854 txns); four still showing as holdings — SUSA 7.000 sh (£1,090), DSI 1.569 (£224), VWID 0.403 (£15.51: the broker sold "everything" and wrote **1167** against **1166.597** held), PDBC 0.002 (£0.03, with *two* `ShrsIn 0.001` plugs a year apart). Fix: a Sell-only **"Sell to clear"** checkbox — stored `txn.action` stays `Sell` (a distinct `SellAll` kind was rejected: it would need teaching to the engine, the QIF parser/writer, `qif_actions` and every action-switching report, for what is a data-entry aid). Ticking it fills the quantity from a new `holdings.shares_held()` and locks it; the **Proceeds** row (the ADR-093/154 tri-field total, relabelled) is what you type and the price is backed out — the right way round, since a statement states the *cash* and the share count is whatever the account held. With the quantity pinned it stops being a solve target (a price edit re-solves *proceeds*, or the solver would overwrite the holding we exist to clear), and on save it's re-read from the engine as `Decimal(repr(held))` rather than parsed back from the trimmed display field — selling a *rounded* quantity is the bug. `shares_held` is date-scoped (a late-entered closure sells what you held *then*) and excludes the row being edited (or re-opening a saved close-out halves the quantity on every save). After the close the security is offered for retirement — **asked, not assumed** (the same security can sit in several accounts) and only when *no* account holds it: that writes **`security.archived_at`**, a column in the schema since ADR-043 that **every read path already filters on** and **nothing had ever written**, so the gate was fully built and never wired — the security drops off the Securities screen and stops spending an ADR-049 Tiingo request. Reversible via *Show retired* + **"Track again"**, so retiring can't become a one-way trap. Repair: `tools/repair_share_oversells.py` (operator tool, dry-run by default, snapshots first, **refuses to commit unless every repaired position replays to exactly zero**) trims a *rounding* oversell (≤0.5 sh) to the shares actually held and deletes **every** compensating plug (not the first — PDBC's duplicate would leave it off zero), never touching the cash amount, which is what makes realised gain correct. A *large* oversell means missing history, so it's reported and skipped unless named with `--add-shares`, which inserts the shortfall *before* the sale and leaves the sale as the broker recorded it. Applied: PDBC/VWID/DSI phantoms gone, portfolio −£239.75 = exactly the phantom value. **SUSA is left alone and stays unresolved** — 56 sold against 49 held is a missing ~7-share purchase, and the owner confirmed it appears on **no statement**, so the gap can't be closed from source documents and no repair is simply *correct* (adding the shares leaves them basis-less and overstates the gain; trimming the sale unmatches the statement; leaving it keeps a £1,090 phantom). Left named rather than laundered — tracked as an open owner action in `docs/RELEASE_1.0_BACKLOG.md`. The engine's silent clamp still exists: this removes the ways it gets fed and repairs what it produced, it does not make overselling impossible. `test_investment_sell_to_clear.py` 12/12. No schema change | 2026-07-12 | Implemented |
| [ADR-156](ADR-156-activation-refresh-guard-and-account-value-cache.md) | **Window activation stops rebuilding Home; account values are cached** (owner: the app "feels sluggish" on Windows — reports take ~1s to open, the UI "sticks" just after closing a report or switching to a register). `RegisterWindow.changeEvent` refreshed Home on **every** `ActivationChange` — which fires whenever focus returns, including when a report closes — and that rebuild measured **472–553 ms** against the live file (35k txns), synchronously on the UI thread, almost always redrawing an *identical* dashboard. Its docstring justified this with "cheap enough to run on every activation", true of the schedules cue it was written for but not of `HomeView.refresh()`, added later under the same sentence. **77% of the cost was `compute_account_values`** (362 ms), which cached nothing and replayed every investment account's *whole* ledger through the FIFO holdings engine (~24k `pence_to_decimal` calls) on every focus change. Fix: `Repository.data_generation()` — a cheap token combining `total_changes` (own-connection writes, a plain attribute, ~90 ns), `PRAGMA data_version` (other-*process* commits) and an explicit `_ext_gen` counter — plus `HomeView.refresh_if_stale()` which compares it before rebuilding (unchanged case **~450 ms → ~0.016 ms**), and a generation-keyed memo on `compute_account_values` (~180 ms → ~0.009 ms). Background threads that write on their **own** connection (the launch + toolbar price/FX refreshes) must now declare it via `note_external_change()` — previously their prices reached the screen *by luck*, since the unconditional rebuild happened to re-read the file; this is the price of the cache and is stated as an invariant. Also fixed a **latent crash**: a Home background pass still in flight at app shutdown emitted from a destroyed `QObject` (`RuntimeError: Signal source has been deleted`) — the emit is now guarded (ownership alone was **not** the fix; A/B'd, the old code passed that test — shutdown is the real trigger). Rejected: caching report windows (treats the smaller half of the cost), moving `gather_home_data` off-thread wholesale (hides redundant work instead of deleting it), invalidating from inside every mutating repo method (10k lines, one missed path = a silently stale balance). Two **pre-existing** flaky tests in ADR-149's file were fixed on the way (a stale card snapshot; a canary asserting that UB reliably segfaults) — verified flaky against unmodified source. Full suite 239/239. No schema change | 2026-07-12 | Implemented |
| [ADR-157](ADR-157-stacked-bar-totals-above-the-bars.md) | **Stacked-bar charts print each bar's total above it** (owner: "the totals of each column should be visible"). A stacked bar's headline quantity *is* its total — comparing segments across stacks is hard, only the bottom series shares a baseline — and it was the one number the chart never showed: the rail gave a grand total and an average, hover gave one segment, but the per-bucket total could only be had by eyeballing gridlines **£20,000 apart** or adding four tooltips up by hand. The value already existed (`_paint_bars` sums each stack and tracks its top edge for ADR-128's corner rounding), so this promotes a number from transient-on-hover to always-visible. Three details carry it: labels **suppress wholesale** when the widest won't fit its slot (granularity goes down to *daily*, so a wide span can produce hundreds of bars — labelling only the ones with room would read as an arbitrary subset, and "no room" would be indistinguishable from "no data"; verified at 144 buckets); the **average pill dodges** them (the last bucket is usually a part-period, so its bar lands near the average — exactly where the pill sits; the total is data and the pill is annotation, so the pill drops below the line); and each label **knocks out its own background** first, because drawing last puts the text *over* the dashed average line but the dashes still showed through the gaps between glyph strokes and read as a strike-through (only surfaced against the owner's real data, on a bar topping out just under the average). Shared widget, so Spending Over Time gets it too. Rejected: per-segment labels (unreadable in thin segments); labelling only the tallest / above-average bars; a totals table in the rail (the value is the number being *next to* the thing it describes). Flagged a `£` hard-coded in the chart — which turned out to be ADR-159. Full suite 246/246. No schema change | 2026-07-12 | Implemented |
| [ADR-158](ADR-158-sankey-savings-is-a-share-of-income.md) | **The Cash Flow Sankey's Savings node is a share of income, not of expenditure** (owner: "do you know why the savings rate here is 98%? It looks a little high"). The report **contradicted itself on the same screen** — the rail said `Saving rate: 49.4% of income` while the diagram's Savings node said `98%`. The arithmetic gives it away: `24,216 / 48,978 = 49.4%` (the rail) vs `24,216 / 24,763 = 97.8%` (the diagram). The chart picked a node's denominator by **which column it sat in** (`side_total = total_income if col < 0 else total_expense`) — right for a *category* (an expense category should read as a share of spending) but wrong for **Savings**, which is not a category but the balancing remainder `income − expense`, appended to the *expense* side so both sides fill the spine and deliberately **not** part of `total_expense`. So it was measured against a total that *excludes it*: the figure runs to 100% as savings approach spending, and **past** it if you save more than you spend. **Deficit** — the mirror case — was already right *by accident*, since it lands on the income side. New `_denominator_for(node, col)` picks by **meaning**, not geometry: balance nodes (Savings *and* Deficit) are a share of income; categories keep their own side's total; the spine keeps the larger side. Label and tooltip already shared one denominator, so both were fixed at once. Accepted cost (owner chose it over the alternatives): the expense side now mixes denominators and its labels don't sum to 100% — Savings is not a spending category and never belonged in that sum. Rejected: making every node a share of the spine (consistent, but rewrites Household 28%→14% and loses the useful "% of my spending" reading) and folding Savings into `total_expense` (would silently redefine "expenditure" to include money that was *not* spent — worse than the bug). **Verified** on the live file: node reads 56.2%, rail reads "56.2% of income". Full suite 253/253. No schema change | 2026-07-12 | Implemented |
| [ADR-159](ADR-159-spending-income-reports-convert-to-a-display-currency.md) | **Spending / Income Over Time convert to a display currency.** ADR-157 filed the hard-coded `£` in `SpendingChart` as a *cosmetic* bug for non-UK users. It was not: pulling the thread found `spending_aggregates` / `income_aggregates` had **no currency awareness at all** — `SUM(-t.amount)` with no `a.currency` grouping — and amounts are stored in each **account's** currency, so the query **added dollars to pounds 1:1** and the chart then stamped a `£` on the result. **The number was wrong, not just the label.** Not hypothetical: the owner's live file is **25 USD accounts + 13 GBP** (34,648 USD transactions), and 2025 income read **416,906** where the true figure is **325,410 GBP** — overstated ~28%. Every *other* report already did this correctly (Sankey, Payee, Income & Expense, Net Worth all take `display_currency` and `GROUP BY ... a.currency`); these two were simply never brought along — the Sankey screenshot that started the thread only looked fine because it was filtered to a single GBP account. Both aggregates (plus the reinvested-dividend pass) now join `account`, group by currency and convert at `date_to` via a new `Repository._to_display_ccy()` — the rule the other reports already inlined, now named once. **Convert → net → clamp**, in that order: netting per-currency would drop a currency's refund (ADR-129 clamps net-negative groups) before it could offset the same category's spend in another currency; the order is load-bearing and pinned by a test. Return shape becomes `{"rows", "unconverted"}`: money with **no FX rate is dropped, not counted at face value**, and surfaced in the summary panel — a silently understated total is a *quieter* version of the same bug, and quieter is worse. The window gains the "Display in" combo the Sankey/Net Worth already have; `chart_helpers.currency_symbol()` is now the single definition of the glyph. Single-currency files are byte-identical and touch no FX. Rejected: passing the symbol through and leaving the arithmetic broken (a correctly-labelled wrong number is *more* believable than an obviously-wrong one); converting at each txn's own date (defensible, but it would disagree with every other report — change it everywhere or nowhere). 10 new tests, all 10 fail pre-fix. Full suite 263/263. No schema change | 2026-07-12 | Implemented |
| [ADR-160](ADR-160-home-stops-rebuilding-itself-on-navigation-and-background-cards.md) | **Home stops rebuilding itself on navigation and on background-card arrival.** ADR-156 guarded the *activation* path and claimed that was the whole problem. It was not: instrumenting a **real launch** against the live file (a UI-thread watchdog plus timers on the hot paths) caught Home rebuilding itself **five times in the first four seconds** — 206 + 142 + 426 + 217 + 180 ms, **1,169 ms** of synchronous work including a **797 ms UI freeze** — before the user touched anything, and none of it through the guarded path. Two causes. `RegisterWindow._show_home()` rebuilt **unconditionally** and sits on the sidebar's *selection* path, which fires more than once during startup and again on every return to Home → now `refresh_if_stale()`. And `HomeView._on_bg_ready()` ran a **full** rebuild — re-running the entire query pass — purely to fold the off-thread trend/performance cards (ADR-150) into a dashboard **it had itself just drawn**; `gather_home_data` is ~85% of a refresh (480 of 553 ms), so the re-query was waste → now `refresh(reuse_data=True)`, which redraws from the cached `HomeData`. (The self-inflicted irony: the off-thread work added in ADR-150 to *avoid* blocking the UI was paying for itself with a second synchronous rebuild on arrival.) `reuse_data` is not blind — the cached data is stamped with its freshness token and **re-gathers if the token moved**, and `set_repo` drops it outright (that `HomeData` belongs to the old file). Rejected: updating only the hero card (the bg payload feeds the hero **and** an investment card in the grid, so a surgical swap touches most of the tree anyway — no saving, real ADR-149 use-after-free risk) and debouncing `_show_home` (the rebuilds are redundant, not merely bunched). **Measured: startup 5 rebuilds / 1,169 ms → 2 rebuilds / 405 ms; freeze gone.** All three paths that rebuild Home are now guarded. 6 new tests, 4 fail pre-fix; they **count `gather_home_data` calls** rather than timing anything, so they pin behaviour and can't go flaky. Full suite 269/269. No schema change | 2026-07-12 | Implemented |
| [ADR-161](ADR-161-account-summary-and-budget-join-the-design-system.md) | **Account Summary and Budget join the design system.** The first design review done by *looking at the app* — every screen rendered out of `mfl_public.mfl` and reviewed as images. P4 closed visual polish as *scoped*, but it was scoped from a list, not from the screens, and the screens said what the list never did: **the app does not look like one app.** Home / register / reports carry the language (teal accent, cards, the ADR-102 scale, `PageHeader`); **Account Summary and Budget carry none of it** — native Fusion tab bar, six identical grey buttons, default grid, accent nowhere. Cause is chronology: both predate ADR-119 and nobody had looked at them *next to* Home since. Looking turned up four defects a code reading would not have: **(1) nothing in the app styled `QTabWidget` at all** — not one rule, so every tabbed surface fell back to the native tab bar (a *global* gap that surfaced here first); **(2)** Budget printed money as **`Pool: GBP 822.64`** — the ISO code, the last surface not using `currency_symbol()` (ADR-159); **(3)** a goal target rendered **"by Jun 49"** — `_fmt_month` drops the century, *correct* for the matrix's twelve one-year column headers and *wrong* for the one date decades out, so a 2049 mortgage payoff reads as 1949; **(4)** the Pool/Assigned/Unallocated line carried **three frozen light-theme hexes** — it is a **rich-text** label, so its colours live in an HTML string that `tokens.themed` cannot reach and the ADR-097 dark-mode sweep (which swept *stylesheets*) walked past: wrong in dark mode since dark mode shipped. Decision: **adopt what already exists, build nothing new** — every piece (`PageHeader`, `mflVariant`, the type scale, `currency_symbol`, tokens) was in the repo and simply unused here. Tabs styled **in `theme.py`** (flat underline, accent on selected — fixes every future tabbed surface at once); both windows open with `PageHeader` (Budget previously had **no title at all**); the budget's six ranked-alike verbs become picker + one filled **`+ New…`** + a **`Manage`** menu with **Delete** below a separator (it was one stray click from Duplicate); the info line is rebuilt from tokens on `notifier.changed` (resolving at render time alone would be correct on open but stale after a live toggle); new `_fmt_month_long()` for a date that stands on its own. Account Summary's title also came off an off-scale `pointSize() + 8`, and its subtitle now takes the canonical label from `account_types.by_storage()` (string-munging gave "Investment std"). Rejected: a `QTabWidget` subclass (the gap was global); recolouring the six buttons (colour is not hierarchy); `Set up…` as primary (it configures once; `New…` is what the empty state points at); a blanket `s/GBP /£/` (the ISO code was the *visible* half — the frozen hexes and the two-digit year sat in the same two files, which is exactly how ADR-159's wrong-number bug got filed as cosmetic). **Known limitation: nobody has looked at the ~47 dialogs** — audited for button order/Esc (ADR-097), never for whether they carry the design language. 8 new tests. Full suite 304/304. No schema change | 2026-07-13 | Implemented |
| [ADR-162](ADR-162-the-register-never-clips-the-money-columns.md) | **The register never clips Amount and Balance.** From the same design review as ADR-161, but a **defect, not cosmetics**. `RegisterWindow` sized columns from a fixed pixel map with `stretchLastSection` off, and the columns demanded **1,160 px (account register) / 1,210 px (all transactions) against a 967 px viewport** — 193/243 px of overflow. Amount and Balance are the **last two columns**, so all of it landed on them: a ledger whose two headline numbers sat behind a horizontal scrollbar while **Memo — empty on most rows — held a fixed 280 px** of the space they needed. All Transactions was worse (adds Account, drops Balance): 243 px of overflow put **Amount entirely off-screen**. Fix: **Memo is the column that flexes** (`QHeaderView.Stretch` — free text, empty on most rows, already elides), every other column keeps a fixed user-draggable width, and the defaults are trimmed so everything *except* Memo fits the viewport. `budget_drilldown_window` already did exactly this; the register never adopted it. **Order is load-bearing and this nearly shipped wrong:** `setColumnWidth` is *silently ignored* on a section still in Stretch mode, and Memo sits at a different index in each register mode — so switching modes left whichever column now held the old Stretch index (Quantity) pinned at Memo's inherited width and the grid overflowed again. Reset every section to Interactive → apply widths → stretch Memo, in that order (pinned by a test). Rejected: `setStretchLastSection(True)` (the last section *is* Balance — stretches the very column being protected, exactly backwards); frozen money columns (a second overlaid view + synced scroll/selection/sort — the absolute fix, but real machinery for a problem trimming solves in the two registers people live in); stretching Payee and Category too (a Stretch section can't be dragged, so the user would lose resize on the columns they most want wider). **Known limitation, stated not buried: the investment register still scrolls in a small window** — eleven columns whose non-Memo widths (~1,090 px) exceed a 967 px viewport *on their own*, so no amount of stretching helps; trimmed to fit from ~1,090 px (a maximised window) and the boundary pinned by a test. **Verification trap worth knowing:** under `QT_QPA_PLATFORM=offscreen` a top-level window **ignores `resize()`** (viewport came back 1,607 px regardless), so the first version of these tests could never observe a clipped column and **passed against the unfixed code** — a green test asserting nothing; resizing the *table widget* is honoured. 5 new tests, **all 5 fail pre-fix**. Full suite 309/309. No schema change | 2026-07-13 | Implemented |
| [ADR-163](ADR-163-home-spending-cards-fall-back-to-the-last-month-with-spending.md) | **Home's spending cards fall back to the last month with spending.** From the same design review: *Top Payees · This Month* and *Top Categories · This Month* both read "No spending yet this month" with nothing under them, above a Budget card showing `£0.00 of £2,474.00` on an empty bar — **three dead cards down one column**, which reads as a broken app rather than a quiet month. Cause: the cards window on **month-to-date**, which is legitimately empty in two ordinary situations — **on the 1st–2nd of any month** (every user, every month) and **on any file whose data stops earlier** (every file between imports). So the emptiest the dashboard can look is a state real users hit routinely. Fix: if the current month has no spending, use **the last month that does — and name it** (`TOP PAYEES · JUNE 2026`). The label is not decoration: a figure silently labelled "this month" that is really June's would be a *worse* bug than the empty card — ADR-159's lesson is that a wrong number is more believable than an obviously-missing one. New `Repository.latest_spending_month(not_after)` is **one indexed `MAX(substr(posted_date,1,7))`**, not a loop of per-month probes (Home is the hot path — ADR-156/160 exist because it wasn't); an active file answers from the first row it touches and takes the normal window unchanged, and a file with *no* spending anywhere keeps the empty card, because that is the honest answer. The query mirrors the report aggregates' definition of spending (expense-kind category, no transfers, no portfolio moves) so the month it names is one the cards will actually find rows in — a card titled "June 2026" that is still empty would be the worst outcome. Rejected: falling back silently (a lie); widening to "last 30 days" always (changes what the card *means* for every user every day, to fix a case that only arises when the month is empty); hiding the cards (lopsided, and they're the entry points to the Payee/Spending reports); **and changing the Budget card — deliberately left alone**, since "you have spent £0 of your £2,474 budget this month" is true and useful on a month that has just started, unlike an empty top-payees list. 7 new tests. Full suite 316/316. No schema change | 2026-07-13 | Implemented |
| [ADR-164](ADR-164-a-report-leads-with-what-it-is.md) | **A report leads with what it is, not with "Untitled".** From the design review: open any report and the biggest text on screen is **"Untitled"** — a statement about the *file* ("you haven't saved this yet"), not about what you are looking at — while the report's actual identity ("Spending Over Time"), the only thing distinguishing it from four other report windows, is the small grey subtitle beneath. Every report opened from the menu is unsaved, so this is the state most reports are in most of the time: the app's most prominent word is a word about nothing. Fix: **unsaved** → title is the *type*, subtitle "Unsaved report"; **saved** → title is the *name the user chose* (which genuinely does outrank the type), subtitle the type — unchanged. Five report windows had each grown their own copy of the folder-prefix / dirty-asterisk / "Untitled" / window-title logic; new `page_header.report_heading()` is the single definition and `report_folder_name()` collapses the same four-line `list_report_folders()` scan all five had inlined (the ADR-084 rule). Rejected: keeping "Untitled" but shrinking it (still spends a line on a non-fact); a badge or asterisk on the type (a bare report isn't *dirty* — it doesn't exist on disk yet, and the asterisk already means "saved, with unsaved changes"); changing the string in five places (the next report window copies whichever it finds first). 7 new tests. Full suite 331/331. No schema change | 2026-07-13 | Implemented |
| [ADR-165](ADR-165-one-currency-glyph-and-no-unlabelled-money.md) | **One currency glyph, and no unlabelled money.** The design review flagged the sidebar for showing `$17,035.62` beside `£19,041.85` "with nothing marking the unit" — **that framing was wrong**, the `$` *is* the marker. Pulling the thread found much worse. ADR-159 introduced `currency_symbol()` and its docstring declared it *"one definition, so a report can't disagree with a chart about what a dollar looks like"* — **it was not one definition**: **sixteen** UI modules carried a private copy of the table (`_CCY_SYMBOLS`, `_CURRENCY_SYMBOLS`, `_SYM`, `_SYMBOL`), and they disagreed. **Most returned an empty string for an unknown currency**, so a **CHF / CAD / AUD** balance rendered as a bare `1,234.00` — *money with no visible unit*, in a sidebar column that also holds sterling — and **four were missing JPY outright**, so a yen transfer chip read `JPY 500.00` where the same amount read `¥500.00` two screens away. Only three of sixteen had the code-prefix fallback `currency_symbol()` has had all along. The defect register carried this as a *consistency* nit ("duplicated in `home_view` and `sankey_report_window`; both are correct today") — it was in sixteen modules and most were **not** correct: **a wrong-display bug filed as tidiness, the exact mistake §1b exists to stop**. Fix: all sixteen copies deleted, every call site delegates; an unknown code returns `"CHF "`, never `""` — **money is never printed without its unit** — while a row with genuinely no currency (a mixed-currency folder total) still gets no symbol, because it must not be stamped with a `£` it hasn't earned. The empty **`REPORTS` sidebar header** is now hidden when nothing sits under it (a bare caption dangling at the bottom reads as a section that failed to load). Rejected: adding the missing currencies to all sixteen tables (sixteen places to keep in sync; the seventeenth window copies one). **Known limitation, stated so it isn't assumed away: the folder *totals* are still a naive cross-currency sum** — a different bug (the ADR-159 `SUM`-without-conversion class), still open; marking each row's unit correctly does not make the total beneath them mean anything. 8 new tests — the one that matters is a **source scan** that fails if any `ui/*.py` other than `chart_helpers` defines a currency→glyph dict, so it stops the seventeenth copy (it earned its keep immediately: it caught four tables a grep for the two known variable names had missed). Full suite 331/331. No schema change | 2026-07-13 | Implemented |
| [ADR-166](ADR-166-a-validated-categorical-chart-palette.md) | **A validated, on-brand categorical chart palette.** The review's complaint was cosmetic — the charts used saturated Tailwind primaries that read as a library default and fought the teal chrome. Running them through a CVD validator found the real defect. `GROUP_PALETTE`'s comment said *"Tested at AA contrast against white"*; **it had not been tested**: **violet-500 vs blue-600 measure ΔE 3.3 under protanopia** — for a red-blind reader (~1 in 12 men) the 1st and 5th category in every stacked bar, treemap and sunburst were **the same colour** — and **four of the twelve sat below 3:1 contrast** on white. It also **cycled** (`index % len`). A palette that is inaccessible is not a matter of taste, and the comment asserting otherwise is how it survived. Replaced with **8 slots, fixed order, no cycling, theme-aware**, resolved from tokens at *paint* time; both columns iterated against the validator until every check passed in **all-pairs** mode (the standard the sunburst/treemap need — the default adjacent-only check would have *hidden* the violet/blue collapse).
