Three findings kept: **(1) the brand accent cannot be a series colour** — `#1f6e78` has chroma 0.075, below the 0.10 floor, so as a large fill it reads *grey*; slot 1 is the same hue at usable chroma (`#0d9488`). **(2) Dark is a separately validated set, not a lightened light one** — the dark band (0.48–0.67) is *narrower and lower*, and the instinct to brighten everything put six of eight out of band. **(3) Blue and indigo are held apart by lightness, not hue** — under deuteranopia they *are* the same hue, and "brighten the indigo for dark mode" collapses them to ΔE 0.6, reinstating the very defect being fixed. The floor-band pairs are legal **only** because of secondary encoding (legend text, ADR-128 segment gaps, ADR-157 bar totals, hover) — a **dependency, not a coincidence**. **Then the render caught what the validator could not:** the demo has **nine** top-level categories, so "Charity and gifts" came out in exactly Housing's teal — a false identity match, *worse* than the old 12-colour list. Spending/Income Over Time now keep the top seven and **fold the tail into a labelled "Other"** (synthetic id −200, non-drillable like ADR-110's Reinvested Dividends; folded, never dropped — totals still reconcile). Rejected: keeping twelve (twelve hues cannot be made CVD-distinct); generating a 9th hue; the accent as slot 1; auto-deriving dark from light. **Known limitations, recorded not fixed: the treemap, sunburst, Sankey and Category & Payee can still exceed 8 series and wrap** (each needs the same fold), and **colour follows rank, not entity** — a filter that drops the largest category repaints the survivors. 13 new tests. Full suite 344/344. No schema change | 2026-07-14 | Implemented |
| [ADR-167](ADR-167-the-dialogs-audit-and-the-dark-mode-sweep-that-was-not.md) | **The dialogs audit, and the dark-mode sweep that wasn't.** ADR-161 closed by doubting that Account Summary and Budget were the only surfaces to miss ADR-119, so the ~47 dialogs were audited: **55 dialog classes**, statically scanned and **rendered to PNG in both themes** and reviewed as images. **The dialogs are fine — ADR-097's audit holds up** (button order, `QDialogButtonBox`, Esc, defaults all as described; the `£` literals a grep flags in eight dialogs are *input parsers* stripping a typed symbol, not hard-coded display — no ADR-159 repeat). **But ADR-097 also declared the *dark-mode* sweep complete, and it was not: 73 frozen light-theme hex literals across 20 modules.** The mechanism: `tokens.themed` styles a widget's **stylesheet**, so anything living in an HTML attribute, a `QColor` constant or a module-level style string was never reached — ADR-097 swept stylesheets and walked past the rest. ADR-161 found the first survivor by accident; this is the systematic version. Three were outright **breakage**: **(1)** `reconcile_wizard` — a core workflow that had never joined the token layer — drew its **only instruction line** in `_INK = "#0F172A"` on the `#0f172a` dark canvas, *the background colour*: **invisible**, since dark mode shipped, and unseeable by any test because no test looks at pixels; **(2)** `transfer_match_dialogs` / `transfer_destination_dialog` wrap the **transaction amount** — the number you are confirming — in `<span style='color:#0F172A'>`, so the themed prose around it read fine and the *number* did not; **(3)** the transactions-list **filter chips** were five frozen hexes, a pale slate pill on the dark canvas. All fixed via tokens (each replaced hex's light value equals its token's light step, so **light mode is pixel-identical**), plus `about_dialog`, `categories_dialog` (a `QColor` frozen at *import*, which can never follow a toggle) and `import_mappings_dialog`. **The durable part is a ratchet**: `tests/test_no_frozen_theme_colours.py` pins **dialogs at zero**, lists every other module with its current count, and fails if any count *grows* or a new module appears — plus a staleness check so a cleaned-up module must tighten its allowance. It scans the **AST**, not a grep, because a hex in a docstring is prose (the first scanner naively split on `#`, mistook every `"#94a3b8"` for a comment and reported **zero** — a scanner that reports what you hoped to hear is worth nothing). Rejected: converting all 73 at once (the remaining 60 are chart *series* colours — readable in dark, just untuned; a different problem needing per-chart judgement) and a blanket regex (some hexes are *correct* — white on a saturated fill is white in both themes; a blind sweep would have "fixed" them into unreadable text). **Known limitation: the 60 are fenced, not fixed** — and the net-worth window's six family colours are a categorical palette that never met the ADR-166 validator. 3 new tests, **2 of 3 fail pre-fix**. Full suite 347/347. No schema change | 2026-07-14 | Implemented |
| [ADR-168](ADR-168-the-sidebar-remembers-a-collapsed-group.md) | **The sidebar remembers a collapsed group.** Owner-reported: collapsing a group in the left panel — a folder, a section header, the Closed-accounts group — never sticks. Collapse one to make room, navigate away and back (or quit and relaunch) and it is expanded again. This is **exactly the limitation ADR-015 recorded and deferred** ("folder expansion state isn't preserved across a sidebar reload… small follow-up"). The mechanism: the sidebar is one `QTreeWidget` whose groups are `QTreeWidgetItem`s, and expand state lives **only** on those transient items; `_populate` rebuilds them hard-coded to `setExpanded(True)`, and `reload` runs after almost anything (txn add/delete, import, report create, account navigation), throwing the choice away each time — and even a `reload`-round-trip like the one `selection` already gets would not survive a *restart*. Fix, three decisions carrying the weight: **(1)** state lives in the file's **`setting` table (ADR-092), not app-level `QSettings`** — the tempting move (mirror the ADR-131 balance-mode toggle) is the trap, because a group's key is its folder's DB id and **folder id 3 in one `.mfl` is a different folder in another**, so an app-level key would bleed one file's collapsed groups onto every other file; **(2)** the value is a `{group_key: expanded}` map of **only the groups the user has actually toggled**, not a collapsed-id set — that is what lets the **per-kind defaults survive**, since Closed-accounts defaults *collapsed* (ADR-069) and a bare collapsed-set cannot encode "deliberately expanded against the default"; **(3)** the write is driven by **`itemExpanded`/`itemCollapsed`, not the click handler** — `_on_item_clicked` only sees a click on the row *body*, but a user collapses via the row, the **disclosure triangle**, or the **keyboard**, and only the tree's own signals see all three (connected *after* the first `_populate`, and `reload` already `blockSignals`, so only a genuine user toggle persists; the write is best-effort so a failed setting never breaks navigation). A file switch reuses the same `Sidebar`, so it gained a **`set_repo`** (called from `_adopt_repository` before the reload, mirroring the Home view's) — which also fixes a **latent pre-existing bug**: the sidebar held a repo reference for its mixed-currency folder roll-ups that was **never refreshed on a file switch**, so after opening a second file its currency conversion read the *first* file's settings; one method closes both. Rejected: app-level `QSettings` (cross-file bleed); a collapsed-id set (flips the Closed-accounts default); round-tripping across `reload` only (survives a reload, not a relaunch — but "even close and reopen the app" was the report); hooking `_on_item_clicked` only (misses the triangle/keyboard — persisting for *some* gestures is worse than none); pruning orphaned keys for deleted folders on every write (inert drift, not worth walking the tree per toggle). **Closes the ADR-015 backlog item and goes past it** — the choice now survives a relaunch and is scoped per file. 6 new tests (survives reload; survives restart; reopening clears the memory; isolated between two files; a `set_repo` switch adopts the new file's state and routes writes correctly; repo-less sidebar no-ops). No schema change — the `setting` table already exists | 2026-07-16 | Implemented |
| [ADR-169](ADR-169-the-income-expense-drill-honours-the-reports-category-scope.md) | **The Income & Expense drill honours the report's category scope.** Owner-reported: on the Income & Expense report, clicking a bar drills into transactions **outside the report's scope** — a "Bedford House ROI" report narrowed to Landlord Expenses has correct bars but its drill shows pet food, groceries, everything. The report supports a category scope (ADR-088 amend): `IncomeExpenseFilters.category_ids`, expanded to descendants and applied as `t.category_id IN (...)` in `income_expense_series` — so the **chart is right**. The leak is in the drill: `_on_segment_clicked` built a `TxnListFilter.for_kind(...)` carrying period, cash-flow kind and **account** scope but **not the category scope**, and the drill window then resolved its category set from `list_categories_flat(kinds=(kind,))` — *every* category of that kind — so a one-category report drilled into all of them. **This is the ADR-147 bug one field over**: the aggregate applied the filter, the drill didn't (there it was the account subset; here the category scope). And fixing it surfaced a **second bug behind it**, hit immediately on the owner's real report: clicking a *non-zero* income bar drilled to an **empty** list, because the report aggregates the split-aware `txn_category_line` view — that year's £14,340 income was entirely **split lines** on parents categorised Uncategorised — while the kind drill matched only a row's own `category_id` and never its split lines (masked before, by the flood of out-of-scope rows). Fix, mirroring how ADR-147 threaded the account subset: **(1)** a new `TxnListFilter.kind_category_ids` field, filled by `_on_segment_clicked` from **the same** `_expanded_category_ids(...)` the chart query uses, so drill and bar agree on which categories (empty == spans all, the historical behaviour, so an unscoped report is unchanged); **(2)** `_apply_filter` **intersects** rather than replaces — `kind_ids &= scope` — because a report scope can hold categories of *both* kinds (it narrows income and expense together) and intersecting with the clicked kind's set drops the other kind's cleanly, so no income category leaks into an expense drill (this is exactly how `income_expense_series` composes its kind clause and its `category_id IN` clause); **(3)** `DrillDownFilterProxy.set_kind_filter` now distinguishes `None` (no restriction) from an **empty set** (reject every row) via `is not None` — once we intersect, an empty result is reachable in principle, and the old `frozenset(ids) if ids else None` contract would have silently reopened the whole kind, the very leak being closed (unreachable through the UI today, but a proxy method that inverts its argument in an edge case is a landmine for the next caller); **(4)** the kind match is now **split-aware**, mirroring the category-descendant drill (ADR-051) one branch up — a row clears the category gate when its own `category_id` *or any split-line category* (`row.split_category_ids`) is in the scoped set, which is what makes the split-line income drillable, and as a consequence the **sign gate** (`amount >0`/`<0`) applies only to whole-transaction rows (`split_count == 0`), since a split parent's *total* sign doesn't reflect the matched line (the report counts the line, not the parent). The scope joins `signature()`, so two drills differing only by category scope open as distinct windows. Rejected: replacing the kind set with the scope (a mixed-kind scope would then pass an income category into an expense drill on sign alone); re-querying the drill in SQL (it is a live editable proxy over the register model, not a re-query — every other drill facet filters in `filterAcceptsRow` too); leaving the falsy-means-all proxy contract alone (unreachable today, landmine tomorrow). The two sibling drills (kind, category-descendant) **no longer disagree about splits**. 8 new tests (scope excludes out-of-scope categories; `None` shows all of the kind; empty intersection matches nothing; income on a split line is surfaced — the Bedford-House shape — and a split's expense line under an expense scope, while an all-out-of-scope split is excluded; end-to-end `for_kind` with a scope shows only the scoped category, and without one shows all). No schema change | 2026-07-16 | Implemented |
| [ADR-170](ADR-170-the-budget-draws-the-category-tree-it-always-had.md) | **The budget draws the category tree it always had.** Owner-reported from two screenshots: the annual matrix drew every budgeted line as a **flat peer** disambiguated only by a parenthetical (`Bills`, then `Cable and Internet (Bills)`, `Council Tax (Bills)`) — a tree rendered as a list, with the parent alongside its own children as though it were their sibling — and asked for indentation, collapsing, and "the top node should include the sum of the group/leaf nodes". The screenshot showed the cost: `Bills` planned **£982/month** with an Actual of **0.00 in every month**, each child at **0.00 budget** against real spending — every child red, the parent green. Nothing was arithmetically wrong: **ADR-024 bucketing** sends each txn to its *nearest budgeted ancestor*, so the moment a `Cable and Internet` line existed it claimed Cable's txns and `Bills` stopped receiving them — keeping the plan those txns justified while losing the spending, and (being a rollover line, ADR-058 D3) **compounding** the unspent £982 into a phantom **£7,553 "available"** by December. The user asked for a breakdown and was silently charged the parent's actuals for it. **The decisive observation: the 'everything else' line the owner was reaching for already exists** — bucketing guarantees a parent row holds *exactly* what no budgeted child claimed (the same reason section subtotals were always correct: parent + descendants double-counts nothing). The model was right; the presentation was lying about it. **So this is a rendering change, not a calculation change.** A budgeted category with budgeted descendants now renders as a **group**: **(1)** a **roll-up header** (own residual + every descendant), **not editable** — a sum with no stored allocation to write to — which buys the property that makes collapsing worth having: **a collapsed group still tells the whole truth about itself**; **(2)** **'Everything else'** — the parent's real line renamed, same `line_id`, still editable — emitted **only** when its allocation or actual is non-zero, so itemise to the penny and it vanishes, leave a gap and it reappears (the whole answer to "I want to avoid it getting too cluttered"); **(3)** a line with **no budgeted descendants is untouched** — the group machinery costs nothing until you ask for detail, and there is no migration: budget `Bills` alone and it stays simple; itemise a child and its £982 becomes `Everything else: £982`, right at every intermediate stage; **(4)** **indentation replaces the parenthetical — but only where it can**, since a line whose parent is *unbudgeted* lands at depth 0 where the suffix is all that separates `Insurance (Car)` from `Insurance (Home)` (`mfl_public.mfl` is exactly this: 21 lines, every parent unbudgeted, renders identically); **(5)** collapse state is **shared by both views and persisted per budget, per file** in the `setting` table (ADR-092) — **inverting ADR-168's collapsed-set rejection, and the inversion is the point**: that ADR needed a `{key: expanded}` map because Closed-accounts defaults *collapsed*; here everything defaults expanded, so there is no default for a bool to protect. Falling out of the tree: subtotals now count **top-level** rows (one group + four children is five rows but one top-level row, and the header already restates the subtotal — ADR-058's single-row rule just needed depth); a group's **drill covers its subtree** (new `is_ancestor_or_self`, new `group` mode) or the list would contradict the number clicked; the **burn-down scope test became a subtree test**, since matching `bucket == target` would chart only the residual's spend against the *whole group's* available — a line that could never reach the floor — and the new test is **exactly equivalent for a leaf** (nothing can bucket below one), so only groups see any change; the **↻ moved off headers** onto the rows that own a policy. **Plus a correction worth recording**: the rider "editing repaints and the user loses their position" was implemented as a scroll restore *before it was checked* — and driving the real window offscreen showed `QTableView` **holds its scrollbar across a reset**, shrinking or not. That fix defended a bug that did not exist and "passed" a test measuring its own side effects. What a reset *does* destroy is the **current index** (→ `-1`), on every edit and every activate — dropping the highlight from the cell just typed into and killing any arrow/tab onward. `_restore_current_cell` fixes the real thing (restoring the index also scrolls its cell back into view, which is what reads as "kept my place"), re-applied via `singleShot(0)` to outlive the queued layout pass and clamped against a table that may have shortened. Rejected: a `QTreeView` (a rewrite — the matrix is a *table* of month columns whose rows are Budget/Actual/Diff triples; a tree would express that as three children per node, destroying the drill and edit paths, for indentation a `depth` field gives free); an **editable header spreading a typed total down** (pro-rata? evenly? into the residual? every answer silently rewrites untouched lines — and the honest place to type a group number exists and is called 'Everything else'); always showing 'Everything else' (the exact clutter the owner asked to avoid); putting it **first** (it is the *remainder* — a remainder goes last; this ADR's own first sketch had it first); **auto-migrating** the £982 (destroying data to fix a rendering bug); **suppressing the parent's rollover** when it becomes a group (would prevent the phantom £7,553 by silently changing a policy the user set — the compounding is now merely *visible*, which is the fix); and the scroll restore (kept out, not left in as harmless insurance — code defending a non-existent bug is a claim the next reader will believe). 13 new tests: 7 Qt-free (a lone parent stays a leaf; header+children+residual order with the roll-up and the residual's own bucket exact; the residual vanishes when itemised; **subtotals don't double-count headers**; the depth-0 orphan keeps its suffix; grandchildren roll up transitively; containment) — the transitive test **caught a double-count in the first implementation**, where a 3-level chain summed the *arranged* subtree containing both a header and the children it had already rolled up — and 6 driving the real window (roll-up not editable while its parts are; collapse hides exactly the subtree and keeps the total; survives a reopen, isolated per budget; a corrupt setting degrades to expanded; the current cell survives a refresh, **failing without the fix**; a shrinking refresh doesn't restore off the end). Full suite 373 passed, 1 pre-existing unrelated failure (the same one ADR-168 recorded). No schema change — a new key in the existing `setting` table | 2026-07-17 | Implemented |
| [ADR-171](ADR-171-the-monthly-budget-row-says-what-it-means.md) | **The monthly budget row says what it means.** The other half of the ADR-170 report — *"I still think it looks pretty messy. It's one of the worst report views in the app, we can do better."* ADR-170 fixed the tree the view draws; this is the row: `Bills ↻ [bar] 0.00 / 7,553.13 (+6,571.13) +7,553.13` — **four numbers, no two independent**. `0.00 / 7,553.13` is spent-of-available, `(+6,571.13)` is the carry, `+7,553.13` is the diff — which is just available − spent, i.e. the two numbers to its left restated; the carry and the diff are largely **the same fact told twice, in two notations, neither labelled**. And the signed diff **means different things in different rows**: positive is favourable (ADR-058), so `+7,553.13` is money *left* on an expense and *over-target* on income — the reader must know the row's kind before reading its last column, and for income the ordinary state of being part-way through a month rendered as an **alarming red deficit**. The case that gives it away: rollover carries overspends *backwards* (D3, deliberately unclamped), so `available` goes negative and the row becomes `32.99 / -158.63 (-158.63) → -191.62` — **not a sentence**: there is no budget of −£158.63 for £32.99 to be "of", the bar is full red because the fraction is undefined, and the reader subtracts two negatives to learn they are £191.62 over. Fix — **two numbers and a sentence**: **(1)** `£32.99 of £33.00`, with the **carry moved to the tooltip** (*"Budgeted £10.00 + £6,571.13 rolled over = £6,581.13 available this month"*) — it is not a third headline number, it is an *explanation* of the second, and this is exactly ADR-124's move when the same annotation overflowed the annual grid's column, which this view kept inline and paid for in a different currency; **(2)** the remainder is **worded, not signed** — `£3,218.25 left` / `£15.76 over`, and for income `£500.00 to go` / `£668.90 above plan` — killing the sign-decoding *and* the kind-dependence at once, and letting income under plan be **muted rather than red** because a month that isn't over isn't a failure; **(3)** a **non-positive available gets different words** (`£20.00 spent` + `£50.00 over`, no "of") — gated on `available > 0`, since a zero budget with spending against it is the same sentence as a negative one; **(4)** **one Pool line per screen** — found only by rendering to PNG: *both* the window and the view draw Pool/Assigned/Unallocated, the window's pinned to **today's** month and the view's following its **selector**, so on Monthly two lines a centimetre apart showed the same three labels **disagreeing**; the view's wins on its own page (it sits beside the selector it tracks); **(5)** **`setParent(None)` before `deleteLater`** — also found in a PNG: taking a widget out of a layout does **not** unparent it, so old rows stayed children of the list and kept painting at their old geometry until the deferred delete landed, and the bottom of the list rendered as **overlapping text** (same fix in `_clear_goals_bar`, which had the identical pattern); **(6)** money gets its **glyph** and the inks come from **tokens**. Two stragglers fell out: **`Pool: GBP 5,000.00`** — ADR-159 declared `currency_symbol()` the single definition and ADR-165 deleted sixteen private tables to make it true, and **this view survived both because it has no table to find**: it just printed `f"{ccy} {amount}"`, the same defect with nothing to grep for; and **three frozen light-theme hexes** (`_MUTED`/`_GREEN_TXT`/`_RED_TXT`), the last on ADR-167's ratchet for this module, which made the remainder text light-theme green on the dark canvas — **ratchet 3 → 0**, and ADR-167's *staleness* check demanded it unprompted (it fails any module whose allowance is looser than its count). Columns 190/160/78 → 248/190/126 (the old split predates both the tree indent and the currency glyph, and clipped both) and names now **elide with the full text in a tooltip**, since a QLabel clips by default and `Digital Subscriptions` vanished mid-word with nothing to say it had. Rejected: keeping a signed diff and only fixing its colour (leaves the kind-dependent sign to decode — the words are shorter to read than the rule for reading the number); a **percentage** (what the bar already says, less precisely, and meaningless for a negative available); **clamping `available` at zero** (fixes a display problem by lying — the deficit is real and D3 carries it on purpose; the row would cheerfully report a £0.00 budget while £158 of overspend went unaccounted); dropping the bar (the one part that worked — it reads at a glance and is the drill target); keeping the **window's** Pool line instead (backwards — it is pinned to today, on a page whose purpose is stepping between months); `del w`/`sip.delete` (immediate destruction mid-signal is how ADR-058's macOS teardown bugs happened — `setParent(None)` solves the painting, `deleteLater` keeps the freeing safe). 8 new tests driving the real window: two numbers + worded remainder; an overspend says "over"; a carried-in deficit says what was spent; the carry is out of the row and in the tooltip; income under plan is muted, never red; money carries its glyph (unknown-currency fallback, sign outside) and the pool line has no ISO code; a rebuild leaves **no ghost rows**; one Pool line per screen. The last two were **written against bugs found in a PNG** and both confirmed failing with their fixes neutered (the ghost guard reporting **11 orphaned rows**) — string assertions pass on both, which is ADR-167's point about invisible ink, still true. Full suite 381 passed, 1 pre-existing unrelated failure. No schema change | 2026-07-17 | Implemented |
| [ADR-172](ADR-172-the-burn-down-burns-down-against-the-plan.md) | **The burn-down burns down, against the plan.** Owner-reported: *"I've never been fully satisfied with this chart"* — an aesthetic complaint on its face, and not one. Reproducing the screenshot's budget and **measuring** what it plots: the month's plan was **£3,673.27**, the dashed "Budget" line was **£19,892.89** (5.4×), "Ideal" claimed you should have spent **£10,909 by the 17th**, and the actual data occupied **7% of the y-axis**. `total_planned` was the scope's **`available`** — allocation *plus accumulated rollover* — so six months of underspending had piled into it and the chart paced the reader against £19,892 in a month they had assigned £3,673 to, telling them they were nine thousand pounds *behind on spending*. Not a plan anyone failed to meet: an artifact of the carry. And because the budget line sets the y-axis, the real spending was crushed into the bottom 7% with 93% empty above it. **The chart was not badly drawn — it was correctly drawing a comparison that had no meaning.** Three more defects sat on top: **it was a burn-down that went up** (every series climbed; the docstring said "depletion chart" and nothing depleted — name, docstring and picture all disagreed); **`projected_end` was computed and read by nothing** (grepped: defined, returned, used by no view and no test — the chart worked out the exact answer to "will I come in under?" then made the reader eyeball where a dashed line stopped); and **red meant nothing** (the actual line was a hard-coded `#dc2626` *always*, so a reader comfortably under budget got a chart shouting alarm-red — five frozen hexes, the module's whole ADR-167 allowance). Fix, with the two genuinely-owner decisions put to the owner (who **overruled the recommendation on the second, correctly**): **(1)** the pacing target is the month's **`allocation`, never `available`** — a rollover surplus is a **buffer, not a target**, and pacing against the plan takes the series from 13% to **72%** of the canvas; symmetrically a carried-in *deficit* doesn't lower it either (the plan is the plan; the debt is on the row). This works *because of* ADR-171: the row now states the ceiling (`£1,460.00 of £19,892.89`), so **the row says what you have and the chart says whether you're pacing it** — the buffer still gets a word in the caption (`+£16,219.62 rolled over if needed`), the difference between "over budget" and "over budget with nothing behind it". **(2)** **It descends** — start at the plan, fall as you spend, and **the day it hits zero is the day you run out** (`Runs out · 16`): the prize a rising line cannot give, since "you'll spend £4,100 of £3,673" is a subtraction and "you run out on the 16th" is a date; the axis extends *below* zero on an overshoot because that is the one thing the chart exists to warn about. **(3)** **The wedge is the reading** — lifted from a reference chart the owner shared: shade between Remaining and Plan, green where more is left than planned, red where less, so the colour *is* the comparison and **the legend is gone** (22px back, one less decode step; the series are direct-labelled at their ends). **(4)** **Colour means over** — Remaining is plain ink (a fact, not a judgement), the projection carries the verdict, and red appears iff something is wrong. **(5)** **The verdict is stated in words** (`On track · £1,010.92 left on 31 Jul`), ADR-164's principle applied to a chart, and what finally spends `projected_end`. `compute_burndown` keeps producing **cumulative spend** (what the bills staircase and run-rate naturally build) — *remaining* is a pure function of it, derived in the paint: model and view, not two models; what moved *into* the model is the arithmetic a test should reach without a Qt loop (`runs_out_day`, `projected_remaining`). Rejected: the reference's **endpoint pills** (right for a chart with no headline — we have a scope-row headline for free, and two places saying "£1,011" is the redundancy ADR-171 just removed from the rows); **keeping the burn-up and only rescaling** (my recommendation, overruled — rescaling fixes the squash but not the name, and forfeits the run-out date); **clamping the axis at zero** (hides the overspend); **pacing against `available` but rescaling** (coherent if rollover *is* this month's money — it isn't the owner's model, and it tells someone who is fine that they're £9,000 behind); **suppressing the buffer** now it doesn't pace (real money, hence the caption); reading the buffer from **`cell.carry_in`** (the obvious field, wrong: a section subtotal sums its rows' `available` but hard-codes its own `carry_in` to zero, so it finds nothing on the whole-budget scope — where the buffer is largest; `available − allocation` is the definition anyway); a literal **`#ffffff`** for the Today pill (white in both themes so ADR-167 would excuse it — but a hex is indistinguishable from the frozen ones the ratchet hunts, and `on_accent` exists and is white in both: zero pixels change, the token says the choice was deliberate). **Rollover budgets change most; non-rollover budgets not at all** (`available == allocation`, so only the inversion and verdict show). Known seam: the chart will say "on track" while the row says you're £30 in the hole from last month — the division of labour working as designed, but if it bites the answer is a second caption, not a second pacing rule. 12 new tests, calc half Qt-free (under never runs out; a crossing **names the day**; an already-blown plan reports the day it *happened*, from the actuals not the forecast; spending *exactly* the plan counts as running out — `>=`, remaining hits zero and there is nothing left; a **zero plan is not a false alarm**; `projected_remaining` reconciles) and view half driving the real window (**paces against the plan not the buffer**, built on the exact shape that caused the bug; ignores a carried-in deficit; a missing cell is a zero not a crash; the verdict states the answer with a glyph, reddens only when over, and names the buffer without pacing on it). Verified by **rendering four scenarios in both themes** — which is how the `Runs out · 16` label was caught being overprinted by the `Remaining` end-label plate (fixed by drawing the marker last and standing `Remaining` down when a run-out is on screen — it is the more important of the two). String assertions passed the whole time; same lesson as ADR-171. **Ratchet 5 → 0**, demanded unprompted by ADR-167's staleness check for the second time in two ADRs. Full suite 393 passed, 1 pre-existing unrelated failure. No schema change | 2026-07-17 | Implemented |
| [ADR-173](ADR-173-every-scheduled-bill-in-the-perimeter-is-projected.md) | **Every scheduled bill in the perimeter is projected.** Owner-reported the moment ADR-172 made the chart readable enough to notice what was missing: *"it does not seem to take into account scheduled bills in the 'projected' — any scheduled transaction should be shown in the projected around the date it's due to post."* ADR-094 had built exactly that (occurrences expanded from cadence, stepping the projection at each due day, amount-matched so a paid bill drops out) and the machinery was **all there and correct**. The **source** was wrong: `list_bill_schedules_for_budget` joined `budget_line.scheduled_txn_id` — the link created by ADR-094's right-click **"Make this a bill…"** — so a schedule was projected only if someone had separately gone to a budget line and linked it, and one created the ordinary way (Manage ▸ Schedules) was invisible **forever**. `mfl_dev.mfl` is the proof and it is stark: **5 active schedules, 0 linked, 0 projected** — four of them real monthly subscriptions (Apple £36.95, Amazon £9.99, STV £3.99, Disney+ £10.99) on perimeter accounts under a budgeted `Bills`, every one a known, dated, future outflow the chart ignored. **Why it survived ADR-094 *and* ADR-172: `mfl_public.mfl` — the file the feature was demoed and eyeballed against — has 2 schedules and *both are linked*, because its demo builder links them. The sample data hid the bug; the one real file had 5 and none.** Fix: **membership is the perimeter, not the link** — a schedule spends from this budget exactly when its **account is in the perimeter**, the same rule `list_perimeter_txns` applies to the actuals that schedule will become; `list_perimeter_schedules` joins `budget_account` instead of `budget_line`. The link keeps its ADR-094 job (it is what makes an envelope a *bill* in the row UI) but has no business gating the projection — whether a future outflow is *known* does not depend on whether anyone filed it under an envelope. **Strictly better, not just broader**: a linked line whose schedule pays from an account *outside* the perimeter used to be projected, and its spending never lands in the perimeter's actuals — the projection was inventing an outflow that budget would never see (`mfl_dev` has one, a £450/mo schedule on a car account). Three rules fall out: **(1)** occurrences now **bucket like actuals** (nearest budgeted ancestor, ADR-024) — which ADR-094 never needed because it read `bl.category_id`, budgeted *by construction*, making bucketing a no-op; a schedule read from the perimeter carries its **own** category (`Cable and Internet` under a budgeted `Bills`), and without bucketing the paid txn lands on Bills, the occurrence sits on Cable, the amount-match never sees them as the same thing, and **the bill is counted twice** — once actual, once unpaid projection (`BillOccurrence.category_id` becomes `Optional[int]`: `None`, no budgeted ancestor at all, is a real bucket the whole-budget scope must still project); **(2)** **expense-kind only** — the chart plots outflows and nothing else, so an income schedule would step a line its own actual never touches; **(3)** the scope filter becomes a **subtree test** (`is_ancestor_or_self`) — **an ADR-170 straggler**: that ADR made a group's burn-down plot against its whole roll-up and converted the *transaction* filter, but left the *bill* filter an exact `==`, so a group scope showed its children's spending against its children's bills **minus the bills**. Same class of bug, one line over, found only by looking at the same function twice. Rejected: keeping the link as the source and telling the user to link their schedules (defensible as opt-in, wrong as a default — the projection's job is to say what *will* be spent, and opt-in makes the chart quietly wrong rather than visibly empty); **unioning** linked + perimeter (double-counts every linked schedule; the perimeter set already subsumes it for everything this budget can see); including **transfers** (`list_schedules_not_in_budget` uses expense+transfer for the *picker*, but intra-perimeter transfers cancel per ADR-024 and the burn-down counts expense only); restricting to **budgeted** categories (tidier — no `None` bucket — and it would silently drop real spending from a whole-budget projection that counts *all* expense outflows); keeping `list_bill_schedules_for_budget` as dead code (nothing calls it; a method encoding the rule this ADR just declared wrong is a trap — deleted, and the test asserts the unlinked condition directly). Consequences: a budget's projection **can now change without anyone touching the budget** (adding a schedule moves the chart — the point, but a real behaviour change); the `None` bucket lumps all unbudgeted expense actuals for matching, so a large unrelated purchase can "pay off" an unbudgeted bill — the same approximation ADR-094 already makes per-bucket, just coarser, noted not fixed; schedules have **no archive path** yet (`archived_at` is read, never written) so the clause is tested by stamping the column directly, correct in advance of the UI. 9 new tests (unlinked is projected; **steps on its due day**, not smeared; outside-the-perimeter is not; income + archived stay out; **buckets like its actuals** so a paid bill isn't double-counted; an unpaid bill projects exactly once; a **group scope sees its children's bills**; an unbudgeted schedule still counts) — both headline guards confirmed failing against the old code. Rendering the real budget also caught a collision ADR-172 left: on a scope that has spent nothing, `Remaining` is pinned to the chart's top — exactly where the `Today` pill sits — and printed straight through it; the pill's rect is now shared between painters and a colliding label ducks below its line. **Third time in three ADRs that rendering found what the assertions could not.** Full suite 402 passed, 1 pre-existing unrelated failure. No schema change — a new query over existing tables | 2026-07-17 | Implemented |
| [ADR-174](ADR-174-the-dock-icon-is-just-the-hexagon.md) | **The dock icon is just the hexagon.** Owner-reported: *"Mac specific: can we make the logo that appears in the dock not have the white background? It should just be a hexagon."* Baked in, not a transparency accident — every pixel of every `mfl_icon_*.png` was **alpha 255** with an opaque `#E9EDEF` wash to the corners. The odd part: **the fix already existed**. ADR-117 built the knockout tool (a flood-fill from the image edges, so internal light details — the gold coin, the light-teal facets — are never touched) and then **deliberately pointed it away from this set**: *"the dock/taskbar `mfl_icon_*` set is deliberately left untouched — that's the packaged app icon, a separate concern from the in-UI mark."* That call was **right about the reason and wrong about the art**: ADR-117's motivation was a light box on the dark-theme *sidebar*, a surface we draw — but macOS draws the dock icon on the **user's desktop**, which we don't control and can't assume is light. The same wash ADR-117 removed from the sidebar was showing on every dark wallpaper — the identical defect, one surface over, exempted by a boundary that turned out not to exist. **Two** artefacts feed the dock and both were boxed: the packaged `.app` → `mfl.icns` (via `packaging/mfl.spec`), and running from source → `resources.app_icon()`, a multi-resolution QIcon over the PNG set handed to `setWindowIcon`. Fix: knock out the whole set and rebuild `mfl.icns` from it; the flood-fill itself is ADR-117's, unchanged. Four things worth recording, **three of them from measuring rather than reasoning**: **(1)** knock out each size **independently**, do *not* downscale a transparent master — reads backwards, and is wrong because **Pillow's `resize` doesn't premultiply alpha**, so the background colour still sitting in the RGB of alpha-0 pixels bleeds back into the edges (measured: downscaling left light fringe at 32px where a direct knockout left **none**; the existing sizes are plain LANCZOS downscales with no hand-tuning to preserve, checked); **(2)** the geometry **already matches Apple's guidance** so nothing is re-inset — the art occupies **78.3%** of the canvas (`bbox=(111,52,913,975)` of 1024) against the HIG's ~80%, so a full-bleed hexagon would have loomed over its dock neighbours but this one doesn't, and measuring first saved a change that would have shrunk the icon for nothing; **(3)** **the light rim is design and it stays** — knocking out the wash exposes a flat `rgb(209,214,217)` band ~9px wide at 1024, which is *not* fringe: it is a **different colour** from the wash (which is why the flood-fill stopped at it), **flat rather than a gradient** (so not a glow), and visible in the original if you look — a die-cut sticker rim, invisible only because it sat on a near-identical near-white background; at ~9/1024 it is **about one pixel at dock size** and helps the badge hold its edge on a dark wallpaper; **(4)** **`iconutil`, not a hand-rolled writer** — it is the format's own compiler and on every Mac, and the packaged bundle's icon is not the place to discover a hand-written container got a header field wrong (skipped with a warning off macOS so the Windows build can still run the tool). The tool is **idempotent**, verified byte-identical on a second run (`knockout` flood-fills over the RGB channels, which survive an alpha-zeroing pass unchanged) — which matters because it overwrites committed assets in place. Rejected: **retiring `mfl_mark.png`/`brand_mark`** now that the set is transparent (they are the same art — the mark is literally generated from `mfl_icon_512.png` — and ADR-084 says consolidate duplicates, but it is kept as a **seam, not a workaround**: the packaged icon answers to Apple's and Microsoft's conventions and may one day grow a platform-shaped backing, while the in-UI mark answers only to our own chrome, and collapsing them would let a future dock-icon decision silently redraw the sidebar — the docstring now says *that* instead of a reason that has expired); a **macOS squircle** (what Apple's post-Big-Sur guidance actually asks for, and the opposite of what was asked — noted so the next reader knows it is a choice, not an oversight); **re-insetting** (unnecessary, see 2); **rebuilding `mfl.ico`** in the same pass (a real loose end, deliberately left — see below); **removing the light rim** for a "cleaner" cutout (the designer's line, not an artifact — deleting brand art because a background change made it visible would be a strange way to honour "just a hexagon"). Consequences: the dock icon is the hexagon on **both** paths and any wallpaper (verified compositing over grey/near-black/near-white/mid-blue); **Windows runtime changed too and its packaged icon did not** — `app_icon()` is cross-platform so the Windows *taskbar* icon is now transparent while **`mfl.ico`** (used by `mfl.spec` + `installer.iss` for the **.exe and installer**) still carries the wash: a new inconsistency created by this change, **flagged rather than fixed**, because the request was Mac-scoped and quietly rebuilding Windows packaging artefacts from a Mac is not a decision to make on someone's behalf; `app_pixmap()` now has **no callers** (every in-UI surface goes through `brand_mark`) and survives as its fallback — noticed, not removed. 7 new tests using **Qt rather than Pillow** (Pillow is a *tool* dependency, not in the app's venv — a test importing it would silently not run; Qt reads png/icns/ico natively): transparent corners; **no PNG is fully opaque** (the sharpest form — `hasAlphaChannel()` was already True *before* the fix, so the channel's existence proves nothing, only its values do); **the hexagon survived** (a flood-fill that ate the artwork would pass a corner test, so the centre must still be teal and 45–75% of the canvas opaque); no opaque wash in the edge bands; `app_icon()` transparent at all seven sizes; the in-UI mark and `app_pixmap` agree; and all **10 `.icns` slots** round-trip through `iconutil` transparent. All five applicable guards **confirmed failing against the pre-fix art**, restored from git into a scratch tree with `resources._root` repointed at it. Full suite 410 passed, 0 failed. No schema change | 2026-07-17 | Implemented |

Enforcement = **offline signed key** validated on-device against a shipped public key (no activation server; encodes buyer + version entitlement); Qt-free verify-only `licensing.py` + Enter-License/Buy flow + About state; time-limited full-feature trial. Store IAP (1.1+) grants the same entitlement, accepts the store cut. | [ADR-078](ADR-078-packaging-and-distribution.md) | Packaging & distribution — **direct signed + notarised downloads first; App Stores deferred to 1.1/1.2** (decision K0, locked; **closes ADR-050 Tier-3**, amends ADR-003). | [ADR-081](ADR-081-mfl-to-mrl-data-exchange.md) | MFL → MRL data exchange — file-based RDF/Turtle export over the shared ontology (workstream M of the 1.0 launch plan; bundle offering, 1.1 fast-follow). Implements ADR-006/009's data-exchange boundary | 2026-06-16 | Proposed |
| [ADR-077](ADR-077-bank-feeds.md) | Bank feeds (Arc H) — pluggable providers, GoCardless first. No free universal bank API exists and the owner's accounts span UK+US, so: a **pluggable provider framework** (`mfl_desktop/feeds/`, Qt-free, stdlib-only) where **each user supplies their own credentials** (no central cost for a freely-shared app), and feeds **reuse the existing import pipeline** (normalise → `_classify_and_stage` → FITID/hash dedup → review → `commit_import`; zero new dedup logic). Rejected: Plaid/TrueLayer (central per-connection cost), auto-commit (review step is the safety), persisting tokens. **Verified** offscreen: normalizer mapping; GoCardless client request-building + HTTP-error handling against a stub; `feed_account` CRUD + cascade; `stage_feed`→`commit_import` re-fetch idempotency (2 imported, then 0/2 deduped). | [ADR-076](ADR-076-design-tokens-and-dark-mode.md) | Design tokens + light/dark theming (Arc B rounds 1–2) — amends ADR-026. **Round 2 (2026-06-15)** finished dark mode by theming the B1 light "islands": `chart_helpers` gained token-based structural-colour accessors (`chart_surface`/`chart_grid`/`chart_axis_ink`/`chart_ink`/`chart_faint`/`chart_tooltip_bg`), all ~12 paintEvent charts' structural `QColor` calls + the `account_summary_window` (`_COLOR_*` + inline styles + paint) converted to them; the series palette stays and white-on-fill text stays white; `apply_theme` now force-repaints all widgets so charts redraw on a live toggle. **Round 1:** Consolidates ~140 scattered hardcoded hex literals (two drifted ramps: gray vs slate, plus casing mismatches) into one **semantic token layer** (`ui/tokens.py`: `canvas`/`surface`/`text`/`heading`/`muted`/`accent`/`positive`/`negative`/… each with a **light** + **dark** value) and adds a persisted light/dark **toggle** (View ▸ Dark Mode). ---

## Summaries

### ADR-001 — Backend language and triple store
Selects **Python** as the backend language and **Oxigraph** (via `pyoxigraph`) as the embedded triple store, consistent with the sister application My Retirement Life. Oxigraph runs inside the Python process with no separate server, has a very low memory footprint suitable for older consumer hardware, and is fully SPARQL 1.1 compliant. The API layer uses **FastAPI**. Consistency with MRL is an explicit goal — both apps share an ontology and are designed to eventually share a database, making stack alignment a strong reason to adopt the same decisions rather than re-evaluate from scratch.

### ADR-002 — Frontend stack
Selects **HTMX + Tailwind CSS + DaisyUI** as the frontend stack, consistent with My Retirement Life. HTMX enables server-driven UI updates from the FastAPI backend without a JavaScript build pipeline. DaisyUI provides a complete component library including built-in light/dark theming. **Chart.js** (CDN) is used for data visualisation. Consistency with MRL is the primary driver; the stack was already validated for this type of application.

### ADR-003 — Packaging strategy
Defines the distribution approach for non-technical end users: **Windows** (PyInstaller → `.exe`), **macOS** (PyInstaller → `.app` bundle), and **Linux** (PyInstaller → AppImage). Consistent with My Retirement Life. A single build toolchain produces all platform targets. Unsigned macOS builds will show a Gatekeeper warning on first launch until code signing is implemented.

### ADR-004 — Cross-platform portability approach
Defines engineering practices that enforce Windows/Linux/macOS portability: `pathlib.Path` for all file path construction, `platformdirs` for OS-appropriate data directories, `.gitattributes` enforcing LF line endings, `python-dotenv` for configuration, and a prohibition on platform-specific runtime dependencies. Consistent with My Retirement Life ADR-004.

### ADR-005 — Ontology strategy — MRL dependency and MFL extension
My Financial Life reuses the My Retirement Life ontology (`mrl:` namespace) as a shared foundation for currencies, jurisdictions, persons, and the full account hierarchy. MFL-specific concepts (transactions, payees, category rules, import batches, valuation events) are defined in a separate `mfl:` namespace in `mfl-ontology.ttl`. Both TTL files are loaded into a single ontology named graph on startup. Extraction to a neutral shared namespace (`mrl-core`) is deferred until both apps are stable. This decision is recorded in MRL as ADR-010.

### ADR-006 — Instance IRI naming strategy
All user-created instance IRIs follow the pattern **`mfl:ClassName_<uuid>`** where the UUID is generated at creation time (e.g. `mfl:Transaction_3f2a1b`). UUIDs are used rather than incrementing integers (as in MRL) because transactions are created at high volume and UUIDs avoid any risk of collision during bulk import. MRL's integer pattern is retained for low-volume entities shared with MRL (accounts, persons) where human-readability in SPARQL is more valuable.

### ADR-007 — Data access patterns — quad patterns vs SPARQL
Establishes a clear split between the two Oxigraph read mechanisms, consistent with MRL ADR-007: **`quads_for_pattern`** is used for fetching all properties of a known IRI and checking existence. **SPARQL SELECT** is used for filtering, aggregation, multi-hop traversal, and reporting queries. All writes use **SPARQL UPDATE** with explicit XSD datatype annotations on numeric, boolean, and date values.

### ADR-008 — Desktop application UI framework
Replaces the v0.1 browser-based frontend with a native desktop UI built on **PySide6 (Qt for Python)**, packaged as a single Windows `.exe` via PyInstaller. macOS and Linux follow. Qt's Model/View architecture (`QAbstractTableModel` + `QTableView`) is purpose-built for the high-performance, editable, virtualised transaction register the application needs and which HTML/HTMX could not deliver to a Banktivity-grade standard. Tauri, Electron, Flutter, and .NET MAUI were considered and rejected — Tauri because it still renders the UI in a WebView and forces either a Rust rewrite of the import engine or a sidecar process; the others because they discard the existing Python parser/import investment. Supersedes ADR-002.

### ADR-009 — Storage engine for ledger data
Replaces Oxigraph as MFL's primary store with **SQLite**, motivated by the actual workload: tens of thousands of transactions, register filter/sort/search/paginate at sub-100 ms, and per-lot IRR/ROI calculations — all materially easier and faster in SQL than SPARQL. **MRL retains Oxigraph** because its workload (tax law across jurisdictions, heterogeneous evolving relationships) is what RDF was designed for. The "shared database with MRL" goal from ADR-001 moves from the storage layer to the integration boundary — MFL can read MRL's store as a reference source and emit RDF for export, but writes its own data relationally. DuckDB is recorded as a future analytical attachment if reports become a bottleneck. Partially supersedes ADR-001.

### ADR-010 — Transactional schema design
Fixes the concrete SQLite schema implementing ADR-009: nine tables (`person`, `account`, `category`, `payee`, `txn`, `lot`, `valuation`, `rule`, `import_batch`), each carrying both an internal `id` and a cross-app `iri` per ADR-006. **Currency stored as INTEGER minor units (pence)** for exact arithmetic; REAL only for non-currency quantities like share counts. **Categories are hierarchical and dual-sourced** (system/user/import), with `parent_id` self-referencing adjacency and `WITH RECURSIVE` for descendant queries. All system-default categories are deletable except the reserved **Uncategorised** row, which serves as the deletion sink (carve-out enforced at the Repository layer). Import path conflicts auto-create as separate categories rather than prompting or auto-merging. Duplicate detection preserved from v0.1 via a partial unique index on `(account_id, import_hash)`. The reference SQL is in [`docs/schema.sql`](../schema.sql).

### ADR-011 — Account delete policy
The desktop app's account-management UI exposes **hard delete only** for v0.1, with a confirmation dialog that names the account, shows the cascaded transaction count, and warns the action cannot be undone. The schema-level `archived_at` column remains **reserved** for a future Archive UX; `Repository.list_accounts` continues to filter it out so adding archive later is additive (Repository methods + sidebar filter, no schema migration). Matches the user's stated request for this milestone; a non-technical user's mental model of "delete" is preserved; cascading is enforced at the FK layer so deletions are never partial.

### ADR-012 — Payee name-management policy
Defines the policy behind the desktop app's payee-management UI. **Rename collisions reject** with an error that directs the user to Merge — auto-merging on rename would silently reassign hundreds of transactions on what looks like a single-row edit. **Merge is the explicit destructive verb**: the user picks 2+ payees, chooses a target — either one of the selected payees or a brand-new name typed at the picker — and confirms a dialog that names the target and states the reassignment count, with the work done atomically in one SQL transaction. Typing a name that matches an existing payee outside the selection is rejected so a single merge never silently pulls in unselected payees. **Delete preserves transactions and clears their payee** via the schema's `ON DELETE SET NULL` FK rule; the confirmation surfaces this consequence explicitly. Same rename / merge / delete shape is reused for category management (ADR-013).

### ADR-013 — Category management policy
Extends the ADR-012 shape to the hierarchical category tree with the **Reparent** verb added. **Rename collisions reject** per-parent (`UNIQUE(parent_id, name)`); the user is directed to Merge. **Reparent rejects cycles** (target in the moved subtree, via `WITH RECURSIVE` descendant query) and **rejects sibling-name collisions** at the new parent. **Merge rejects sources with subcategories** — the cascade-collision morass of moving children with the merged node is avoided by forcing the user to reparent or merge children first. Merge target may be one of the selected categories or a brand-new top-level name; an existing-outside-selection match rejects per ADR-012. **Delete reassigns transactions to the reserved Uncategorised row** (ADR-010 id=1) after a counted confirmation, **rejects Uncategorised itself**, and **rejects categories with subcategories** rather than silently demoting children via `ON DELETE SET NULL`. Every destructive verb stays at one level at a time; deep restructures are a sequence of small reversible steps, not a single click whose effects are hard to predict.

### ADR-014 — Category kind
Adds a **per-category `kind` column** with values `income`, `expense`, `transfer` (CHECK constraint), so reports and cashflow can interpret signed amounts: a positive amount on an expense category reads as a refund; a negative on an income category as a correction; transfers don't count in either bucket. Migration `0002` adds the column, backfills via recursive CTE (Income subtree → income; everything else → expense), and seeds `Transfer` as the third reserved top-level system root. **New top-level categories pick their kind**; **sub-categories inherit the parent's kind**. **Reparenting across kinds is an explicit confirmation** — confirming cascades the new kind to all descendants. **Merging across kinds is rejected** up front so the user converts kind first via reparent. Uncategorised defaults to `kind='expense'`; reports should surface its transactions as "needs categorising" separately rather than rolling them into the refund total. Import-created top-level categories default to `expense`. Per-row column chosen over derived-from-root because it matches the Banktivity mental model the owner is coming from and avoids forcing a migration of every existing top-level non-system category under a kind root.

### ADR-015 — Account folders in the sidebar
Replaces the flat `QListWidget` sidebar with a two-column `QTreeWidget` (Name | Balance) so accounts can be grouped into Banktivity-style folders. Migration `0003` adds an `account_folder` table (id, name, sort_order, archived_at) and a nullable `account.folder_id` FK with `ON DELETE SET NULL`. Folders are **flat** (no nesting) in v1 — nesting is an additive future migration. Folders are **display-only** — clicking a folder toggles expansion; only accounts and "All transactions" change the register view. Folder-as-view-mode is recorded in the backlog. Balance computation is `opening_balance + SUM(txn.amount)` per account in one query; folder sums are computed in the sidebar, **summed naively across currencies** (documented limitation). Folder verbs: New, Rename, Delete (accounts inside fall to root), Move Up/Down (swap sort_order with neighbour), plus Move Account → Folder ▸ submenu on the account context menu. Account reordering inside folders is deferred per the owner's steer.

### ADR-016 — File save / open model
**No plain Save** menu item — every Repository commit already hits disk, so a "Save" verb would be a no-op and mislead. Two file verbs only: **File → Save Copy As… (Ctrl+Shift+S)** writes an atomic SQLite backup of the current DB to a chosen path via `sqlite3.Connection.backup()` (online + WAL-safe); **File → Open… (Ctrl+O)** closes the current Repository, opens a new one against the chosen file (migration runner upgrades older backups to the current schema), and rebuilds sidebar + category cache + filter combo + register model in one swap. Window title shows the current filename so the user can't accidentally edit the wrong file when juggling backups. File extension: `.mfl` preferred, `.db` accepted on Open; Save Copy As defaults to `.mfl` when the user doesn't type an extension. Document-style dirty tracking is rejected — autosave is universally preferable for financial data, and matching the on-disk-is-truth contract is correct given how Repository writes already work.

### ADR-017 — Bulk edit shape
The register's bulk-edit verb is a **modal dialog with per-field checkboxes**: Payee, Category, Status, Memo. Each row has a leading checkbox that enables its editor; only checked fields are applied to the selection. Empty Payee or Memo with the box ticked **clears** that field on every selected row. Category and Status are NOT NULL, so they have no clear semantics — the user must pick a value. One repository call (`bulk_update_transactions` with an `_UNSET` sentinel that distinguishes "don't change" from "clear to None") runs every checked field's UPDATE inside a single SQL transaction; failure mid-way rolls back the whole batch. Triggers: Transaction menu → Bulk Edit Selected… (**Ctrl+E**) and the table's right-click menu (entry only appears when ≥2 rows are selected). Single-row edits stay on the existing inline editor — the bulk dialog would be noisier for one row. Bulk bar (persistent inline editor strip) and per-field context-menu actions were rejected: bulk bar mixes "what's selected" with "what's editable" in one UI region, and per-field actions break the atomic-across-N-rows feel by requiring one prompt per field.

### ADR-018 — Reports framework + first chart: Spending Over Time
Reports open from a new top-level **Reports** menu into **non-modal `QMainWindow`s**, single-instance per report (re-clicking raises the existing window). Chart library is **QtCharts** (bundled with PySide6 — no extra dep). The first report is **Spending Over Time**: stacked bar chart, granularity = weekly / monthly / quarterly / annually, configurable date range, account filter, category-group filter, Include Uncategorised toggle, dashed average line drawn across the chart, and a summary strip showing total + average + bucket count. Defaults: Monthly, last 12 months, all accounts, all groups, Uncategorised included. Spending semantics: **strict outflow** — `SUM(-amount)` on `kind='expense'` rows where `amount < 0`. Net-spending (refunds reduce) was considered and rejected for v1 because Uncategorised's `kind='expense'` default (ADR-014) misclassifies imported income as refunds, producing negative bar segments that don't render cleanly. Refund handling moves to the future Cash Flow report. **Pie charts are explicitly out** (owner rule). Grouping rule for stack segments: a transaction's category rolls up to its **deepest ancestor whose parent is a root** — so `Expense → Groceries → Tesco` groups as `Groceries`. Uncategorised is its own group with its own toggle. Auto-refresh on every control change (no Refresh button) — at ~1.3k rows the SQL is well under a frame. Average line uses an invisible second `QValueAxis` on the bottom because mixing categorical-x bars and numeric-x lines in one `QChart` needs two x-axes sharing one y-axis.

### ADR-019 — Net Worth report
Three-column non-modal `QMainWindow` modelled on Pocketsmith's Net Worth view, opened from **Reports → Net Worth…**. **Summary** (left): big net-worth total, a horizontal **`ProportionalBar`** showing asset-family widths (no pie — owner rule), colour-coded legend. **Assets** (middle): green header + total, `QTreeWidget` grouped by `account.family` (Cash & Bank, Investments, Property), each group expanded with its individual accounts; "+ Asset" button at the bottom. **Debts** (right): red mirror — liability balances stored negative in the DB are displayed as positive amounts (£429 owed, not -£429); "+ Debt" button. Family → label/colour mapping is a small static table; adding a new family means adding a row there. Investment / property balances in v1 still use `opening_balance + sum(txns)` — the schema's `valuation` table is reserved for mark-to-market but isn't wired yet. Add Account opens the existing `AccountDialog` (same dialog from both + buttons, no preset) and refreshes the register's sidebar after creation.

### ADR-020 — Account transfers
A transfer is **one user intent realised as two linked `txn` rows** — outflow on the source, inflow on the destination — paired by a shared `transfer_id TEXT` column (`mfl:Transfer_<uuid8>` per ADR-006). Migration `0004` adds the column and a partial index. The **verb is the category**: there is no dedicated New Transfer menu item; picking a `kind='transfer'` category on any creation/edit flow (New Transaction, inline cell edit, Bulk Edit) prompts for the destination account and creates the partner row. **`create_transfer`** handles fresh transfers from New Transaction; **`convert_to_transfer`** handles existing-row → transfer-half conversion (inline edit); **`bulk_set_category_and_convert`** handles bulk-edit batches atomically. Direction is encoded in the source row's signed amount — partner gets the opposite sign — so the same conversion logic works regardless of whether the user is entering an outflow or an inflow. **Delete is partner-aware**: `delete_transactions` expands the selection via `expand_transfer_partners` so the user can't strand half a transfer. Payee convention: `create_transfer` sets both halves to "Transfer to/from {account}"; `convert_to_transfer` leaves the source's existing payee alone (preserves import-derived payees) and only the new partner gets the convention payee. Edit-sync, auto un-transfer on category change away from transfer kind, and import-side transfer detection are all deferred to future revisions.

### ADR-021 — Generic CSV column-mapping wizard
Closes the open hole in CSV import: when `_detect_format` returns `"generic"` (Pocketsmith, generic bank CSVs, anything that isn't Banktivity/credit-card/OFX/QFX), a new single-screen modal `CsvMappingDialog` lets the user map Date / Amount / Payee / Memo / Category to columns in their file. **Smart-default pre-fill** scans the file's headers against the alias lists already in `csv_parser.py` (`_DATE_ALIASES` etc., plus a new `_CATEGORY_ALIASES`) so conventional Pocketsmith-style files open with all combos already set — the user just confirms. **Amount style** is a radio toggle between *Single signed column* (with an `Invert sign` checkbox for credit-card-style positive=debit exports) and *Separate debit and credit columns*. **Date format** offers `auto` plus named strptime presets plus a free-text custom. **Live after-mapping preview** re-parses the staged 5 preview rows on every widget change and shows `(unparseable)` cells in red so date-format mismatches and inverted-sign confusions are visible before commit. The dialog is **purely value-producing** — accepts → caller reads `.mapping`, rejects → caller calls the new `ImportService.discard_pending_map(token)` — and `register_window._on_import` now routes the mapped result through the same `_commit_pending()` helper as known-format imports, so the silent-commit-and-status-bar pattern (per the no-dialog-for-known-imports feedback) holds once the format is understood. **No schema change**; no new tables. **Saved mapping profiles are explicitly deferred** — auto-detecting a repeat Pocketsmith CSV by header signature and skipping the dialog is its own future ADR, not bolted onto this one.

### ADR-022 — Register typeahead delegates + inline category create
Replaces the register's bare `QLineEdit`/`QComboBox` cell editors with two repository-backed typeahead delegates so payee and category inline edits match the dialog flows (`make_category_picker`). **`PayeeTypeaheadDelegate`** wraps a `QLineEdit` with a `QCompleter` populated from a new `Repository.list_payee_names()` (contains-match, case-insensitive); new names continue to be silently created via the existing `get_or_create_payee` path. **`CategoryTypeaheadDelegate`** uses the same `make_category_picker` combo as `NewTransactionDialog` and `BulkEditDialog`, reading `list_categories_flat()` fresh on every `createEditor` so a category created inline appears immediately in the next opened editor (no delegate-rebind dance). When the user types a name that doesn't match any category, the delegate calls back to the window which shows a single Yes/No confirm prompt ("Create category 'X' as a new top-level expense category?"); on Yes the category is created with `parent_id=None`, `kind='expense'`, `source='user'` and the cell commit proceeds. Defaults match the import path's `find_or_create_category_path(default_root_kind='expense')` so inline-create and import behaviour are aligned; re-parenting or re-kinding happens in Manage ▸ Categories. A new lightweight `_reload_category_cache()` on the window refreshes the cached choice list and the filter-bar combo without resetting the model, so the inline-create path is safe to call from inside a delegate's `setModelData` (the existing `_refresh_categories_view` still does the full reload + delegate rebind for the import and category-management mutation paths). No schema change.

### ADR-023 — Scheduled transactions
First half of the budget arc — adds the `scheduled_txn` template primitive that the budget round will consume for planned-spending projection. **Schedule-as-template**: one schedule row stores cadence (`weekly` / `biweekly` / `monthly` / `quarterly` / `annual`), an anchor date, a next-due date, an optional end date, an estimated signed amount, a `variable` flag (prompt for actual amount on post), and an `auto_post` flag. Posting materialises exactly one `txn` (or one transfer pair via `create_transfer` if the category is `kind='transfer'`) and advances `next_due_date` — past materialised txns are independent records; the schedule is the template, the txn is the truth. **Manual post by default**, per-schedule auto-post opt-in; a launch-time sweep materialises all `auto_post=1` schedules due through today (loop-based so a user gone two months catches up in one launch). **Anchor-based cadence math** (`min(anchor.day, days_in_target_month)`) so Jan 31 monthly → Feb 28 → Mar 31 (not Mar 28) and Feb 29 annual → Feb 28 in non-leap years. **Transfer schedules reuse `create_transfer`** behaviour from ADR-020 — sign of estimated amount picks source vs destination; `transfer_to_account_id` required when category kind is `transfer`. **`Manage → Schedules…`** single menu entry with table view + New / Edit / Post Now / Delete buttons. **No back-link** from materialised txn to source schedule in v1 (deferred — additive when added). **No `rule` reuse** — categorisation rules and schedule templates are different verbs and stay separate primitives. Migration `0005` adds the table + two partial indexes (one for the auto-post sweep, one broader for the budget projection).

### ADR-058 — Budget redesign (hybrid envelope / zero-sum / long-term planning)
**Supersedes ADR-024 + ADR-025.** Umbrella for a re-design prompted by the owner re-stating the budget's principles after real use of the (always-"rough") original. Twelve principles: multiple budgets + scenarios; a genuine hybrid of envelope + zero-sum + long-term planning (every app picks one); accounts picked first with the **available pool = their balance** (later: credit-card credit as a source + a pay-down feature); a **budget period** (default Jan–Dec); category selection with **historical-average suggestions**; **roll-up budgeting that still tracks children** (budget Bills £500, track electric/gas/council-tax under it); **rollover** (or take the excess elsewhere); a **12-month matrix** of Budget/Actual/Diff by income/expense/transfer; **unbudgeted spending shown as such**; the matrix **editable**; matrix = default annual view, plus a **monthly view** with charts; a **burn-down for any category or the whole budget that projects forward at the current spend rate** (better than Pocketsmith's stop-at-today). The load-bearing pivot: ADR-024's single amortized `amount+cadence` can't support editing one month or rollover, so the model moves to **explicit per-month `budget_allocation` rows** (the matrix is the native object) with a **copy-forward affordance** on edit (just this month / this + later / all 12). Owner-resolved forks: **soft** zero-sum (an `Unallocated = pool − assigned` indicator that reddens but never blocks); **auto-rollover** per line (default on for expenses; `carry_in` computed, not stored; reallocate by editing cells — no move ledger). Migration 0019 extends `budget` (`start_month`/`length_months`/`currency`), adds `budget_line` (envelope: category + role + rollover) + `budget_allocation` (per-month cell), migrates + drops `budget_category`. Actuals + rollover stay **computed** in a rewritten-but-still-pure `budget_calc.compute_matrix`; perimeter cancellation, nearest-budgeted-ancestor bucketing, and paintEvent charts all carry forward. Phased (R1–R4b shipped; R4c remaining): **R1** foundation + editable matrix (+ auto-rollover math, suggestions, soft Unallocated) → **R2** per-line rollover/role controls (context menu + ↻ glyph; inline child-expansion dropped in favour of the R1 drill-down) → **R3** monthly progress-bar view + projected burn-down (`compute_burndown` + rebuilt `burn_down_chart.py`, Annual/Monthly toggle) → **R4a** credit cards as a budget pool source (migration 0020: `account.credit_limit` + `budget_account.contribution` = balance/available_credit/excluded) → **R4b** pay-down goals (migration 0021 `budget_goal`; pure `goal_calc` on signed balances; balance-based progress measured from a captured baseline; a Goals strip with `_GoalCard`s + `GoalDialog` in both views) → **R4c** savings goals (the asset-side mirror, mostly already built via the `kind='savings'` path). Plus an annual-matrix polish pass (Total column, Net bottom line, collapsible sections, section-header budget totals).

### ADR-024 — Budget core *(superseded by ADR-058)*
Second half of the budget arc — adds the budget itself: which accounts are in scope (perimeter), which categories have per-period targets at what cadence, and the screen that renders the math. **One budget per file in v1, schema supports many** via dedicated `budget` / `budget_account` (M:N perimeter) / `budget_category` (target + cadence + role) tables (migration 0006). **Perimeter rule**: transfers between two in-perimeter accounts cancel out; transfers crossing the perimeter count as a normal flow. Enforced at SQL via a `NOT EXISTS (… partner …)` subquery in `list_perimeter_txns`. **Per-category amount stored as positive magnitude**, direction inferred from `category.kind` (income/expense/transfer) — single source of truth. **Role on `budget_category` not `category`** (bills / saving / discretionary) — keeps multi-budget future open without category-level lock-in. **Transfer-kind budget categories are skipped in the tile math entirely** (post-ship amendment) — actuals already cancel for intra-perimeter transfers; the planned amount no longer leaks into Income / Bills / Saving / Spending and quietly reduces Available. **Nearest-budgeted-ancestor bucketing** for actuals: a txn on a sub-category lands under the closest ancestor that has a budget; if none, it falls to the "Other" bucket. Matches the user mental model regardless of where they choose to budget (leaves, parents, both). **Pure-Python `mfl_desktop/budget_calc.py`** does the bucketing, pro-rating (`365.25/12` for non-monthly cadences, identity pass-through for matching cadence on its own calendar period), and the four Simplifi-style tiles: Income after bills & saving (planned income − planned bills − planned saving) / Planned spending (sum of discretionary expense budgets pro-rated) / Other spending (actual outflow magnitude on un-budgeted categories) / Available (income tile − planned spending − other spending). **Cash-on-hand badge** in the header separately answers "is my account balance going to survive?" — complementary to the plan-side tile math. **No rollover** in v1. **Two-line non-monthly card display** ships in ADR-025. Setup dialog is a two-tab modal (Accounts + Categories) with Add/Edit/Remove on the category rows; the budget screen is a non-modal `QMainWindow` opened from a new top-level **`Budget → Open Budget…`** menu (`Ctrl+B`), refreshing on `WindowActivate` so flipping back from the register reflects new actuals.

### ADR-025 — Budget visualisations
Third and final round of the budget arc — closes the four ADR-024 deferrals in one pass. **Full-cadence-period subtitle**: a non-monthly card (e.g. £1,800/year Holidays) now shows the pro-rated monthly figure on its first subtitle line *and* a second italic line "£1,800 annually · this year: £450 of £1,800" so the long view is preserved. Cadence-period boundaries follow the global anchor rule (Monday weeks, calendar quarters/years; bi-weekly is the 14-day window ending on the reference date pending a future per-schedule anchor). **Burn-down chart** (`mfl_desktop/ui/burn_down_chart.py`): QtCharts line chart sitting under the tile strip, two series (Actual cumulative outflow red solid, Ideal linear pacing grey dashed), with a vertical today-marker. Total planned = bills + saving + planned_spending (income excluded — depletion, not net-cash; transfers already excluded by ADR-024's tile-math fix). **Proportional summary bar** (`mfl_desktop/ui/proportional_bar.py` reused from ADR-019): horizontal segmented bar showing Bills / Saving / Planned spending / Other spending / Available as positive segments summing to Planned income, with a colour-keyed legend underneath. Owner's no-pies rule (ADR-018) preserved. **Scheduled projection**: per-card "+£X expected" badge surfaces un-posted scheduled outflows whose `next_due_date` falls in the screen period (overdue schedules from prior periods are deliberately *not* surfaced — they belong in `Manage → Schedules`). All computation lives in `mfl_desktop/budget_calc.py` as additive optional inputs to `compute_budget_view`; the pure-function contract that made round-B testability cheap carries forward. No schema change, no new repository methods — everything reuses primitives from rounds A (`list_perimeter_schedules_due_through`) and B (`list_perimeter_txns`).

### ADR-026 — Visual style baseline and chart-engine comparison
Two related decisions in response to the "1990's Microsoft" feel surfaced after ADR-025. **Visual baseline adopted**: Fusion style + a custom QPalette (Tailwind v3 slate neutrals + `blue-600` accent) + a minimal QSS layer for inputs/buttons/table-header/scrollbars, centralised in `mfl_desktop/ui/theme.py::apply_theme(app)` and called once from `__main__`. Native `windows11` rejected for ignoring palette overrides and producing inconsistent cross-platform metrics; third-party themes (qt-material, PyQtDarkTheme) reserved as the next step if the Fusion baseline doesn't go far enough. **Chart engine — custom paintEvent chosen** after a side-by-side comparison (QtCharts vs pyqtgraph vs hand-rolled QPainter, ran behind a temporary Engine combo on the Spending window with real ~1,300-transaction data). Owner picked paintEvent for the modern flat look (rounded top corners on the topmost stack segment, 1px white separators, soft gridlines, pill-shaped dashed average label) plus full typography/format control plus zero new dependency; performance was a non-issue at the current data scale. Same paintEvent approach ported to the burn-down chart at the same time (`burn_down_chart.py` rewritten, public `set_data(BurnDownData)` contract preserved so `budget_window.py` didn't change). Shared chart primitives (palette, `nice_ticks`, `fmt_currency`, `legend_chip`) live in `mfl_desktop/ui/chart_helpers.py` so any future chart shape reuses them. `pyqtgraph` removed from requirements; QtCharts no longer imported by either chart widget (still pulled in transitively by PySide6, just unused).

### ADR-027 — Create Schedule From Transaction (right-click verb)
Tiny UX addition built on ADR-023's existing schedule primitives — owner asked for "right-click on a transaction → Create Schedule From Transaction" with payee / amount / category / account / date pre-filled and a monthly default cadence. **Seeding mechanism**: new frozen `ScheduleSeed` dataclass in `schedule_dialog.py` (account_id, payee_name, category_id, transfer_to_account_id, amount, anchor_date, cadence, memo — all `Optional`) carried via a new `seed=` kwarg on `ScheduleDialog.__init__`. Dialog stays in create mode; the existing `if is_edit ... else <default>` ternaries become `if is_edit ... else (seed.value if seed else <default>)`. Edit mode ignores the seed if both are passed. Reusable for future "create schedule from X" entry points (e.g. payee-management dialog) without further dialog surgery. **Anchor / next-due semantics** (revised same-day after owner feedback): handler pre-computes the next future occurrence by stepping `txn.posted_date` forward by the default cadence until the result is strictly after today, then passes that date as `seed.anchor_date`. The dialog surfaces it as **"Next occurrence:"** (label change applied to both seeded and from-scratch flows — drops the misleading "First occurrence (anchor)" wording).
