On save anchor = next_due = that future date — same shape as a from-scratch schedule. Cadence default `monthly`. The earlier ADR-027 design kept anchor=txn-date and overrode next_due=anchor+cadence to preserve "31st of every month" rhythm; owner found the dialog showing the txn's *past* date confusing, so the rhythm-preservation property was traded for a simpler one-flow design. Edge case (Jan 31 seed → schedule sticks to 28th forever instead of bouncing back to 31st) is recoverable by hand-editing the anchor in edit mode. **Transfer pre-fill**: new `Repository.get_transfer_partner_account_id(txn_id)` returns the partner row's account_id via a single-row SQL query, called only when `txn.transfer_id IS NOT NULL`. Seeds `transfer_to_account_id` so transfer-half rows work identically to regular rows. **UI placement**: right-click menu item appears between New Transaction and the destructive verbs, with separators above and below; visible only when exactly one row is selected (multi-row seed merging deliberately rejected). Status-bar confirmation includes the computed next-due date so the user can sanity-check the rhythm at a glance. No schema change, no new migrations.

### ADR-028 — Payee aliases, canonical labels, and the auto-categorisation arc (planning)
Planning ADR for a three-round arc that closes the long-running payee-cleanup and rules-engine gaps. Originated from an in-session question about auto-deleting orphan payees after a rename; the conversation broadened to the architecture every mature personal-finance app converges on (Banktivity "Payee Aliases", Quicken "Memorized Payees", YNAB "Payee renaming rules"). **Three concepts kept separate**: canonical payee (preferred label + metadata), alias (raw imported string that maps to a canonical), category rule (independent automation that can fire on either). Owner's two import paths fall out — Path A (fastidious, alias rewrites raw → canonical, category from canonical) and Path B (no cleanup, raw payee stays, category from rule pattern). **Schema choice — Option A self-referential `canonical_id` on the existing `payee` table** (chosen over a two-table split or stuffing aliasing into the `rule` table). One nullable column, one index, no `txn.payee_id` change. `canonical_id IS NULL` means "I am canonical"; non-NULL means "I am an alias of …". Typeaheads filter `WHERE canonical_id IS NULL`; reports roll up via `COALESCE(canonical_id, id)`. Two-level rule (no alias-of-alias) enforced at the Repository layer. **Three rounds in order**: round 1 — data model + manual alias UI (polish-scope, one sitting; closes the "clean my list by hand" case without import-engine changes); round 2 — import-time alias lookup as its own arc (exact match at minimum, pattern / fuzzy as follow-ups); round 3 — rules engine as its own arc (long-deferred CLAUDE_CONTEXT backlog item, finally wired up). Recommended scheduling: round 1 before Reports round 2 (typeahead and rollup helpers make the hierarchical category picker cleaner); rounds 2 and 3 after Reports round 2. **ADR-012 will be amended after round 1** to record the canonical/alias model and the "merge vs alias" distinction. **CLAUDE_CONTEXT "Categorisation rules engine" backlog item absorbed into round 3.** **Orphan-cleanup question dissolved** — typos become aliases (cheap, recoverable), not deletes (lossy). No round-1 implementation in this ADR; per-round implementation ADRs follow when each round starts.

### ADR-029 — Payee aliases round 1 — data model + manual alias UI
First round of the ADR-028 arc, owner-managed aliasing (no import-engine change). **Schema**: migration 0007 adds `payee.canonical_id INTEGER REFERENCES payee(id) ON DELETE SET NULL` + a partial index. Existing rows canonical by default; additive migration. **Two-level rule** (no alias-of-alias) enforced at the Repository — SQLite CHECK isn't expressive enough. **Repository additions**: `set_alias_of`, `promote_to_canonical`, `list_canonical_payees`, `list_aliases_of`. `list_payee_names` filtered to `canonical_id IS NULL` so the typeahead and bulk-edit completer only suggest canonicals. `list_payees_with_usage` rewritten to return one flat SQL list, Python rolls alias direct counts up to their canonical; `PayeeRow` extended with `canonical_id` / `canonical_name` / `direct_usage_count`. **Merge updated** to re-point aliases of sources onto the target before deleting sources (FK's `ON DELETE SET NULL` would otherwise auto-promote them — wrong for a merge). **Payees dialog**: 3 columns (Name / Alias of / Used in) instead of 2; aliases indented with `↳ ` and italic; column 1 shows `alias of <canonical>` in grey; sort-on-column-0 disabled to preserve grouped order; filter matches against stored name not display text. Two new buttons: **Make &Alias of…** (≥1 selected) and **&Promote to Canonical** (≥1 selected AND all aliases). Target picker mirrors the merge-target picker — editable combo over existing canonicals, typing a brand-new name creates one. **Display surfaces deferred from round 1**: register inline display doesn't roll up to canonical (silent rewrite-on-no-change pitfall via the inline typeahead; round 2's import-engine work is the natural place); reports payee aggregation has no current call sites (grep empty). **ADR-012 amended** with the canonical/alias model + merge-re-points-aliases subtlety + the three-shape verb table (Merge / Alias / Delete).

### ADR-030 — Spending Over Time rollup levels — Top / Group / Leaf
First Reports round-2 follow-up to ADR-018. Adds a **Rollup** combo to `SpendingReportWindow` with three positions and flips the default. **Top level** (default) walks each expense category up to its topmost ancestor (`parent_id is None`); **Group** preserves ADR-018's second-tier rule unchanged; **Leaf** is the identity map (every category is its own bucket). New `mfl_desktop/reports.py::category_root_map` helper mirrors `category_group_map`'s shape so the report window doesn't case-split at filter time — it picks the active map and uses it the same way. Categories checklist rebuilds on rollup change with all items checked; per-rollup preservation of unchecked state intentionally not attempted because the bucket-id set changes across rollups. Uncategorised's separate toggle survives at all three levels (Uncategorised is itself a root, so its bucket is itself in every mode). Rejected alternatives: replacing the default rather than adding a control (loses drilldown without re-open); folding rollup into the deferred hierarchical-picker tree widget (rollup is a single global level, expand-state is per-row — conflating the two complicates both); persisting per-window rollup preference (out of scope, report window is stateless by ADR-018). Naming: "Top level / Group / Leaf" picked over Root/Mid alternatives because "Top level" mirrors existing UI vocabulary and "Group" is the ADR-018 term users already see.

### ADR-031 — Hierarchical category picker via full-path labels
Second Reports round-2 follow-up. Closes the "typing 'Food' should reveal Food's descendants" gap and the same-named-leaves-under-different-parents disambiguation gap across every category picker in the app in one repository-level change. **Data layer**: `CategoryChoice` gains a `path: str` field; `Repository.list_categories_flat` builds it via a two-pass walk (one cheap SELECT over all non-archived rows to build the `{id: (parent_id, name)}` map, walk the chain per row) and sorts the result by path so siblings cluster DFS-style under their parent. **Picker layer**: `make_category_picker` uses `c.path` as the display label — drops the `Name (ImmediateParent)` branch. `selected_category_id` is unchanged (it already matches displayed text to itemText, which is now the path). The `CategoryTypeaheadDelegate.setEditorData` keys by id, so the label-format change is transparent. **Reports layer**: new shared `mfl_desktop/reports.py::category_path(nodes_by_id, cid)` helper feeds the spending report's checklist so its labels show full paths (matters most at Leaf rollup per ADR-030). **Rejected alternatives**: genuine tree popup replacing QCompleter (more code, different feel from the payee typeahead, hard contains-match semantics — do unmatched branches collapse, hide, grey out?); hybrid flat-for-typeaheads-tree-for-checklists (deferable additively if the spending report's checklist ever surfaces a browsing-by-hierarchy need). Same `→` separator and root-handling convention as the merge picker and `_path_for`. Five combo surfaces (transaction dialog, bulk edit, schedule, budget setup, register inline typeahead) inherit the fix from one helper change. Categories dialog's private `_path_for` stays for now — duplicate of `category_path` but local to that dialog; migrate when convenient.

### ADR-032 — Vehicle account type and the `vehicle` family
Sixth account type alongside the original five (ADR-010). `account_types.py` gains `AccountTypeSpec("vehicle", "vehicle_std", "Vehicle", "VehicleAccount", "vehicle", False)`. Migration 0008 widens the `account.type` CHECK via the standard SQLite table-recreate (six-step swap: foreign_keys OFF, create `account_new`, copy, drop, rename, recreate `idx_account_folder`, foreign_keys ON — FK references INTO account from txn/lot/valuation/import_batch/scheduled_txn/budget_account survive the rename automatically). New `vehicle` family slots into `_FAMILY_VIEW` in the Net Worth window between Property and Cash & Bank with an amber-500 colour (`#f59e0b`), distinct from the existing four hues. **Rejected**: stuffing vehicles under the `property` family (semantically wrong, would mislabel a car as a building in the legend); dropping the CHECK entirely instead of widening it (caught at least one typo bug, defense-in-depth worth the migration cost). The MRL `VehicleAccount` class name follows the existing `<Type>Account` ADR-006 convention so future MRL integration is symmetric. Valuation pipeline for vehicles (KBB / Autotrader-style mark-to-market) is deferred under the broader valuation-pipeline backlog — same family of work as property and investment valuations.

### ADR-033 — Per-account summary screen — combo chart, period selector, top-N breakdowns
Per-account focus screen — the missing other-axis view next to the cross-account register, the budget window, and Net Worth. Banktivity-inspired layout the owner pointed at as a reference. **Combo chart** chosen over a pure line: income bars above the zero baseline, spending bars below, balance polyline overlaid in blue-600 — owner's framing was "would be good for current accounts and also quite a nice view for a credit card to see the balance coming down if you're trying to pay off a debt." `BalanceFlowChart` is a paintEvent widget reusing `chart_helpers` (palette, `nice_ticks`, `fmt_currency`). Single y-axis with independent positive/negative scaling and a shared step so gridlines line up; dual axes deferred as the obvious v2 if real use shows the bars getting stunted when the balance scale dwarfs the flow scale (or vice versa). **Period selector**: six fixed presets — Last 30 days / Last 90 days / YTD / Last 12 months / Last 5 years / All time — each auto-picks a bucket granularity (daily ≤45d, weekly ≤120d, monthly ≤800d, quarterly ≤2200d, yearly beyond). Default Last 90 days. **Pure-Python `mfl_desktop/account_summary.py`** mirrors `budget_calc.py` in shape: `compute_balance_flow_series` / `compute_period_summary` / `compute_status_breakdown` / `top_payees` / `top_categories` / `upcoming_scheduled`, all over the `TransactionRow` and `ScheduledTxnRow` records the Repository already returns. Strict-outflow semantics for the top-N panels (matches ADR-018 / ADR-030). **Status breakdown**: Pending+Uncleared grouped as "uncleared" matching user-facing language; Cleared+Reconciled as cleared. Recorded balance = cleared + uncleared. **Window** (`mfl_desktop/ui/account_summary_window.py`) is a non-modal `QMainWindow`, two-row split (chart + info panel up top, top-payees + top-categories below) in nested `QSplitter`s so the owner can re-balance any of the four panes. Refreshes on `WindowActivate`, same idiom as `BudgetWindow`. **Entry points**: sidebar context menu (Account Summary… first item on account rows), sidebar double-click on an account row, Account → Summary… (Ctrl+I) in the menu bar. **Single-instance per account**: `RegisterWindow._account_summary_wins: dict[int, AccountSummaryWindow]` keyed on `account.id`; opening an account that already has a window raises and focuses it. **Reconcile placeholder**: the screenshot's "NO STATEMENTS · RECONCILE ›" row is rendered now (info dialog says reconciliation is coming) so the layout doesn't churn when the reconciliation arc lands — owner explicitly asked for the entry point to be reserved in the layout. **Balance semantics for non-cash families** (investment / property / vehicle): same `opening + cumulative txn.amount` formula as cash/credit, with an amber honesty banner — "Balance reflects recorded transactions; valuations not yet wired." — until the valuation pipeline arrives (ADR-032 / future ADR). No schema change. **Follow-ups** (most closed by ADR-034 in the same session): dual-axis combo chart [ADR-034]; section borders [ADR-034]; Top-N drill-down [ADR-034]; inflow Top-10; cleared-only balance variant; per-account sparkline in the sidebar; saved period preference per account; custom date range; reconciliation arc.

### ADR-034 — Per-account summary polish: dual-axis chart, section cards, Top-N drill-down
Polish round on ADR-033 after one session of real use. Three pieces in one ADR. **Dual y-axis on `BalanceFlowChart`** — independent left axis (bars) and right axis (balance line), each with its own `nice_ticks` scale; right-axis labels coloured blue-600 to match the line. Bars own the zero baseline; the line doesn't get its own. Forced-common-zero rejected because it breaks the always-positive-balance case (zero pins to the bottom, spending bars draw off the chart); runtime detection rejected because the owner asked for the fix unconditionally. **Section cards** around the four panels (chart, info, top-payees, top-categories) — `QFrame` with rounded 10px border, 1px slate-200 outline, white background on a slate-50 window canvas. Splitter handles widened to 12px so cards have a visible gutter. Drop shadows rejected (Qt repaint cost vs. visual gain). **Top-N drill-down** — new `mfl_desktop/ui/transactions_list_window.py` housing a non-modal `QMainWindow` with a breadcrumb chip strip (Account / Period / Category / Payee, each removable via its ×), the same six-preset period selector as the summary screen, and a `QTableView` reusing the existing `TransactionTableModel` + inline delegates (PayeeTypeaheadDelegate / CategoryTypeaheadDelegate / StatusDelegate). New `DrillDownFilterProxy` subclasses `TransactionFilterProxy` with `set_date_range` / `set_payee_id` / `set_category_descendant_ids` — the category filter is "this category and descendants" (uses `Repository.category_descendants` which already includes the seed id). New `TxnListFilter` frozen dataclass carries the spec; `for_payee` / `for_category` factory constructors keep call sites tight. **`TopNRow` gains an `entity_id` field** so the drill-down can filter against ids rather than labels; `_top_n_by_id` aggregates by id with a synthetic `None` bucket for missing payee_ids (rendered non-clickable until a "rows with NULL payee" filter lands). `_TopNList` becomes interactive — hover tints the row slate-100 and the cursor switches to pointing-hand on clickable rows; press emits `row_clicked(TopNRow)`. **Window policy**: one drill-down per distinct `(account_id, period_key, category_id, payee_id)` signature — clicking the same row twice raises the existing window, clicking a different row spawns a new one (owner picked this over replace-in-place via AskUserQuestion). Drill-downs parented to the summary so closing the summary closes them all. **Deferred follow-ups**: reusing `TransactionsListWindow` from other screens (Spending Report bar clicks, Net Worth account rows); drill-down for `(No payee)` / `(Uncategorised)` synthetic buckets; richer footer (inflow / outflow / net rather than just signed sum).

### ADR-035 — Multi-currency foundation
Bakes true multi-currency support into the data layer before the first USD account is imported. Migration 0009 adds three tables — `setting` (flat key/value: openexchangerates API key, last-refresh timestamp, matcher tunables, future prefs), `fx_rate(date, base, quote, rate, source)` (daily granularity; provider rows are USD-base per free-tier constraint; manual entries allowed in any direction), and `transfer(iri, from_account_id, to_account_id, rate, rate_source)` (parent row per pair; matches `txn.transfer_id` IRI; `rate_source` ∈ {derived, manual, fx_rate}). Existing same-currency pairs backfilled at rate=1.0. **`txn` does NOT gain a currency column** — a txn's currency is its account's currency, single source of truth; `account.currency` and `person.base_currency` already existed in 0001. **`Repository.get_fx_rate_nearest` six-step lookup**: exact bilateral → exact inverse → exact USD-pivot → nearest-prior bilateral → nearest-prior inverse → nearest-prior USD-pivot. Inverse step is critical — without it, asking for `GBP→USD` against a USD-base feed silently returns no rate. `convert_amount` is the single conversion path; same-currency early-exits. **Transfer plumbing is end-to-end currency-aware**: `create_transfer`, `convert_to_transfer`, `post_scheduled_txn` each take optional `to_amount` / `rate` / `rate_source` with a two-of-three resolution rule (supply any one and the others derive; supply none and FX-table is consulted with nearest-prior fallback). Destination row's stored amount is the receiving-side magnitude, not a converted echo of the source. `transfer.rate` records intent; the two txn amounts are the truth-of-money. **`mfl_desktop/fx.py`** is a no-Qt urllib client + `refresh_latest_into(repo, force=False)` (skips when last refresh <24h ago and when no non-USD accounts exist — single-currency users pay no API budget) + `backfill_historical()` for explicit ranges. **Background launch refresh** wired in `__main__.py` via `QThreadPool` with its own Repository connection. **Manage → Currencies… dialog** holds API key (with "stored in this file" disclaimer), Refresh Now, latest-rates table, Add manual rate row, and the ADR-036 matcher tunables (window-days default 3, FX tolerance default 1.0%). **Rejected**: per-txn currency column (deferred for the rare manual foreign-currency-on-domestic-card case), per-budget currency override (deferred), OS-keychain key storage (acceptable v1, follow-up ADR if real sharing becomes a thing). **Deferred follow-ups**: report display-currency selector + conversion (the headline reason for the arc); `backfill_historical` wired into the Currencies dialog with a cost-confirmation per the ADR's guard-rails; provider rotation hooks.

### ADR-036 — Transfer matching: link existing other-side row instead of always creating a partner
Replaces ADR-020's always-create-partner behaviour with a matcher that finds an unmatched candidate on the destination account first. Critical for the import-everything-then-categorise workflow — without matching, importing both sides of a transfer separately and then marking one as transfer creates a duplicate inflow on the destination. **`Repository.find_transfer_candidates`** filters by opposite-sign amount, `transfer_id IS NULL`, posted_date within ±`transfer_match_window_days` (default 3), and (for cross-currency) amount within `transfer_fx_tolerance_pct × 5` (default 1.0 × 5 = 5%) of `source_magnitude × spot_rate`. Returns scored candidates ranked best-first. **`Repository.link_transfer`** writes a fresh `transfer_id` IRI on both rows, **rewrites both rows' `category_id`** to the source's transfer category (the rewrite is the whole point — the user's mental model is "this inflow *is* the other half"), and inserts a `transfer` parent row with the rate back-derived from the two amounts. **`mfl_desktop/transfer_reconcile.py`** holds pure-Python `score_candidate` (weights: 100 base, −5×|days_apart|, −50×amount_mismatch_pct/100, −20 if currencies differ, +10 on payee-token overlap with a stopword filter that skips "transfer/from/to/payment/deposit"), `strength_for_score` bins (≥80 Strong, ≥60 Good, else Possible), and a generic `greedy_pair` helper used by ADR-037. **UI dialogs** in `mfl_desktop/ui/transfer_match_dialogs.py`: `TransferMatchConfirmDialog` (one candidate; [Match] / [Create new partner] / [Cancel]), `TransferMatchPickerDialog` (many candidates; ranked table with strength chips + trailing "Create new" sentinel row), and `BulkTransferReviewDialog` (per-row decision cell — fixed label for unambiguous rows, inline combo with top-score pre-selected for ambiguous ones). All wired into `register_window.py`: the inline category-edit flow routes through `_offer_transfer_match` before falling back to `convert_to_transfer`; the bulk-edit dispatcher does phase-1 field updates (category + payee/status/memo) then runs the matcher per row, opens the review dialog, and commits via `bulk_match_or_create_transfers` (single SQL transaction; mixed LinkExisting / CreateNew plan). Matcher errors fail soft — status-bar message + fallback to create-new, so a missing FX rate never blocks the flow. **Rejected**: auto-decide on one strong candidate (owner explicitly asked for confirmation — silent linking is too easy to get wrong); a Hungarian-algorithm optimal bipartite matcher in the reconcile path (greedy is good-enough for personal-finance shapes and ~30 lines of pure Python); per-account-override of the window/tolerance (acceptable v1; per-bank-settle-latency follow-up if real use surfaces it).

### ADR-042 — Inline register entry (quick-entry bar) — Parked
**Built, trialled, and reverted on 2026-06-08 on owner feedback** — a permanent fixed-bottom entry strip looked out of place, consumed permanent space, and didn't feel faster to type into. The implementation was removed (register back to modal/Ctrl+N entry); the ADR is kept as a record so a future attempt avoids the same shape (the ADR's parked-outcome note points at an in-grid append row or an on-demand inline row instead). Original (now-superseded) decision below: adds a docked **quick-entry bar** under the register so manual transactions can be typed in place instead of always through the New Transaction modal — closing the paired backlog items (inline add row + Cancel / Save / **Save and add another** verbs) and the older "visible New Transaction button" discoverability gap as a side effect. **Mechanism — a decoupled `QuickEntryBar` widget** (chosen over an in-grid model "draft row" and over a column-aligned scroll-synced strip). The bar is *not* part of `TransactionTableModel` or the proxy: it produces the same `NewTransactionValues` object the modal does and hands it back to the window, leaving the ADR-041 date-window, sort/filter proxy, selection, delete, and net-of-rows status line byte-for-byte untouched (zero regression surface on the most-recently-churned code), and Tab works natively between real widgets. The in-grid draft was rejected because draft-awareness would smear across `register_model` / `filter_proxy` / a dozen `register_window` call sites (sort-pin, filter-accept, window-exempt, id-skip on selection/net/delete) — many sharp edges for a convenience feature. **Scope — single-account view only** (the bar targets "this account"; the all-transactions view has no single target and mixes currencies, so it keeps the modal). **Fields & Tab order**: Date → Payee → Category → Status → Memo → Amount → Save and add another, with a **single signed Amount field** (ADR-038 sign-authoritative) replacing the modal's direction radios so Tab stays linear. Payee reuses the ADR-022 contains-match completer; Category reuses `make_category_picker` (existing categories only in v1 — inline-create-in-the-bar is a follow-up). **Verbs**: Save and add another (default / Enter — commit, reset, refocus Payee for the next entry), Save (commit, reset, focus back to the grid), Cancel (clear without committing). Validation is **non-blocking** — a missing/zero/unparseable amount or blank category shows a status-bar message and focuses the offending field, leaving the rest of the row intact. **Transfer-kind category mid-row** is resolved by refactoring `_on_new_transaction` to extract **`_commit_new_transaction(values)`**, shared by the modal and the bar, so a transfer category pops the same `TransferDestinationDialog` + `create_transfer` path (cross-currency partner amount included) — the bar uses the modal/create path, *not* the ADR-036 import matcher (that's for reconciling existing imported rows). **ADR-041 interaction**: a back-dated entry below the active window's lower bound commits fine but won't show; the bar surfaces a one-line "switch Show to All" hint. **No schema change, no migration** — reuses `insert_transaction` / `get_or_create_payee` / `create_transfer` / `commit`. Follow-ups: inline category-create in the bar, an optional in-grid draft row, an all-transactions bar with an account field, a memo-history completer, and a focus-the-bar shortcut.

### ADR-037 — Bulk transfer reconcile dialog
Manage → Reconcile Transfers… (Ctrl+Shift+R) for housekeeping after importing both sides of many transfer pairs separately. The headline multi-currency power feature: one screen that pairs `$1,000 USD on 12 Mar` with `£785 GBP on 13 Mar` via the day's spot rate. **`Repository.find_transfer_pairs(account_a, account_b)`** builds the cross-product of A's unmatched × B's unmatched, scores each potential pair using the shared `score_candidate` from `transfer_reconcile.py`, then runs `greedy_pair` (highest-score-first; each source/target claimed at most once; ties broken deterministically). Returns ranked `TransferPair` rows with `implied_rate` (back-derived from amounts), `spot_rate` (FX-table lookup with nearest-prior fallback), and `rate_deviation_pct` for the sanity-check display. **`mfl_desktop/ui/transfer_reconcile_dialog.py`**: two account combos at the top, read-only tunable summary line ("Window: ±3 days · FX tolerance: ±1.0% (change in Manage ▸ Currencies)"), checkbox table of proposed pairs with strength chip + side-by-side view (A date/amount/payee | B date/amount/payee), and cross-currency rows surface a payee-cell tooltip: "Implied 1.2739 · Spot 1.2700 · Δ +0.31%". Three shortcut buttons — Check all Strong / Check all Strong + Good / Uncheck all. Default: every Strong pair pre-checked so the common case is one click. Transfer-only category picker reusing `make_category_picker` filtered to `kind='transfer'`, defaulting to the seeded Transfer root. Apply writes via `bulk_match_or_create_transfers` (same atomic helper the bulk-edit path uses) then re-runs the search so matched rows drop from the list and the user can iterate. **Rejected**: N-account / wildcard mode in the B combo (additive follow-up; the two-accounts-at-a-time framing matches how users think about transfers between *these two specific accounts*); auto-rejection of pairs whose rate-deviation exceeds X% (informational only — the user might legitimately have taken a bad bureau-de-change rate; confidence binning is the right surface, hard rejection is the wrong one); per-pair category override (acceptable v1; small additive change later if real use surfaces it).

### ADR-043 — Investment accounts & QIF import (arc plan + round 1)
First round of the investment arc, and the QIF on-ramp. **Data model (owner-confirmed fork): extend `txn` with nullable investment columns** (`action / security_id / quantity REAL / price REAL / commission` pence) rather than a separate `investment_txn` table — one interleaved register per account (Buy/Sell/Div/Cash in one stream, as QIF/Banktivity/Quicken model it), `action IS NULL` ⇒ ordinary cash row so the entire cash path is untouched. New **`security`** master (migration 0012) referenced by name (the QIF `Y`; ticker `symbol` is often blank). **The crux is the action→cash-sign mapping**: `txn.amount` stays the *signed cash impact* so cash balance = `SUM(amount)` holds — Buy −T, Sell/Div/CGShort/CGLong +T, Cash signed-T as-is, ShrsIn/ShrsOut/ReinvDiv/StkSplit 0 (a reinvested dividend nets to zero), XIn/XOut ±T; `quantity` is the positive magnitude, action carries direction. New **`qif_parser.py`** (investment-focused, structured for `!Type:Bank`/`CCard` later) emits the same normalised dict the cash importers do plus the investment extras, so the import service reuses its sign/dedup/category machinery; dividends route to the system *Investment income* category by action. The import service gains investment-aware staging (richer dup-hash on action+security+quantity; skips the cash-only ±2-day manual-match), creates the securities master at commit, and threads the investment kwargs into `Repository.insert_transaction`. Register gains a `COLUMNS_INVEST` layout (Date/Action/Security/Qty/Price/Status/Memo/Amount/Balance), read-only security columns in R1, selected by `account.family == "investment"`; `*.qif` added to the import filter. **Round 1 = data in + visible + cash balance correct**; holdings/cost-basis (R2, `lot`), market value (R3, `valuation` — Net Worth understates an investment account to its cash until then), and transfer-linking (R4, reuse ADR-036 for the `L[Account]` cash rows) are deferred. **`!Type:Cat` parsed but not bulk-created**; `action` is free-text validated in Python (no CHECK) given QIF quirks. Verified end-to-end on the real E*Trade export: 957 transactions, 91 securities, cash balance $46,839.77 vs the file's stated $46,839.61 (16¢ sub-cent reinvestment-rounding residual), re-import dedups to zero.

---

### ADR-044 — Investment holdings (FIFO) + prices (Tiingo + manual) + market value
Round 2 of the investment arc: the holdings screen and prices. **FIFO cost basis** (owner's choice; US-style per-lot), **computed on the fly** from transactions in `mfl_desktop/holdings.py` (not persisted to `lot` — no second source of truth to sync; `lot` stays reserved for manual-basis/specific-ID needs). Share direction comes from action sets **extracted to `mfl_desktop/import_engine/qif_actions.py`** so the importer and holdings engine share one source of truth. **Prices: Tiingo** (free key, best fund coverage) via `mfl_desktop/prices.py` (urllib, Qt-free, mirrors `fx.py` — client + `refresh_latest_prices_into` + 24h throttle + background launch runnable in `__main__`), **plus mandatory manual entry** (56 of 91 securities carry no ticker). New `security_price` table (migration 0013, date-stamped like `fx_rate` so history is a round-3 add-on; **not** the account-level `valuation` table). **Market value** wired through a new `Repository.compute_account_values()` (investment = cash + Σ shares×latest price, fallback to cash when unpriced; every other family unchanged) which Net Worth + the sidebar now read — closing the ADR-019 follow-through; the register's cash ledger is untouched. New **Manage → Securities…** dialog (mirrors Currencies) and a **Holdings table** replacing the Top-Payees/Top-Categories row on an investment account's summary (Symbol/Security/Shares/Avg cost/Cost basis/Last price/Market value/Unrealised gain; `basis_incomplete` flagged for transferred-in/oversold/split rows). Edge cases flagged not faked: `ShrsIn` with no price (unknown basis), oversells (clamped at zero), stock-split ratios (deferred), whole-account `XIn`/`XOut` transfers (don't move lots — round 4). **Verified on live data:** 30 positions, $162k cost basis, lifetime FIFO realized gain $2,672 (Tesla round-trip = +$354.00, fully closed); a manual price flows straight through to market value, account value, and net worth. Current prices only this round; historical backfill + value-over-time is round 3.

### ADR-045 — Investment dashboard (tabs + value chart; analytics tabs)
Reworks the cramped, cash-shaped investment summary into a dashboard. **Phase 1 (shipped):** for investment accounts the per-account summary becomes a `QTabWidget` (first tabs in the main UI) — **Overview** (a new value chart + the info card) and **Holdings** (full-width table + a live search box). Cash accounts keep the ADR-033/034 single page (factored out as `_build_cash_layout`); `reload()` branches into `_reload_investment` / `_reload_cash` so the investment path never touches the cash-only chart/report/period/Top-N widgets. New `value_chart.py` paintEvent widget: one two-tone bar per security — base = cost basis (blue), tip = **green gain** (value ≥ cost) or **red loss** (value < cost), full height = max(cost, value); unpriced = a cost-only bar; currency-aware hover. Selectable via a **Securities…** picker (reuses the ADR-039 `CheckListPanel`) and a **Portfolio total** toggle (one aggregate bar). Models `spending_chart`'s segment-paint + hover and reuses `chart_helpers`. **Phase 2 (planned):** Returns tab (appreciation + dividends + realised, via a new `compute_returns()` in `holdings.py`), Dividends tab (income-over-time + per-security), Allocation tab (**treemap** by market value — owner floated a pie, but a treemap scales to ~30 holdings without slivers and keeps the ADR-018 no-pie rule intact). No historical prices needed (snapshot chart + recorded-date dividend timeline); value-over-time stays the round-3 item. Verified on live data: gain/loss/unpriced bar mapping correct, portfolio-total aggregates over the priced subset.

**Amendment (2026-06-09):** the Overview top-left chart was corrected from the cost-vs-value *snapshot* to **portfolio valuation over time** (the owner's intent). The snapshot bars moved to a new **Positions** tab; the Overview hosts a new `value_history_chart.py` (two lines — **Invested** cost basis + **Market value** — with a green/red fill between). This pulled **historical prices** forward from round 3: `TiingoClient.fetch_historical` + `backfill_historical_into` (one call per ticker → `security_price`), `Repository.price_series`/`get_security_price_nearest`/`bulk_upsert_security_prices`, and `holdings.compute_value_history` (FIFO replay snapshotting cost basis + market value at month-ends; cost fallback when a holding is unpriced on a date → `fully_priced=False`). A **Backfill history** button in Manage ▸ Securities populates it. The **Portfolio** tab (renamed from Positions) defaults to an **allocation treemap** (`treemap_chart.py`, squarified, sized by market value with cost-basis fallback) with a view switch to the cost-vs-value bars — the treemap was pulled forward from Phase 2 to be the default portfolio view. Tabs now **Overview / Holdings / Portfolio**. Verified: Invested line equals FIFO cost-basis snapshots; backfill→series→nearest→value-history chain works; squarify tiles the box proportionally; all current holdings tickered. **Still Phase 2:** Returns + Dividends tabs, and a value-chart period-zoom selector.

### ADR-050 — Cross-platform as a first-class goal (macOS + Windows)
Retires ADR-008's "Windows-first" framing: development is back on macOS and both OSes are now equal, supported, *maintained* targets. A 2026-06-10 porting audit of `mfl_desktop/` found the app already almost entirely platform-clean (zero `sys.platform` branches, all-`pathlib` paths, no OS-shell coupling, `%-d`-free dates, Fusion style) — it `pip install`s and launches on macOS with **no code change**. The risk this ADR addresses is *regression*, so it fixes a binding **rule set** (also copied into `CLAUDE_CONTEXT.md`'s carry-forward pitfalls so it's seen every session): (1) always `pathlib.Path`; (2) user data via `QStandardPaths.AppDataLocation`, never cwd — chosen over ADR-004's `platformdirs` since Qt is already a dep; (3) shortcuts via `QKeySequence.StandardKey`, else a per-OS modifier helper (a literal `"Ctrl+N"` does **not** become ⌘ on Mac — only `StandardKey` does); (4) menu roles on About/Preferences/Quit; (5) cross-platform system font leads the cascade (`-apple-system` before `"Segoe UI"`); (6) Fusion + QPalette only (no native style); (7) no `os.startfile`/`subprocess`/`QProcess` — use `QDesktopServices.openUrl`; (8) no `%-d` date directives; (9) no OS branches in feature code (only in isolated shims); (10) LF line endings. **Release path**: build on each OS (PyInstaller can't cross-compile) → `.app`/`.dmg` + `.exe`, ideally a GitHub Actions `macos-latest`+`windows-latest` matrix; **macOS code-signing + notarization** (Apple Developer Program, $99/yr) is the one big *operational* piece, required so non-technical friends don't hit the Gatekeeper wall. **Work items** the audit surfaced (none blocks running on Mac): convert the 9 hardcoded `Ctrl+` shortcuts; fix the `Ctrl+I` collision (Import vs Account Summary); reorder the font cascade; move the default DB off cwd (`__main__.py:85`) onto `QStandardPaths` alongside the ADR-016 save/auto-save amendment; packaging is its own later round. Amends ADR-003 / ADR-004 / ADR-008.

### ADR-051 — Split transactions
Makes split transactions first-class — one payee/date/total divided across several categories (each with its own memo and a **signed** amount, so a −120 groceries line + a +20 cashback line net to −100). Until now the Banktivity CSV importer flattened splits into the memo and filed them under Uncategorised, mis-attributing them in every report/budget. **Key decision: a new `txn_split` child table holds the lines while the parent `txn` keeps the full signed total**, so the entire money layer (balance, `balance_as_of`, `statement_residual`, holdings, net worth, running balance, dedup hash) is **untouched** — only *category attribution* unrolls. Child-`txn` rows and JSON-on-txn were rejected (they'd force every `SUM(amount)` query to de-dup, or aren't queryable). A single SQL **view `txn_category_line`** (non-split txns map to themselves; splits explode into one row per line) serves the two SQL category consumers with a one-line `FROM` swap (`spending_aggregates`, `list_perimeter_txns` — its transfer-cancellation subquery stays on base `txn`); the per-account Top-Categories screen unrolls in memory via `split_lines_for_txns`. Migration 0017 adds the table (FK mirrors `txn.category_id` — `NOT NULL`, no `ON DELETE`; the category delete/merge path repoints split lines to the sink) + the view; the invariant `Σ lines == parent total` is asserted on every write (integer pence, exact). In the register a split shows as **one row reading "—Split—"** and is **fully dialog-edited** (non-editable inline, like investment rows); double-click opens the new **`SplitTransactionDialog`** (header + a category/memo/signed-amount line table + a live "Unassigned" gate that must hit 0; transfer-kind categories excluded — split ⊥ transfer in v1). A **"Split…"** button on New Transaction routes the header+amount into the same dialog; **Bulk Edit** prompts before converting split parents to a single category. Import: the parser→service dict gains an optional `splits` key (Banktivity-only); `_collapse_banktivity_splits` now emits structured lines instead of memo text, **auto-balancing** with an Uncategorised remainder line when the source doesn't sum (never rejects, no float tolerance); the dedup hash stays parent-level. **Scope (v1): cash/bank/credit only** (investment rows keep the ADR-048 dialog); QIF split import (`S`/`E`/`$` in bank sections) is a deferred extension of the same `splits` contract. **Verified headless on a copy of the live DB:** split insert holds the invariant and surfaces `split_count`; converting plain↔split leaves balances and statement residual byte-identical; spending unrolls to line categories; a Banktivity split block imports as parent + lines, an unbalanced block gets a remainder line, and re-import dedups to zero. (Qt-runtime smoke of the model flags/dialog awaits the project venv — PySide6 isn't installed on the dev Mac yet.)

### ADR-052 — Merge securities
Fills the long-standing "merge-securities verb is still unbuilt" gap (open since ADR-044). Because `security.name` is `UNIQUE` and the importer keys on it, a renamed fund lands as **two records sharing one ticker** — the owner's TSBIX split into "Nuveen Core Impact Bond R6" (id 47, ticker, 219 Tiingo prices, 23 txns) and "TIAA CREF CORE IMPACT BD INST" (id 65, 131 txns, 59 transaction prices), so holdings and the Returns report saw two half-positions. New `Repository.merge_securities(source_ids, target_id)` mirrors `merge_payees`/`merge_categories`: re-point `txn.security_id` to the survivor, move `security_price` rows via an `INSERT…SELECT … ON CONFLICT` whose guard keeps the higher-precedence price on a shared date (the ADR-047 rule, rank-based: manual=3 > tiingo=2 > transaction=1, ties keep the survivor), delete the source rows, all in one transaction; then `seed_prices_from_transactions([target])` so a trade moved onto an untickered survivor still seeds a price. **Only two tables reference a security** (`txn.security_id` SET NULL, `security_price.security_id` CASCADE; `lot` keys on `symbol`), so **no migration** — pure data + UI. UI: a **"Merge…"** button on the Stock Record opens `merge_securities_dialog.py`, which lists every other security (same-ticker matches surfaced first + pre-selected), shows a side-by-side comparison (ticker / #txns / #prices / latest price) and a **survivor radio defaulting to the better-data record** (real ticker, then more real prices, then more txns — owner picked this default over "keep the one I opened" via AskUserQuestion), with a live "N transactions and M prices move to «survivor»; «other» is deleted — can't be undone" line. The Stock Record closes if the record in view was absorbed, else reloads. **Known limitation:** a saved Investment Returns report filtered on the absorbed security keeps a stale id (matches nothing) — re-pick after merging. **Verified** on a WAL-consistent snapshot of the live DB (merging 65→47 moved 131 txns to 154 total, deleted the source, zero dangling refs, preserved the price-date union, dropped the one transaction price colliding with a Tiingo date, no PK collisions) + an offscreen Qt smoke (PySide6 6.11.1) of the pre-selection, default survivor, comparison grid, flip behaviour, and wired button.

### ADR-053 — In-kind share transfers (ShrsIn / ShrsOut) are not sales
Fixes a phantom realized loss: the owner moved a position Morgan Stanley → E\*Trade as an in-kind transfer (`ShrsOut` from one account, `ShrsIn` into the other, $0 cash), and the Returns report showed TSBIX with a **−$52,865 realized loss** that never happened. Cause: `shrsout` sat in `SHARE_OUT_ACTIONS` with `sell`, so it was booked as a disposal with $0 proceeds (`realized = 0 − full cost basis`), while the matching `ShrsIn` re-added the shares at zero basis. Fix: a new `SHARE_TRANSFER_ACTIONS`/`is_share_transfer` (in `qif_actions.py`) marks ShrsIn/ShrsOut as custodian moves; `holdings.py` (all three engines — `compute_holdings_view`, `compute_returns`, `compute_value_history`) now removes shares on a `ShrsOut` with **zero realized gain** and parks the popped FIFO lots in a per-security **transfer pen**, from which the matching `ShrsIn` pulls its **carried cost basis** — so a clean out→in transfer nets to no realized impact and preserves basis. The Returns report (`investment_returns_window.py`) now groups selected accounts **by currency** and runs one replay per currency group (was per-account), so a transfer between two same-currency *accounts* nets (both legs in one replay); conversion is unaffected since a rate depends only on the currency. **Depends on ADR-052:** the funds were renamed on the move, so each transfer's two legs were recorded under two `security` records (e.g. "CRA Qualified Investment" → CRANX; two EMNT records; KLD 400 → DSI) — those must be **merged** first for the pen to match cross-record legs. Options rejected: leaving ShrsOut as a sale (the bug — −$265k of phantom portfolio losses); skipping ShrsIn/ShrsOut like XIn/XOut (positions would be wrong — these carry real share quantities); full persisted cross-currency transfer-linking (round-4, deferred — the pen is the lightweight same-currency form). **Verified** on the live DB: TSBIX total return unchanged at **$19,865.56** but realized **−$52,865 → +$11,593** / unrealized **−$64,492 → +$33** (total-return invariance proves the change is conservative); EMNT held cost **$2,109 → $59,474** and CRANX **$1,630 → $51,532** once their pairs are merged; non-transfer securities are byte-identical (code path unchanged when `is_share_transfer` is False); the Stock Record was already correct (single cross-account replay).

### ADR-054 — Stock splits adjust the FIFO lots
Closes the ADR-044 deferral of stock splits, prompted by **HDV's 5-for-1 split**: Tiingo stores real prices (~$140 pre-split → ~$27 post-split), but the engine never scaled the share count, so it valued 214.779 pre-split shares at the $27.54 post-split price → a bogus −72.7% "loss" (and corrupted the Stock Record, the Returns Unrealized column, and the value chart). The split had been recorded not as a `StkSplit` but as an **`XIn` of 859.116 shares @ $0** (= 214.779 × 4, the extra shares of a 5:1), which the engine ignores. Decision: model a split as a **`StkSplit` action whose `quantity` is the ratio** (new shares per old — 5 for 5:1, 0.1 for a reverse 1:10); a shared `_apply_split` scales every open FIFO lot (`qty ×ratio`, `unit_cost ÷ratio`, **total basis unchanged**) in all three engines (`compute_holdings_view`, `compute_returns`, `compute_value_history`), so market value stays continuous (shares step up as price steps down) with **no price rewrite**. The investment dialog (ADR-048) gains a "Stock split" action with a single "Split ratio" field (hides qty/price/amount, keeps security; seeds the ratio in edit mode). Rejected: rewriting stored prices to be split-adjusted (fights the Tiingo feed); auto-detecting `XIn @ $0` as a split (XIn is a legit transfer). The owner's HDV row is converted by editing it (Action → Stock split, ratio 5). **Verified** on the live DB: HDV 214.779 → **1,073.895 shares**, cost unchanged **$21,655**, avg **$20.17**, market value **$29,575**, unrealized **−$15,740 → +$7,920**; offscreen Qt confirmed the dialog's split mode, save (`StkSplit`/qty=ratio/price=NULL/amount=0), and edit-mode ratio seeding.

### ADR-055 — Net Worth converts to a display currency
Fixes a materially wrong headline: with 7 GBP + 7 USD accounts and (at the time) 0 fx rates, `NetWorthWindow` summed `compute_account_values()` (which returns each account's value in its *own* currency) as bare pence and labelled it "£", so the ~$300k USD brokerage was added to GBP **at par**. The ADR-035 FX layer (`convert_amount`, `get_fx_rate_nearest`, manual-rate entry in the Currencies dialog) already existed but was never plumbed in. Fix: a **display-currency selector** (default = `get_setting("base_currency")`, else GBP, else first in use); `_convert_all` converts every account to the display currency via `convert_amount(on_date=today)` before any total is summed; per-type/family/Assets/Debts/net totals all use the converted values; per-account leaves show converted with the **native amount in the tooltip**. **Missing-rate policy differs from ADR-046's `_conv`:** a 1:1 fallback *is* the bug here, so an unconvertable account is **excluded** from the totals and surfaced in a banner ("8 USD accounts ($1,791,172.60) excluded — no rate to GBP") with a **"Set exchange rate…"** button opening the Currencies dialog. Rejected: 1:1+warn (re-introduces par-add behind a warning); block until rates set (single-currency users still want their number); auto-fetch on open (needs key + network — offered via the button instead). **Sidebar folder roll-up has the same class of bug** but degrades to no-symbol on mixed folders — left as a scoped follow-up. **Verified** on the live DB: 0 rates → correct GBP-only total + USD excluded with the dollar sum in the banner; after a manual USD→GBP rate the brokerage folds in at the converted value (assets £2,561,848 = GBP £1,146,822 + USD $1,791,172×0.79) and the banner clears; the display-currency switch re-denominates the whole report.

### ADR-082 — Date & period standardisation: one period vocabulary, one date-edit factory
First engineering bite of the 1.0 launch plan's **P1**. A polish audit found date/period handling fragmented: **3+ preset vocabularies** (register `30d/90d/6m/12m/ytd/all`; reports `quarter/6m/ytd/1y/3y/custom`; investment `ytd/1y/3y/5y/max/custom`; Sankey `ytd/mtd/last_month/custom`), **period-bounds maths duplicated in four places** (`account_summary.period_bounds`, the register's `_current_since`+`_months_before`, and inline `_resolve_bounds` in the Sankey + Investment-Returns windows), **the `_PERIOD_LABELS` dict copy-pasted into ~10 files**, and a **latent bug** — the register computed `6m`/`12m` calendar-accurately (`_months_before`, same day-of-month) while `account_summary.period_bounds` used day-deltas (`180`/`365`), so `"6m"` silently meant two different windows depending on the screen. Plus two date display formats across ~14 `QDateEdit` sites (ISO on entry forms, `d MMM yyyy` on a couple of human dialogs, and `schedule_dialog` with no calendar popup). Since the preset keys are **persisted in saved-report `filters_json`**, consolidation had to keep them byte-stable. **Decision:** a new Qt-free **`mfl_desktop/periods.py`** becomes the single source of truth — one `PERIOD_LABELS` registry, the per-context preset SETS (`REGISTER_PRESETS`/`REPORT_PRESETS`/`INVESTMENT_PRESETS`/`SANKEY_PRESETS`, keys unchanged), one `period_bounds(key, today, *, earliest=, custom_start=, custom_end=)` covering every key (`None` start only for unbounded `all`/`max`; raises on `custom` without dates), plus `months_before`/`period_since`/`fmt_date_range`/`period_label`/`labels_for`/`options_for` — and a Qt **`ui/date_widgets.py`** with `make_date_edit(...)` (calendar popup + the one user-facing `d MMM yyyy` format, decision P1a) and `make_period_combo(keys, current=)`. Consumers delegate: `account_summary` + `reports/filters` **re-export** the vocabulary under their historical names so the ~12 importer files keep working unchanged and persisted keys round-trip; the register drops `_months_before`/its preset list/`_current_since` body; the Sankey + Investment windows drop their inline `_resolve_bounds` (custom/`max` edge-handling preserved); all ten duplicated `_PERIOD_LABELS` dicts are removed (the eight report-shape consumers reuse `account_summary.PERIOD_LABELS`, the two investment ones use the full `periods.PERIOD_LABELS`; Sankey's inline combo *options list* with its deliberate `Custom…` ellipsis is left, being a display list not the duplicated dict). **Deliberate semantic alignment:** month/year windows are now calendar-accurate everywhere (the report `6m`/`1y`/`3y` + investment `5y` shift 0–3 days off the old day-deltas, landing on the same day-of-month) — kills the `"6m"`-means-two-things bug; day windows (`30d`/`90d`/`quarter`) stay rolling-by-days. Rejected: one preset set everywhere (the sets legitimately differ — `All`/`5y`/`max`/`mtd` belong to different screens — and it would break persisted keys); hand-syncing the duplication (that drift *was* the bug). **Verified:** `periods.py` unit tests (every key's bounds, the 31 Mar→Feb day-clamp, custom/all/max edges, `period_since`); compute-layer delegation parity + saved-filter round-trip; whole-app import; offscreen construction of the spending + investment filter dialogs (period combos build, `5y`/`max` resolve from the shared registry) and the register preset/since logic. **Follow-up "P1 part B":** roll `make_date_edit` across the ~14 `QDateEdit` sites (incl. the no-popup `schedule_dialog`) to finish the one-date-format half, and adopt `make_period_combo` in the filter dialogs to retire the last label references.

### ADR-080 — Enable Banking production activation & application-key custody (planning; deferred)
Frames decision **F1a** of the 1.0 launch plan without locking it. ADR-077 shipped the Qt-free BYO provider cores (incl. Enable Banking, the free UK/EU Open Banking feed); **automated feeds are a 1.1 fast-follow, so nothing here blocks 1.0.** The path to **production** does need framing: Enable Banking "full activation" requires a contract, **KYC**, a billing account, an end-user-visible app description, a data-protection email, and **privacy-policy + ToS URLs** — none of which exist until workstreams B (company/legal) and W (website) land (and those URLs are launch deliverables anyway, so they double-count). The load-bearing open question: **who holds the EB application registration + private key (`.pem`)?** Options: **BYO** — each user registers their own EB app and supplies the key (what the cores assume; max privacy, MFL is a local tool and **not** a data controller / regulated entity, lightest compliance; cost = one-time setup friction); **MFL-hosted shared registration** — one registration, click-to-connect UX, but MFL becomes data-controller / TPP-adjacent with heavier UK/EU GDPR + KYC + PSD2 obligations and server-side key custody, likely **reopening subscription** (ADR-079's escape hatch); or a **hybrid** (BYO default + optional hosted convenience later). **Decision: defer the custody choice to after the B3 compliance read; ship 1.0 with the BYO cores unchanged.** Constraints that hold either way: the key **never** lives in the binary or the `.mfl` (BYO → OS keychain, the F2 backlog item; hosted → server custody with its own review); EB **consents expire ≈90 days** → a re-consent flow is required (F2); **activation path = Restricted mode first** (whitelist the owner's own accounts so the full consent→fetch→`stage_feed`→review→commit round-trip is owner-tested before any manual review) **→ then Unrestricted** (EB manual review + KYC + contract + billing), gated on B1/B2/B3; the non-sandboxed distribution choice (ADR-078) keeps local custody viable. Trigger to make the call (and write it up as an ADR-080 amendment): **B1 (entity) + B2 (privacy/ToS live) + B3 (PSD2/AISP role determination) done** — i.e. once we actually know whether the hosted model carries regulated-entity obligations we'd take on. Until then, **don't architect against either option** — keep the cores BYO-compatible and credential-source-agnostic. Consequences: 1.0 unblocked; the activation path de-risked by Restricted mode; the F2 work (keychain + re-consent) is correct under either future, so not wasted. Trade-offs: BYO setup friction persists for 1.1; the decision is genuinely blocked on **legal** input, not engineering; a later hosted choice cascades into data-controller status + subscription.

### ADR-079 — Licensing & pricing: one-time perpetual, everything included, offline key
Locks decision **C1** of the launch plan. The decisive fact: MFL is **local-first with BYO feed credentials (ADR-077) — no ongoing server or per-user cost to amortise** (the app only talks to third-party APIs the *user* holds keys for), which removes the usual justification for a subscription. **Pricing: a single one-time perpetual purchase (~£25–45 / $30–50), everything unlocked** — all feed providers (incl. SimpleFIN/Plaid), all reports, investments, multi-currency — with **2.0 as a new paid upgrade** (1.x keys keep working on 1.x forever). This supersedes the earlier "willing-to-pay unlocks SimpleFIN/Plaid" framing: all providers are in the box; the user still supplies their own provider key/cost under BYO. **Enforcement = an offline signed license key, no activation server:** the app ships a public key, a purchased license is a token **signed by our private key** (held by the MoR / fulfilment) and validated entirely on-device — fits local-first + privacy, needs no backend; the key encodes buyer name/email + an **edition/version entitlement** so a 2.0 upgrade is a new key. New **Qt-free `licensing.py`** (verify-only, never holds the private key) + an Enter-License/Buy flow + About-box state; a time-limited **full-feature trial** unlocked by a key. **Payments via a Merchant-of-Record** (Paddle / Lemon Squeezy / FastSpring), not bare Stripe — the MoR is the seller of record and handles **UK/EU VAT + US sales tax + invoicing + key delivery**, the single biggest tax-compliance relief for a solo founder (cross-ref ADR-078: direct distribution means we'd otherwise owe cross-border tax). **Stores (1.1+):** store policy may mandate the store's IAP for digital unlocks (15–30% cut, no out-linking) — the license *model* is unchanged, a store purchase grants the **same entitlement**; reconciled when K3 starts. Rejected: **tiered unlock** (base + paid "Plus" for premium providers — with no marginal cost per provider there's nothing to meter, and it tangles with store IAP); **subscription** (churn-prone with no recurring cost — *only* defensible if MFL ever takes on hosted infra per ADR-080's hosted model, kept as an explicit escape hatch). Trade-offs: offline keys are crackable (accepted — honest non-technical audience; gentle friction, not DRM fortress; online activation can be added if piracy bites); no recurring revenue (fine — no recurring cost); version-entitlement bookkeeping; the MoR takes ~5%+. Ongoing: protect the signing private key; set the 2.0 upgrade price when 2.0 is real; keep the entitlement check store-agnostic.

### ADR-078 — Packaging & distribution: direct signed + notarised downloads first; App Stores deferred
Locks decision **K0** of the launch plan, **closes ADR-050 Tier-3** (packaging — "its own round; own ADR when started"), and **amends ADR-003** (settles the deferred PyInstaller-vs-Briefcase tool choice + "signing TBD"). The owner's "notarised … so it's seen as legit and safe" conflates two separable things: **trust** (a Developer-ID-signed + **notarised** `.app`/DMG passes Gatekeeper; a **code-signed** Windows installer seasons SmartScreen — **neither needs an App Store**) versus **store presence** (badge + auto-update + store-handled payment/tax, at the cost of review, a 15–30% cut, and — on the Mac App Store — **sandboxing**). The sandbox is **fundamentally at odds with MFL's file model** — arbitrary `.mfl` files anywhere (ADR-016), `Snapshots/`+`Library/` written *beside* the live file (ADR-057), the AppData default + cwd bridge (ADR-050 Tier-2) — without security-scoped bookmarks for every user file and relocating the sidecars into the container, a substantial rework. **Decision: ship 1.0 as direct, signed, notarised downloads from our own website; defer both App Stores to 1.1/1.2 as a separate channel** — removing the sandbox work from the 1.0 critical path (the biggest scope lever in the plan). **Toolchain: PyInstaller per-OS** (consistent with ADR-003/MRL; Briefcase considered for its built-in dmg+sign+notarise automation but rejected to keep one toolchain we already run, wiring signing in ourselves); **macOS universal2** (Apple Silicon + Intel) `.app` → `codesign` → `notarytool` → staple → signed DMG, **Sparkle** appcast auto-update; **Windows x64** signed installer (Inno Setup) or signed **MSIX**, **WinSparkle**/App-Installer update feed; Apple Developer Program **$99/yr**, Windows cert **~$200–400/yr** (or Azure Trusted Signing), **hardened runtime** with minimum entitlements (outbound network for FX/prices/feeds + user-selected file access, **no `app-sandbox`**); a reverse-DNS bundle id added to the existing ADR-050 `setApplicationName("MFL")`. Linux/AppImage (from ADR-003) stays possible but is **out of 1.0 scope**. Stores deferred with the rework documented (sandbox entitlements, security-scoped bookmarks, relocate sidecars, store IAP grants the same ADR-079 entitlement). Rejected: **stores day-one** (puts sandbox rework on the launch critical path + concedes the cut before the product proves it sells); **both in parallel** (pays the direct-signing *and* sandbox costs at once for no launch benefit). Consequences: full trust without store gatekeeping, zero sandbox rework, file model retained, one build toolchain. Trade-offs: we run our own signing/notarisation/update infra; Windows cert cost + SmartScreen seasoning lag for a new publisher; no store auto-discovery (distribution leans on the website); we handle payment/tax → the ADR-079 Merchant-of-Record. Ongoing: renew certs, notarise every macOS release, keep update feeds current, hold the ADR-050 portability line, and keep new file-access code sandbox-aware so the future store port isn't made harder.

### ADR-081 — MFL → MRL data exchange: file-based RDF export over the shared ontology
Closes the MRL-integration gap in the 1.0 launch plan (workstream M). MFL (SQLite ledger) and **My Retirement Life** (RDF/Oxigraph retirement + tax projection) are sold as a bundle and must interoperate. ADR-009 already retired the "shared database" idea (ADR-001) for a **data-exchange boundary**, and ADR-006 kept MFL's accounts/person on **`mrl:`-namespaced IRIs** precisely so this would be cheap. Owner decisions (2026-06-16, `AskUserQuestion`): integration is a **1.1 fast-follow**, direction **MFL → MRL**, mechanism **file-based RDF export**, commercial relationship **bundle**. Division of labour: **MFL = financial reality today; MRL = projects it forward** (growth/drawdown/retirement/tax assumptions). The MRL ontology already models the entities MFL owns the data for (`mrl:Account`/`CashAccount`/`InvestmentAccount`/`CreditCardAccount`/`PropertyAsset`, `mrl:Person`, `mrl:IncomeSource`, `mrl:Currency`) and even annotates `mrl:PropertyAsset` *"Activated in v1.0.1 for use by My Finance Life."* **Decision:** a user-initiated, one-way, **point-in-time** Turtle snapshot of **balances + entities, not the transaction ledger** (MRL projects from current balances, not 35k rows). Mapping: `mrl:Person_1` → firstName/lastName/baseCurrency; each account → its stored IRI **verbatim** with `accountName`/`accountBalance` (from `compute_account_balances`/`compute_account_values`)/`balanceDate`/`accountCurrency`→`mrl:Currency_<CODE>`/`isLiability`/`creditLimit`/`accountType`→skos concept/`ownedBy`→`mrl:Person_1`/`exchangeRateToBase`+`Date` (ADR-055 nearest rate, only when account ccy ≠ base). **IRI-class vs rdf:type:** MFL mints `mrl:SavingsAccount_N`/`PropertyAccount_N`/`VehicleAccount_N`, which have **no MRL class** — the IRI is opaque so it's emitted verbatim while `rdf:type` is set to the real MRL subclass (`CashAccount`/`PropertyAsset`/`OtherAsset`). **The authority contract** (the crux of the two-app boundary): MFL is authoritative for, and MRL overwrites on merge, exactly the predicates above; MFL **never emits** the MRL-owned assumptions (`annualGrowthRate`/`annualInterestRate`/`annualDividendRate`/`reinvestDividends`/`drawdownPriority`/`statementDay`/`dateOfBirth`/`targetRetirementAge`/`lifeExpectancy`/`employmentStatus`/`residesIn`/`plansToRetireIn`/`accountJurisdiction`), so a re-import never clobbers the user's MRL inputs. **Mechanism:** Qt-free `mfl_desktop/export/mrl_rdf.py` (`build_mrl_turtle(repo, as_of) -> str`, pure/headless-testable like `fx.py`), a `File ▸ Export for My Retirement Life…` verb, and a CLI `export-mrl`; a **hand-rolled stdlib Turtle writer** (no new runtime dependency, consistent with the post-ADR-009 RDF-free stance) validated in CI by parsing with `rdflib` (test-only) + an Oxigraph round-trip — ⚠ open sub-decision to ship `rdflib` at runtime instead if escaping/prefixes prove fiddly. The `mrl-ontology.ttl` version is a **pinned contract** (ADR-005: never edited from MFL); shared-ontology changes are coordinated. **Phase 1** (the M2 deliverable): person + currencies + accounts. **Phase 2:** `mrl:IncomeSource` derived from `scheduled_txn` income rows (annualised), property metadata, jurisdiction. Rejected: shared DB / live read of MRL's Oxigraph (storage coupling, must locate the store, fragile, breaks under the 1.2 App-Store sandbox), JSON/CSV (discards the shared ontology + aligned IRIs that make this nearly free; MRL is RDF-native). Consequences: cashes in ADR-006 (1:1 account mapping, no matching heuristics), no new shipped dependency, decoupled/one-way/privacy-clean (a user-produced file, easy to disclose in the privacy policy), survives the future sandbox. Trade-offs: one-way + snapshot-only (no projections back into MFL → later M3; no balance history); the merge/authority split must be honoured on the MRL side (recorded here as a joint contract + round-trip-tested); shared-ontology version coupling; IncomeSource/jurisdiction deferred. **ADR-006's IRI-namespace discipline is now load-bearing for interop**, reinforcing pitfall #3. Status **Proposed** — to be Accepted when M2 implementation begins.

### ADR-077 — Bank feeds (Arc H): pluggable providers, GoCardless first
The last arc, and the owner's make-or-break feature: pull transactions automatically instead of exporting + importing files. There is **no free, universal, private bank-feed API**, and the owner's accounts span **UK** (HSBC, Smile, YBS, Capital One UK…) *and* **US** (Ally, Chase, Discover, eTrade, Morgan Stanley…), which no single free mechanism covers — OFX Direct Connect (free/local, US-leaning), GoCardless Open Banking (free, UK/EU only), SimpleFIN (cheap, US), Plaid/TrueLayer (broad but paid). Two constraints follow: a freely-shared app **can't bear central per-user cost**, so each user supplies their own credentials → a **pluggable provider framework**; and a feed only needs to *produce transactions*, so it **reuses the entire existing import pipeline** (staging, FITID/hash dedup, the manual-match heuristic, the review dialog, commit). Owner decisions (`AskUserQuestion`): **GoCardless first** (free, covers their UK banks), and a **manual "Update accounts"** refresh (downloaded transactions land in the existing review/dedup before commit), with background/scheduled refresh deferred. Round 1 (this commit) is the headlessly-testable foundation: `mfl_desktop/feeds/` (Qt-free, stdlib `urllib`, no new dependency) with `gocardless.py` — base `https://bankaccountdata.gocardless.com/api/v2`, `POST /token/new/` (secret_id+secret_key → 24h access), `GET /institutions/?country=GB`, `POST /requisitions/` (hosted bank-consent `link`), poll `GET /requisitions/{id}/` for `status == "LN"` + account ids, then `/accounts/{id}/transactions|balances|details/`; the desktop has no web server so consent opens in the system browser and completion is detected by **polling** (the redirect is a harmless localhost URL — no firewall-prompting local server). `normalize.py` maps a GoCardless booked transaction to the parser raw-txn dict (`bookingDate`→date, abs `transactionAmount`→amount with sign→tx_type, creditor/debtor/remittance→payee, `transactionId`→`fitid`); pending rows are skipped in v1 (they mutate and would churn the dedup). **Migration 0026** adds `feed_account` (MFL account ↔ provider account, one feed per account, `ON DELETE CASCADE`; `UNIQUE(provider, external_account_id)`); the GoCardless `secret_id`/`secret_key` persist in the `setting` table (ADR-035, "stored inside this file" disclaimer) and the short-lived access token is kept in memory only. `Repository` gains a `FeedAccount` dataclass + `link/get/list/unlink/mark_synced/set_status` (link upserts on the account); `ImportService.stage_feed(account_iri, raw_txns)` runs feed rows through `_classify_and_stage` so dedup (`fitid`→`import_hash`) makes a re-fetch of the overlapping window idempotent. A `cli.py feeds-check --secret-id … --secret-key …` probe lists the user's bank institutions so connectivity (the make-or-break) can be proven before any UI is built. Rejected: Plaid/TrueLayer (central per-connection billing can't be sustained for a freely-shared app), catching the OAuth redirect with a bundled local web server (polling is simpler, no firewall prompt), auto-committing fetched transactions (they go through the same human review as file imports), persisting access/refresh tokens (re-minted per session from the secret). **Verified** offscreen (no live network): the normalizer maps booked/pending correctly and drops malformed rows; the GoCardless client mints the token first without auth, sends `Authorization: Bearer` on subsequent calls, builds the requisition body correctly, parses status/accounts/transactions, and turns an HTTP 401 into a `GoCardlessError`; `feed_account` CRUD round-trips, upserts on re-link, and cascades when its account is deleted; and `stage_feed`→`commit_import` imports 2 rows then dedups a re-fetch to 0 imported / 2 skipped (idempotent). Live bank connectivity is verified by the owner against their own GoCardless secret. **Deferred:** the Manage ▸ Bank Feeds UI — connect a bank (browser consent + poll), link provider accounts ↔ MFL accounts, **Update accounts** → review → commit, balances + last-synced (H2); re-consent on ≈90-day expiry, error/empty states, scheduled/background refresh, and a US provider (OFX Direct Connect / SimpleFIN) (H3).

### ADR-076 — Design tokens + light/dark theming (Arc B rounds 1–2)
**Round 2 (2026-06-15)** completed dark mode by theming the B1 "light islands" (the paintEvent charts + the per-account Summary window). `chart_helpers` gained structural-colour accessors (`chart_surface`/`chart_grid`/`chart_axis_ink`/`chart_ink`/`chart_faint`/`chart_tooltip_bg`/`chart_tooltip_ink`) returning a token at paint time; all ~12 charts' structural `QColor("#…")` calls (plot background, gridlines, axis text, segment separators, tooltips) were converted to them, while the `GROUP_PALETTE` series colours and white-text-on-coloured-fill (bar/tile labels, the amber today-pill) deliberately stay fixed. `account_summary_window` (its `_COLOR_*` constants + inline `setStyleSheet` + paintEvent) was converted to `tokens.themed()`/`tokens.c()`. `theme.apply_theme` now force-repaints every widget after re-applying, so charts (which read tokens at paint time) redraw into the new theme on a live toggle with no per-chart wiring. Verified offscreen on a live-DB copy: chart structural colours switch with the theme; the account-summary (cash + investment), Spending, and Investment-Returns windows build in dark and survive a light↔dark toggle. **Round 1** (foundation) below.

### ADR-076 — Design tokens + light/dark theming (Arc B round 1)
First Arc B round, amending ADR-026's light-only baseline. The per-window styling allowed by ADR-026 had sprawled — ~15 UI files hardcoded **hundreds** of hex literals — and drifted: the baseline used a *gray* ramp (`#6b7280`/`#374151`) while the feature windows used the true Tailwind *slate* ramp (`#64748b`/`#334155`/`#0f172a`), so there were two "slate-500"s plus casing mismatches, and no way to add a dark theme without editing every file. Owner decisions (`AskUserQuestion`): the design-system foundation **and** a dark-mode toggle. Solution: a semantic token layer (`ui/tokens.py`) — named tokens (`canvas`, `surface`, `surface_alt`, `border`, `text`, `heading`, `muted`, `subtle`, `accent`, `accent_subtle`, `positive`, `negative`, `warning`, …), each carrying a light and a dark value, resolved by `c(name)`. The safety discipline that makes a ~140-site refactor low-risk: **every token's light value equals the hex it replaced**, so light mode is unchanged by construction and only the dark values are a fresh design (the gray ramp is unified onto slate as the intended consolidation). Live switching uses two mechanisms re-run on a theme change: (1) `theme.py` rebuilds the QPalette + global QSS from the tokens, re-theming every standard widget (windows, dialogs, inputs, buttons, menus, tables, trees, scrollbars) for free; (2) a **themed-stylesheet registry** — `tokens.themed(widget, "color: {muted}; font-size: 11px;")` formats the template with the active tokens, sets it, and stores `(widget, template)` in a `WeakKeyDictionary`, re-formatting every registered widget on switch (handles arbitrary colour+size+weight combos a fixed CSS-class vocabulary couldn't; `_format` substitutes `{token}` via regex so literal QSS `{ … }` blocks pass through untouched). `tokens.notifier.changed` is emitted so paintEvent charts can repaint. The toggle (`theme.apply_theme(app, name)`) persists `ui_theme` to the `setting` table (no migration); `__main__` reads it on launch (before any window shows, so no flash); a **View ▸ Dark Mode** checkable menu in the register window drives it live. The conversion was done by two bounded regex sweeps (single-line, then multi-line concatenated-literal `setStyleSheet` calls) mapping each hex to its token, plus hand edits for `f-string`/dynamic colours; the register, sidebar, Home dashboard, all dialogs, and the saved-report windows (Spending / Income & Expense / Payee / Category×Payee / Net Worth / Sankey / Investment Returns) theme fully. **Intentionally deferred to B2 as readable light "islands":** the paintEvent charts (they fill a white plot background and draw dark text on it) and the per-account Summary window (`account_summary_window`, a paintEvent dashboard on module-level `_COLOR_*` constants) — both stay internally consistent and legible (dark text on their own white surface) in dark mode; theming them onto the tokens is the next sweep. Rejected: a fixed `QLabel[cssClass="muted"]` vocabulary (the app's inline styles mix colour with size/weight/letter-spacing in too many combinations), apply-on-restart dark mode (worse UX), and keeping the gray ramp (perpetuates the two-ramp split). **Verified** offscreen on a copy of the live database: tokens resolve per theme (`text` `#0f172a`↔`#f1f5f9`, `canvas` `#f8fafc`↔`#0f172a`); a registered probe label restyles on toggle; the register window (with its Dark Mode action checked) and the Spending, Payee, and Net Worth report windows and the Rules dialog all build in dark mode without error; and the toggle round-trips the `ui_theme` setting light↔dark.

### ADR-075 — Home / dashboard screen (Arc F)
The app dropped you into a register on launch; as MFL heads toward being shared with non-technical friends/family it should open on an at-a-glance overview. Every number already exists as shipped compute, so this arc is an assembly + presentation layer — **no new aggregation semantics, no schema change, no migration**. The register window's right side becomes a `QStackedWidget` with two pages — the **Home** dashboard and the existing register/report panel (filter bar + table) — and a **Home** row sits at the very top of the sidebar (above ACCOUNTS), emitting `selection_changed("home", None)`; the `_show_*` methods flip the stack to the register page, and `_show_home` flips back and refreshes. **Home is the default landing view on launch** (owner fork), replacing "open the first account". Owner-chosen cards, each self-hiding when it has nothing to show: **net worth** (headline assets − debts in the display currency, FX-converted with ADR-055 rules — no-rate accounts excluded and counted, never par-added; click → Net Worth window); **budget this month** (the default budget's Expenses-section planned vs actual for the current month from `compute_matrix`, with a progress bar that reddens when over; hidden when no budget covers the month); **accounts overview** (each account's market value grouped by family with subtotals; account rows click → that register); **upcoming bills** (the next few due/overdue schedules from `list_scheduled_txns`, overdue-cued; click → Manage ▸ Schedules); **recent activity** (the latest N transactions via a new bounded `Repository.list_recent_transactions(limit)` so the dashboard never materialises the full ledger; rows click → account); **top-5 payees this month** (`payee_spending_aggregates` + `build_report`, FX-converted); **top-5 categories this month** (`category_payee_matrix` rolled up by category, FX-converted — chosen over the native-sum `top_categories` precisely because the owner's data is 11 GBP + 15 USD accounts and a bare pence sum would mix currencies); and **investment performance** (top-5 unrealised gains and top-5 losses by security, aggregating `compute_holdings_view` across all investment accounts, **each holding converted to the display currency before aggregating** so a USD holding's gain isn't mislabelled or par-added — the same ADR-055 discipline). New Qt-free `mfl_desktop/home_dashboard.py` (`HomeData` dataclass + `gather_home_data(repo, today, *, recent_n, top_n)`; each card assembled in isolation so one failure logs and degrades to empty rather than blanking the screen) keeps the FX/period logic out of the widgets and offscreen-testable; `mfl_desktop/ui/home_view.py` is presentation only (a `QScrollArea` of card frames, navigation `Signal`s the register window wires to its existing handlers, refresh on `WindowActivate`). Period for the spending cards is the current calendar month (labelled "this month"); the investment card is a point-in-time unrealised snapshot, not a time-weighted return (that's ADR-046). Owner forks (`AskUserQuestion`): Home as the default landing view; the eight cards (the owner expanded the original four — net worth / bills / recent / accounts — with budget summary, top payees, top categories, and investment gains/losses). Rejected: a separate Home window (a stacked pane keeps one window and reuses the sidebar), recomputing bespoke aggregates (would risk drift from the dedicated screens), Home opt-in only (owner chose default). Deferred: a per-card period selector, card reorder/hide customisation, quick-action buttons (menus/shortcuts already cover those). **Verified** offscreen on a seeded file and on a copy of the live database — net worth £2,655,972 with 0 excluded; the five family groups (Cash/Credit/Investments/Property/Vehicles) summing to it; budget "June 2026" £1,900 planned vs £2,320 spent (over); FX-converted top payees (IRS, Amazon, …) and categories; per-security gains shown in GBP (Morgan Stanley +£131k +312.9%) with the lone loss (WEN −£258); plus offscreen-Qt that the Home view builds its cards and emits its navigation signals, the sidebar exposes a Home row whose `select_home` emits `("home", None)`, and a real `RegisterWindow` lands on the Home page (stack index 0) and flips to the register (index 1) on account selection and back on Home selection.

### ADR-074 — Capture a scheduled transfer's destination at post time
Owner-reported bug: posting a transfer-kind scheduled transaction that had no destination account failed with *"Transfer schedule is missing a destination account."* (raised by `post_scheduled_txn`) and gave no way to fix it. Setup normally captures the destination — `ScheduleDialog` reveals an inline picker and validates it whenever the category is transfer-kind — but a schedule can become transfer-kind *without* one if its category's kind was switched to `transfer` after the schedule was created (the stored `transfer_to_account_id` stays NULL while `category_kind` flips), or if it was seeded from a transaction without one. The launch auto-post sweep already swallows such failures per-schedule, so the only visible breakage was the manual Post Now flow. Fix (owner's suggestion — capture at setup *or* posting): `SchedulesDialog._on_post_now`, before the amount prompt/confirm, detects a transfer-kind schedule with no destination and opens the existing `TransferDestinationDialog` (unlocked, so any non-source account can be picked; explains and stops if there's no other account), persists the choice via new `Repository.set_scheduled_transfer_destination(schedule_id, account_id)` (validates dest≠source), re-reads the schedule, and continues — so the confirm shows the chosen destination and the existing cross-currency block still collects the partner amount when the currencies differ. Persisting (rather than a one-off destination for this post) repairs the template, so future manual posts *and* the auto-post sweep work and the Schedules list shows the destination.
