No schema change, no migration; reuses the same destination widget as the register's inline-transfer and cross-currency flows. Rejected: post-once-without-persist (re-prompts every occurrence, auto-post keeps skipping it), fixing only setup/edit (doesn't help the user who hits the error at post time and doesn't know the schedule is mis-configured). **Verified** offscreen: a schedule inserted with `transfer_to_account_id = NULL` raises on post, then after `set_scheduled_transfer_destination` posts both halves with a shared `transfer_id` and correct signs, and dest==source is rejected; offscreen Qt drives `_on_post_now` with the destination dialog stubbed and confirms the destination is persisted, both halves post, and `schedules_changed` fires.

### ADR-073 — Auto-categorisation rules engine (Arc G round 2)
Round 2 of the auto-categorisation arc (ADR-028 round 3), and the screen the owner sketched: *"a dedicated screen to be able to see all of the aliases, and be able to create or delete rules — 'if contains xxxx then payee yyyy', or starts with / ends with / is exactly."* ADR-072 (round 1) covered the *exact-payee* case (a payee remembers its category); this covers the *pattern* case (a stable substring of a varying merchant string). The `rule` table has sat unused since migration 0001; its `pattern_kind` CHECK only allowed `substring`/`regex`, which doesn't match the owner's vocabulary, so **migration 0025** recreates the table with `CHECK(pattern_kind IN ('contains','starts_with','ends_with','is_exactly'))` (the report-CHECK recipe; the table was empty so the CASE-mapping copy is defensive). Aliases and rules stay **separate at the data layer** (ADR-028 Option C / ADR-072 — identity vs. automation); the "unified screen" is a view. The engine is a pure, dependency-free `rules_engine.py`: `rule_matches(rule, payee_text, memo)` (case-insensitive, the four kinds, empty-pattern never matches) and `apply_rules(rules, payee_text, memo)` (priority ascending = highest first, ties by id; **field-independent first-win** so a payee-only rule and a category-only rule compose) — it takes duck-typed rule objects so the Repository's `RuleRow` works without a circular import (mirrors `budget_calc`/`goal_calc`). Applied in `ImportService.commit_import` **after** the ADR-072 alias resolution, loaded once per batch: a rule that sets a payee **overrides** the resolved one (and the per-payee default is re-read from the rule's payee); category precedence when the source left the row Uncategorised (and it isn't a split) is **rule category → else per-payee default**, a file-carried category still winning; `rule_payee` applies to split parents (payee is parent-level) but `rule_cat` doesn't (the parent stays Uncategorised, its lines carry categories). Re-import dedup is unaffected (cash hashes on `payee_raw`). Manual entry runs no pattern rules (no raw text — you pick a payee); instead `NewTransactionDialog` now pre-fills the category from a typed payee's remembered category (optional callback, backward-compatible — the deferred G1 nicety). Retroactive application (owner fork: **ask each time**): on creating/editing a rule the screen offers *"Apply to N matching existing transactions?"*, reusing the same pure `rule_matches` against each transaction's **stored payee name** (the original raw import string isn't retained, so the current name is the proxy — a `contains TESCO` rule still matches a row now named "Tesco") and memo, filling only an **Uncategorised** category / **NULL** payee, never overwriting, never touching transfers or split parents (`count_txns_matching_rule` / `apply_rule_to_existing`). Repository: `RuleRow` (+ display `set_payee_name`/`set_category_path`), `list/create/update/delete_rule` (validates matcher kind/field + at-least-one-setter), `new_rule_iri()`. UI: `rule_edit_dialog.py` (match-field + matcher-kind combos, pattern, optional canonical-payee picker, optional category picker, priority spin; validates pattern non-empty, typed payee resolves, ≥1 setter) and `rules_dialog.py` — **Manage ▸ Rules…**: an editable rules table (When / Sets payee / Sets category / Priority + New/Edit/Delete) and a **read-only aliases** table (the existing `canonical_id` aliases as implicit "is exactly → payee" rules, "manage in Payees…"), giving the owner the whole picture in one place without duplicating alias CRUD. Owner forks (`AskUserQuestion`): rules screen with aliases shown read-only; retroactive ask-each-time; rules set payee and/or category. Rejected: merging aliases into `rule` (conflates identity/automation, disturbs the load-bearing `COALESCE(canonical_id,id)` rollup), regex matchers (power-user feature at odds with the non-technical audience — easy to re-add), matching rules against the resolved payee (that's what the per-payee default already does), rules on manual entry (no raw text), retroactive overwrite (would clobber deliberate edits). **Verified** offscreen: the pure engine (each kind + case-insensitivity, priority + field-independent compose, empty guard); the migration CHECK swap (`is_exactly` present, `substring` gone); Repository CRUD with display names + retroactive scope (only unset/uncategorised, no transfers/splits, never overwrite); an end-to-end Banktivity import (a `contains` rule sets payee + category on a matching row, a file-carried category is kept, rule-category beats the per-payee default, the split guard holds); and offscreen Qt (rule edit round-trip + empty-pattern/no-setter rejection, the rules dialog listing one rule + one read-only alias with the right "Payee text contains …" text, and the New Transaction dialog pre-filling the category from a remembered payee).

### ADR-072 — Payee→category memory (Arc G round 1)
First round of the auto-categorisation arc (ADR-028). After every import the owner re-categorises the same merchants by hand; the app should remember "Tesco → Groceries" and apply it. The schema reserved the hooks long ago (`payee.default_category_id` + the `rule` table, both since migration 0001) but nothing read or wrote them, and the import engine did **zero** payee/category lookup. This round closes the highest-value slice — a payee remembers its category and imports apply it — and defers the pattern-rules engine + unified management screen to round 2. Owner forks (`AskUserQuestion`): **import-memory first**; memories created by a **confirm prompt** (not silent learning, not manual-only); retroactive application **offered each time** and only ever onto **Uncategorised** rows. The memory is stored on the **canonical** payee's `default_category_id` (so every alias of one merchant shares it); reads/writes resolve alias→canonical via `_canonical_id_for`, and Uncategorised(1) clears it. **No migration.** New `Repository.resolve_import_payee(raw) -> (payee_id, default_category_id)` — empty → `(None, None)` (investment rows, ADR-071); an **alias** name returns its **canonical** id (ADR-028 round 2: new ledger rows point at the canonical, so the register shows the clean name and history rolls up without a read-time `COALESCE`); unknown → a new canonical. `ImportService.commit_import`'s plain-insert branch fills the category from the memory **only when the row would otherwise be Uncategorised** and isn't a split (a category the file carried always wins; split parents stay Uncategorised, their lines live in `txn_split`); re-import dedup is unaffected (cash hashes on `payee_raw`, not `payee_id`). Capture point: a `MemoriseCategoryDialog` fires on a non-transfer inline register category edit **only when the payee has no memory yet** (a deliberate one-off override never re-prompts; changing a memory is a Payees-dialog job) — "Always categorise **Tesco** as **Groceries**?" with an opt-in "also apply to N existing uncategorised" checkbox (shown only when N>0). Management: the Payees dialog gains an **Auto-category** column (canonical's category as a full breadcrumb path) + an **Auto-category…** button (single selection → picker with a **Clear** verb → same retroactive-apply prompt). Retroactive helpers `count_/apply_default_category_to_uncategorised` operate over the canonical **and its aliases** (`expand_canonical_payee_ids`), touching only `category_id = Uncategorised`, `transfer_id IS NULL`, non-split rows, returning the row count and never overwriting. `PayeeRow` gains `default_category_id`; `list_payees_with_usage` selects it. Rejected: silent learning (less control for a fastidious owner), manual-only (misses the capture moment), storing the memory on `rule` now (conflates identity and automation — ADR-028 Option C; round 2 adds rules as a distinct concept), always-overwrite retroactively (would clobber deliberate categorisations). **Verified** offscreen: `resolve_import_payee` (empty/unknown/alias→canonical + carried default); `set/get` alias→canonical + Uncategorised-clears; an end-to-end Banktivity import (Tesco with no source category → Groceries via memory, a Tesco row whose file carried Food kept as Food, an unknown payee left Uncategorised); `count_/apply` scoping (2 across canonical+alias, already-categorised row untouched); and offscreen Qt (MemoriseCategoryDialog's apply flag honours the count; the Payees dialog renders the Auto-category column showing "Food → Groceries" and enables the button on single selection).

### ADR-071 — Investment QIF `P` field is a description, not a payee
Closes the root cause behind the 2026-06-14 live-DB cleanup that deleted 150 junk payees. Investment QIF rows carry a `P` line; in the brokerage exports the owner imports (Banktivity → QIF) it is a free-text **description** ("DIV - SABRA HEALTH CARE REIT INC REC 08/29/25 …"), but ADR-043's round-1 parser copied it into `payee_raw`, and the import service mints a payee from `payee_raw`. So every investment import created one payee per distinct description string, and **re-importing the same QIF regenerated them** — the cleanup was a one-off that the next import undid. The real identity is already captured by the security (`Y` → `security_id`, ADR-044) and the action (`N`); `P` is useful only as memo text. Fix is **parser-only** (`qif_parser._normalise_invst_record`): the memo is now composed from `P` **and** `M` (de-duped so `P==M` doesn't double up) ahead of the existing `Transfer to/from [Account]` note, and `payee_raw` is set to `""` so the service's `get_or_create_payee("")` returns `None` — **investment-action rows never mint a payee**. No schema change, no migration, no Repository/UI change; the cash CSV/OFX/QIF-bank paths don't go through this normaliser and are untouched. **Re-import dedup is unaffected**: investment rows hash on account+date+action+security+quantity+amount (`compute_investment_hash`), never the payee, so previously-imported rows still match and the junk is simply never created again. Owner forks (`AskUserQuestion`): scope = **all investment-action rows** (not just Div/income — `P` is a description for every action type, so gating only dividends leaves the same trap on Buy/Sell/Cash); `P` text = **folded into the memo** (not dropped — no information lost). Amends ADR-043. Rejected: drop `P` entirely (loses the text); gate only Div rows (narrower, same trap elsewhere); a payee-cleanup migration (orthogonal — the one-off already ran; this fixes the *source*); map `P` to the security as payee (conflates two first-class concepts). **Verified** offscreen on a synthetic investment QIF: Div (`P` only) → `payee_raw=''`, memo = the `P` text; Buy (`P`+`M`) → `payee_raw=''`, memo folds both deduped; Cash/transfer (`P`+`L`) → `payee_raw=''`, memo = `P` + the transfer note; confirmed `get_or_create_payee('')` is `None` and the dedup hash excludes the payee.

### ADR-070 — Category lifecycle: archive / restore
Arc D, the sibling of ADR-069 on the hierarchical `category` tree. The only category removal today was `delete_category`, which re-points the category's transactions to **Uncategorised** and drops the row — destructive of the historical attribution. The owner wants to *hide* a category without rewriting history and bring it back later. `category.archived_at` was reserved by ADR-011 and the tree/picker/budget queries already filter `WHERE archived_at IS NULL`; nothing set it. So, **no migration** — mirror the account decisions: one **Archive** concept, excluded-by-default with a "Show archived" toggle, flow-report history retained (reports aggregate `txn`/`txn_category_line` by `category_id`, never gated on `archived_at`). The tree adds one wrinkle: archiving must keep it consistent — no active child stranded under an archived parent. So **archive cascades down** the subtree (`archive_category(id)` archives id + all descendants; rejects Uncategorised id=1; idempotent) and **restore cascades down *and* up** (`unarchive_category(id)` clears id + subtree + every ancestor to the root, so a restored node is always reachable), maintaining the invariant **"every non-archived category has a non-archived parent (or is a root)."** The parent pickers (New / Reparent) refuse archived nodes, and `find_or_create_category_path` **resurrects** (un-archives) any matched archived path on import — the `UNIQUE(parent_id, name)` constraint blocks a fresh sibling, and an import re-using a path means it's in use again. `CategoryNode` gains `archived`; `list_category_tree(include_archived=False)`; new private `_category_ancestors` (the recursive mirror of `category_descendants`). The Categories dialog gains a **"Show archived"** checkbox (archived rows greyed + a "(archived)" suffix) and one **Archive/Restore** button that flips by selection (Restore when every selected row is already archived, else Archive — which confirms, noting the subtree cascade and that history is kept). `delete_category` stays as the destructive variant; the dialog now leads with Archive. Trade-offs: cascade restore can un-archive children individually archived earlier inside a since-archived branch (acceptable for "restore a branch"); reports' category checklists drop archived categories from their *filters* (history still in the unfiltered totals); `category_descendants` / `category_has_children` / `_sibling_exists` deliberately still see archived rows so a name collision with an archived sibling still blocks a rename/create. **Verified** offscreen on a live-DB snapshot: archiving a real 13-node branch cascades to exactly its 13 descendants; the branch vanishes from the default tree and returns with `include_archived=True` (all flagged `archived`); restoring a deep descendant restores its ancestors so it's reachable; full restore brings the branch back; archiving Uncategorised raises; an archived leaf re-imported via `find_or_create_category_path` returns the same id (no duplicate) and reappears; and the dialog's Show-archived reload runs clean.

### ADR-069 — Account lifecycle: close / reopen (soft-close)
Arc C of the lifecycle arc. Accounts accumulate over a financial life and get closed — but the only removal today is the destructive `delete_account`, which cascades away every transaction and all import history. Wrong for a *closed* account: its history is real and should still count in the flow reports; the owner just wants it out of the sidebar and Net Worth. `account.archived_at` was reserved by ADR-011 and every list query already filters `WHERE archived_at IS NULL` — the column was never *set*. So this is almost entirely UX + a verb, **no migration**. Owner decisions (`AskUserQuestion`): **one Close verb** (not Close vs. Hide), and **excluded-by-default with a "Show closed" toggle**. Repository: `AccountSummary` gains `archived_at` + an `is_closed` property; `list_accounts` / `list_investment_accounts` / `compute_account_balances` / `compute_account_values` gain `include_closed=False` (default **unchanged**, so every existing caller — transaction/transfer pickers, budgets, all reports — is byte-identical; only the sidebar build and Net Worth's toggle pass `True`); new `close_account(id)` sets `archived_at = datetime('now')` (idempotent), `reopen_account(id)` clears it, `delete_account` stays as the destructive variant. Sidebar: the register window feeds it `include_closed=True` and it **partitions** open vs. closed itself — open accounts render exactly as before, closed accounts are pulled into one **collapsible "Closed accounts (N)" group** at the bottom of the ACCOUNTS section (collapsed by default, muted slate-400 leaves that stay selectable so a closed account's register is viewable, a `CLOSED_ROLE` marker so the context menu offers the right verbs; `select_account_by_iri` descends into and expands the group). Register window: Account menu gains **Close Account…** (above Delete, enabled only for an open selection); a closed account's right-click offers Summary / **Reopen Account** / Delete, an open account's offers Edit / Move / **Close Account…** / Delete. Net Worth: a **"Show closed accounts"** checkbox threads `include_closed` into every total, donut, and column (closed leaves get a " (closed)" suffix). **Flow reports keep closed history by construction** — Spending / Income & Expense / Sankey / Payee / Category aggregate the `txn` / `txn_category_line` tables and never gate on `account.archived_at`, so a closed account's transactions flow into the unfiltered totals; only the report *account-pickers* (which use `list_accounts`) stop offering it. Trade-offs: you can't *filter a report to* a single closed account (additive per-report toggle if it bites); closing doesn't auto-zero a non-empty account (it just disappears from Net Worth until "Show closed" is ticked). **Verified** offscreen on a WAL-consistent live-DB snapshot (28 checks): close/reopen membership in `list_accounts` + `compute_account_values` (with and without `include_closed`), the Net Worth sum dropping then restoring the closed balance (headline £2,589,980 ↔ £2,656,421), idempotent re-close keeping its timestamp, the sidebar rendering a collapsed Closed group with the `CLOSED_ROLE` marker and `select_account_by_iri` finding the closed account, the Net Worth toggle changing the headline, and the Categories dialog smoke.

### ADR-068 — Category & Payee report (two-level cross-drill)
Arc E round 3 (E3), the last reports thread. Spending Over Time answers "where does my money go" (by category) and the Payee report (ADR-066) "who do I pay" (by payee); E3 is the **intersection** — within Groceries, which payees? for Tesco, which categories? Owner picked (via `AskUserQuestion`) a **two-level drill report** (over a cross-tab matrix grid or folding the breakdown into the two existing reports) with a **Category-first** default. Level 1 ranks the **primary dimension** (a top-bar Category/Payee toggle); clicking a row drills to a **level-2 breakdown by the other dimension** for that item; clicking a level-2 row opens the **transactions**; a ← Back button + breadcrumb pop level 2 back to level 1. Adopts the house defaults without re-asking: strict outflow (`kind='expense'`, `amount<0`), transfers excluded with a toggle, a display-currency selector (view-only), top-N per level with a hidden-count note (no "Other"). `report.type` never reserved `category_payee`, so **migration 0024** widens the CHECK (the 0014/0023 table-recreate recipe). One aggregate `Repository.category_payee_matrix` runs a single grouped query → spending per **(leaf category, canonical payee, currency)** cell, FX-converted to the display currency at period-end (no-rate slices excluded + noted, ADR-055), payees rolled to canonical (`COALESCE(p.canonical_id,p.id)`), transfers dropped unless included. Returning the *matrix* rather than a pre-pivoted list lets the window **pivot, roll up, and drill entirely in-memory** — toggling the dimension or drilling never re-queries. The category dimension rolls leaf categories up to the **budget-line level** (`category_group_map` — Groceries, Transport…, *not* the Income/Expense roots `category_root_map` would collapse everything into); the transaction drill then uses `category_descendants(group)` so nothing under the group is missed, paired with the payee expanded back to canonical + aliases (`expand_canonical_payee_ids`) or the NULL-payee group, in the shared `TransactionsListWindow` (ADR-034, which already filters by category *and* payee together). Reuses the Payee report's ranked-bar `PayeeChart`, `build_report` ranking (top-N + hidden-count), the sortable-table pattern, and the drill-down window — so E3 is one new repo method + one window (`category_payee_window.py`) + one filter dialog (`category_payee_filter_dialog.py`) + the type plumbing. `PayeeSpendRow.payee_id` carries "the current row's item id" whichever dimension it is (a category-group id or a canonical-payee id), documented in the window; `group_by`/period/accounts/top-N/transfers persist, the display currency + drill are view-only. Wired into the New Report dialog, the Reports menu (`Reports ▸ Category & Payee…`), and the bare/saved dispatch. Trade-offs noted: two levels only (the second click goes to transactions, not a third axis); top-N truncates silently in the chart (summary flags hidden count); the reused `payee_id` field naming smell; coarse drill account scope (single account exact, subset → cross-account, can over-include); budget-line grouping hides the leaf until you reach the transactions. **Verified** offscreen on a seeded temp DB: the matrix merges Tesco's canonical + alias spend into one £60/2-txn cell on the leaf; level-1 category-first yields the budget-line groups (Groceries/Transport/Dining) with Groceries rolling its leaf+sub spend to £65; drilling Groceries → payees gives Tesco £60 + Shell £5, and (payee-first) drilling Shell → categories gives Groceries £5 + Transport £30; the level-2 leaf click opens the (Groceries, Tesco) transactions as exactly 2 rows (alias rolled in); Back clears the drill; and a saved `category_payee` report round-trips through `create_report`/`load_from_id` preserving `group_by`.

### ADR-067 — Net Worth two-ring donut (a scoped exception to "no pies")
Arc E round 3 (E4). The Net Worth window's summary panel used a horizontal **proportional bar** for composition precisely because ADR-018 ruled out pies ("rarely convey accurate data"). The owner asked to replace it with a **two-ring donut**: inner ring = account *type*, outer ring = the *individual accounts* within each type. That conflicts with ADR-018, so it's an explicit decision to **narrow** that rule, not ignore it — the coherent line: pies/donuts stay banned for **time-series / cross-series comparison** (the spending, income & expense, payee, Sankey, returns reports — where a pie is actively worse than bars+line), but a donut is **allowed for a point-in-time composition of one positive whole**, which is the one case it reads well (and the two-ring form adds a type→account level a single bar can't show without a dense stack). A donut also can't hold a **negative** slice and net worth has debts (stored negative), so — owner pick via `AskUserQuestion` — there are **two donuts**: a larger **Assets** donut and a smaller **Debts** donut (the latter flips stored-negative balances to positive "amount owed" and hides entirely when there are no debts). New generic `mfl_desktop/ui/donut_chart.py` — `DonutChart` (stateless `paintEvent`, `set_data`/`show_empty`) over `DonutSegment` (a type) each holding `DonutChild` outer slices (accounts); the annulus is drawn by full `drawPie` wedges with the inner ring overpainting the inner band and a punched centre hole, thin white separators, angles tracked **clockwise from 12 o'clock** and converted to Qt's CCW-from-3-o'clock 1/16° convention only at draw, hover tooltip with amount + share. Outer slices are progressively lighter tints (`_shade`) of the type's family colour so they read as one type while staying distinct; the hollow centre shows the side's total. `net_worth_window._donut_segments(type_totals, kind)` builds the data from the **already-FX-converted** per-account values, so the entire ADR-055 currency story carries over unchanged: display-currency selector, an account with **no rate excluded** from the donut (never par-added) and still surfaced in the missing-rate banner, native-amount tooltips in the columns. The family legend, Assets/Debts columns, and banner are untouched; the summary column was widened a little for the donuts. Reuses the existing standalone Net Worth window — no new saved report type, no migration (the reserved `net_worth` saved type stays unused; a second entry point would only confuse). Owner forks (`AskUserQuestion`): two donuts (over assets-only or one signed magnitude donut), replace the bar in the existing window (over a new saved report), inner ring = account type (over family). `proportional_bar.py` is now unused but left in place (still a valid generic widget). **Amends ADR-018** (status note added there). **Verified** offscreen on seeded temp DBs: the assets inner ring is exactly the three seeded asset types; the Savings type nests its two accounts (ISA + Savings) whose values sum to the type's £8,000; outer children carry distinct shaded colours; the debts donut shows one Credit card type (£500) and is shown/hidden by debt presence; a USD account with no GBP rate is excluded from the donut and appears in the missing-rate list; and the empty + single-segment paint paths render without error (via `grab()`).

### ADR-066 — Payee report (ranked spending by payee)
Arc E round 2 (E2). Adds the `payee` report type — spending ranked by payee, "who do I pay the most?" — the by-whom cut to sit alongside Spending Over Time (by category) and Income & Expense (over time). Unlike `income_expense` (reserved in the 0010 CHECK so ADR-064 needed no migration), `payee` was never reserved, so **migration 0023** rebuilds the `report` table to widen the `type` CHECK (the 0014 recipe: `foreign_keys=OFF` swap, indexes recreated). **Measure = strict outflow** (`kind='expense'` AND `amount<0` — the ADR-018 rule that keeps bars positive and stops income/refunds muddying the ranking), over the split-unrolled `txn_category_line` view (ADR-051), grouped per **canonical payee** via `COALESCE(p.canonical_id, p.id)` (ADR-028/029 — "AMZN" and "Amazon UK" count as one, labelled with the canonical name); no-payee lines collapse to a single group. **Transfers excluded by default with an "Include transfers" toggle** (drops `transfer_id` legs too), mirroring ADR-064. **Display-currency selector** converts each (payee, currency) slice at period-end; a slice with no rate is excluded + noted, never par-added (ADR-055); the currency is a view preference, not saved. **Visual = ranked horizontal bars over a sortable detail table** (payee / spend / % / txns). **Top-N keeps the biggest payees and the tail is simply omitted — no "Other" bucket** (an owner review of the first cut found the "Other" row more clutter than insight); the summary instead reports `hidden_count` ("Showing top 15 of 73 payees (58 hidden)"), `top_n=0` shows all, and each row's pct/total are over *all* payees so the visible bars can sum to under 100% (each bar's % is its true share). **Both the bars and the table rows are click-through** to the underlying transactions: a click opens `TransactionsListWindow` (ADR-034) scoped to that payee over the report's date range, **expanding the canonical payee id back to canonical + aliases** (`expand_canonical_payee_ids`) so the drill lists exactly what the bar counted, while the "(No payee)" group drills to NULL-payee transactions. That required widening the shared drill-down: `TxnListFilter.for_payees` (a `payee_ids` set + a `payee_is_null` flag, with `signature()` updated) and `DrillDownFilterProxy.set_payee_ids` / `set_payee_null` (the existing single-id path untouched). New `Repository.payee_spending_aggregates` (one grouped SQL pass + per-slice FX), pure `reports/payee_report.py` (`build_report` ranks, truncates to top-N, attaches pct, derives the summary incl. hidden count — no Qt/SQL, no Other), `payee_chart.py` (hand-rolled horizontal-bar paintEvent, ADR-026/no-pies; single accent hue, hover tooltip, `payee_clicked` signal + pointer cursor), `payee_report_window.py` (display-currency + Filter/Save/Save-As, chart over clickable table, summary panel with the hidden-count note, the ADR-039 bare/saved + dirty/close lifecycle), `payee_filter_dialog.py` (period + custom range + "Show top N" spin + transfers toggle + accounts checklist). Wired into the New Report dialog, the Reports menu (`Reports ▸ Payee…`), and the bare/saved dispatch. Owner forks (`AskUserQuestion`): spending-only (over two-sided income+expense / signed-net), bars+table (over either alone), canonical roll-up (over raw payee), exclude-transfers + toggle (over always-exclude); **review-driven changes**: drop the "Other" row, make rows clickable. Trade-offs noted: aliases not linked to a canonical still show (and drill) separately (payee-data hygiene, now visible); top-N truncates silently in the chart (only the summary flags the hidden count); the drill-down's account scope is coarse (single account exact, account-subset opens cross-account and can over-include); the drill list shows *all* of the payee's transactions in range, not just the strict-outflow expenses the bar summed. **Verified** offscreen on a seeded temp DB: alias roll-up (£50+£30→one £80 Amazon, 2 txns); income / refund / transfer-kind / linked-leg all excluded under the default; the no-payee group; the include-transfers toggle adding the linked leg; USD spend excluded with no rate then converted ($100×0.80→£80) once a rate exists; pure rank + top-N truncation + hidden-count + pct + `top_n=0` (and no `is_other`); the alias-rollup drill showing 2 rows and the null-payee drill showing 1; a click spawning a drill window; and the Qt window building/populating + a saved `payee` report round-tripping through `create_report`/`load_from_id`.

### ADR-065 — Historical FX rate backfill (UI + sampling granularity)
Wires the `fx.backfill_historical` backend (written for ADR-035 but never given a caller) to a **"Backfill historical…"** button in the Currencies dialog. The gap bit in practice: the owner's `fx_rate` table only had June-2026 rows while their data has cross-currency activity going back years, and `get_fx_rate_nearest` is nearest-*prior* — so a 2025 transaction got no conversion (excluded from report totals) and the cross-currency transfer matcher found 0 candidates purely for want of a rate (adding one surfaced all 11 as Strong). New `FxBackfillDialog` (`ui/fx_backfill_dialog.py`): date From/To (From defaults to the earliest transaction date, To today), **Monthly / Weekly / Daily** sampling, a live "≈ N API calls (one per sampled date)" estimate naming the currencies, a large-run (≥60) confirm restating the free-tier budget (ADR-035 guard-rails), and a synchronous run behind a `QProgressDialog` where cancel stops after the current date (fetched rates kept). Backend: `backfill_historical` gains a `granularity` param; new pure `sample_backfill_dates` enumerates the dates (daily = every day; weekly = every 7 days from the start; monthly = the start date then the 1st of each following month; `date_to` always appended), the fetch loop iterates samples keeping skip-if-present + per-date error accumulation. USD-base only (free-tier), so quotes = non-USD currencies in use; a USD-only file disables the button. Monthly is enough because nearest-prior fills the gaps and a linked transfer's stored rate is back-derived from the real amounts (the sampled rate only drives display conversion + match confidence). Owner fork (`AskUserQuestion`): monthly default + selectable (over daily-only / monthly-only). **Verified**: `sample_backfill_dates` monthly/weekly/daily counts + `date_to` inclusion + reversed-range guard; `backfill_historical` with a mocked client fetched exactly the sampled dates, upserted, and a re-run skipped all (0 calls); stored rate retrievable via nearest-prior; offscreen Qt (dialog builds, estimate updates by granularity, USD-only disables). Amends ADR-035; closes its "backfill_historical wired in the Currencies dialog" backlog item.

### ADR-064 — Income & Expense report (cash-flow over time)
First round (E1) of the Reports arc (Arc E). Fills the `income_expense` report type that ADR-039 reserved (and "(coming later)"-flagged) but never built — the classic cash-flow view of money in vs. money out per period. No migration: the type was already in the `report.type` CHECK (migration 0014). **Income vs. expense by category kind** — income = inflows (`amount > 0`) on `kind='income'` categories, expense = outflows (`amount < 0`) on `kind='expense'` categories, **transfers excluded** — the same rule as the Sankey report (rejected: raw amount sign, which lets refunds/transfers muddy the totals). **Transfers excluded by default with an "Include transfers" toggle** — `kind='transfer'` is always excluded by the kind rule, and the off-by-default toggle additionally drops linked transfer-pair legs (`transfer_id IS NOT NULL`) that were filed under an income/expense category; a transfer recorded under an income/expense category but not linked as a pair still needs its kind set to `transfer` to drop out. **Chart** = income bars above the zero baseline / expense bars below + a **net (income − expense) line**, with dashed average-income/expense reference lines — the `BalanceFlowChart` (ADR-033/034) shape on a **single shared y-axis** (net is bounded by the bar magnitudes, so no dual axis), hand-rolled paintEvent (ADR-026, no pies). **Multi-currency**: a "Display in:" selector converts every (bucket, currency) total to one currency before summing (the report sums across accounts, so a bare par-add would be the ADR-055 bug); no-rate buckets are excluded + noted, never folded at 1:1; the currency is a view preference, not saved (like Net Worth/Sankey). New pure `reports/income_expense.py` — `enumerate_buckets` builds the continuous bucket list with keys byte-identical to the SQL `strftime` (calendar-analytic for year/quarter/month; day-walked for weeks because SQLite's `%W` splits a Mon–Sun span across two `%Y` years at New Year), `build_buckets` gap-fills + converts pence→pounds, `compute_summary` derives totals/net/savings-rate/averages. New `Repository.income_expense_series` (one grouped SQL pass + per-bucket FX), `income_expense_chart.py`, `income_expense_window.py` (top bar, chart + summary panel; Save/Save-As/dirty mirror the Spending window; no drill-down in E1), `income_expense_filter_dialog.py` (period + granularity + accounts checklist). Summary panel: total income/expense, net saved (sign-coloured), savings rate %, per-bucket averages. Wired into the New Report dialog, the Reports menu, and the bare/saved dispatch. Owner forks (`AskUserQuestion`): kind-based definition, income-up/expense-down + net line, display-currency selector, all four summary metrics. **Verified**: pure helpers (month/quarter/year/week enumeration incl. the New-Year `%W` straddle vs. live SQLite, gap-fill, summary, zero-income guard); Repository on a temp DB (single-currency buckets with transfers excluded; USD excluded with no rate; USD converted + folded in after a manual rate); offscreen Qt (window renders 2 buckets, summary populated, save→load round-trip).

### ADR-063 — Schedules access from the register + overdue/due-soon cue
Closes **A6**, the last item of the register tidy-up (Arc A). Schedules were reachable only from **Manage ▸ Schedules…** (two menu levels deep) with no ambient signal on the register that a bill was overdue or imminent — so a scheduled bill could slip past unnoticed. Adds a **"Schedules" button** to the filter bar (between ＋New Transaction and Reconcile) that opens the existing cross-account `SchedulesDialog` (reuses `_on_manage_schedules`, so Post Now / edits already refresh the register + sidebar). The button label carries a cue, computed by a new pure `account_summary.bills_due_summary(schedules, today, horizon_days=3)` (+ `BillsDueSummary` with `total`/`has_alert`): plain `Schedules` when nothing's pending, amber `Schedules ● N` when items fall due within 3 days (inclusive), red `⚠ Schedules (N)` (N = overdue + due-soon) the moment anything is overdue; the tooltip splits the count. Computed over **all** active schedules across every account (the dialog is cross-account); `today` is injected so the helper is pure and offscreen-testable. `_refresh_schedules_cue()` runs after the launch auto-post sweep (so a just-advanced auto-poster doesn't flash overdue), on schedule changes, and on window re-activation (a new `changeEvent`/`ActivationChange` override, since the due/overdue split is date-relative and the app can sit open across midnight). View-layer only — no schema/Repository/model change; best-effort (a DB error resets to the plain label). Owner forks (`AskUserQuestion`): the **"Schedules" label + count badge** (over "Bills"/bare dot — keeps the app's existing vocabulary, shows the count without opening the dialog) and counting **all** schedules incl. auto-post (over excluding auto-posters — matches the dialog's own "due in N days" summary). **Verified**: pure helper across overdue/due-today/+3-inclusive/+4-exclusive/far-future/auto-post and empty cases; offscreen Qt on a fresh temp DB drove the three button states (plain → amber `● 1` → red `(2)`) with correct colours + tooltips and confirmed the click handler is wired.

### ADR-061 — Register search performance (debounce + cached haystack + coalesced status)
Closes a freeze the owner hit: opening a busy account with **Show: All** and typing in the Search box froze the screen on every keystroke. Profiling the real DB (heaviest account = 13,550 rows on the All window) found three costs running synchronously per keystroke with no debounce: `filterAcceptsRow` rebuilt a 7-field haystack + two `f"{x:.2f}"` amount formats for *every* row (~15 ms/pass); `_update_status` walked every visible row (`mapToSource` + `Decimal` add, ~25 ms) and fired **2–3× per keystroke** because it was wired to `rowsRemoved` + `rowsInserted` + `layoutChanged`; and nothing debounced the typing, so a fast typist stacked ~90 ms passes back-to-back. This is the search-time follow-on to ADR-041's flagged "All is still slow on huge accounts" (ADR-041 made *load/sort* of All opt-in but left *search over* an All view untouched). Fix is all view/model-layer, no migration/schema/Repository change: **(a)** the Search box debounces through a 200 ms single-shot `QTimer` (stash text → restart timer → one `set_search` when typing settles); **(b)** `TransactionTableModel` caches each row's lowercased search blob (`_search_blobs`, index-parallel with `_rows`, built in `reload()` and refreshed in `setData`; `search_blob_at` exposes it), so `filterAcceptsRow` is a single substring test (~15 ms → ~2 ms/pass, verified byte-identical to the old inline logic across all 13,550 rows); **(c)** the four proxy signals route through a zero-delay single-shot timer that coalesces a filter invalidation's burst into one `_update_status` walk. Rejected: server-side SQL search (premature — 2 ms in memory now); disabling `dynamicSortFilter` (forward-typing pays no sort cost, so it targets the wrong case). **Verified** offscreen on the live DB: the heaviest account loads 13,550 rows + 13,550 blobs with 0 parity mismatches; a keystroke leaves the view unchanged until the debounce fires, then filters correctly (13,550 → 99 for "amazon"); the status walk over ~9.9k visible rows is one 25 ms pass.

### ADR-060 — Configurable grandfather-father-son snapshot retention
Amends ADR-057. Prompted by the owner asking to "let people configure snapshots… after 6 months there could be several GBs" once the Data Library screen (ADR-059) made the `Snapshots/` folder visible. The disk worry is inverted — the flat `SNAPSHOT_KEEP = 10` already bounds the folder — but it exposes the real defect: a busy day fires the 30-min timer well past 10 times, so keep-newest-10 holds only the last few hours and **every restore point older than this morning is already gone** (defeating ADR-016's "my data as of last Saturday"). Fix is the owner's own framing — *30-min on the day, then daily for a week, then monthly* — a **grandfather-father-son (GFS)** scheme: keep *all* snapshots within `subdaily_hours`, then *one per calendar day* back to `daily_days`, then *one per calendar month* back to `monthly_months`, dropping older (defaults 24h / 7d / 12mo). Two owner forks (`AskUserQuestion`): **editable tier values** (spin boxes, not presets) and a **capped** oldest tier (not kept-forever), so disk stays bounded (~today's captures + 7 daily + 12 monthly). Four knobs persist per file in the `setting` table (ADR-035) via a `RetentionPolicy` dataclass + `load_policy`/`save_policy`, floor-clamped so junk/zero can't disable retention. `prune` rewritten as `prune(db_path, policy, now)` — walking newest→oldest, keep-all / newest-per-day / newest-per-month / drop; a new `_stamp_of` parses the embedded filename timestamp (tolerating the `-N` collision suffix) and returns `None` for unrelated files so they're never deleted; `maybe_snapshot` prunes on both the wrote-a-snapshot and nothing-changed paths so an aging set self-thins on idle days. UI: a small `SnapshotSettingsDialog` (four `QSpinBox`es + a live plain-English summary) reached from a `Settings…` button on the Data Library Snapshots tab; Save persists + prunes immediately + emits, and the window re-arms its capture timer to the new cadence (and per-file on adopt, since policy travels with a loaded file). No migration (`setting` exists), no new dependency, pure-stdlib date math. **Verified** offscreen: a 14-month, every-6-hours set of 1680 fakes pruned to 25 (5 sub-daily / 7 daily / 13 monthly), nothing kept past the 12-month cap, one-per-day/month uniqueness, idempotent re-prune; policy save/load round-trip + floor-clamp; and dialog build / summary text / `policy_saved` → list-refresh + `settings_changed` relay.

### ADR-059 — Data Library: visual save / load of whole datasets
Answers the owner's "a way to open a file… a small screen showing saved data and the ability to load and save" — a visual library for juggling test datasets, since `Save Copy As…` / `Open…` (ADR-016) and the `Snapshots/` folder (ADR-057) are blind file-pickers with no view of what's saved. Two owner-resolved forks (`AskUserQuestion`): the screen lists **named saves *and* snapshots** (so it doubles as ADR-057's deferred "Restore from snapshot…"), and **Load takes a *fresh working copy*** — clones the chosen dataset *onto* the live working file so the **saved original stays pristine** (load a baseline, edit it, reload it clean), the decisive difference from `File ▸ Open`, which makes the picked file itself live. New `Library/` folder beside the live db, parallel to `Snapshots/` (one `pathlib` derivation, ADR-050). Qt-free `mfl_desktop/data_library.py` holds the at-rest ops: `list_saved`/`list_snapshots`, `library_path`/`sanitize_name`, `rename_saved`/`delete_file`, and `clone_database` — **read-only source** (`file:…?mode=ro`, so a load never migrates/mutates the pristine copy) written to a temp file via the backup API then **atomic `os.replace`**, so a failed clone leaves the working file intact. `mfl_desktop/ui/data_library_dialog.py` is the modal (tabs Saved datasets / Snapshots; Load / Save current as… / Rename / Delete); it emits `load_requested` and closes (loading replaces the live file — only the window can drive that). `register_window` splits `_swap_repository` into **`_adopt_repository`** + **`_teardown_repository`**; `File ▸ Open` adopts-then-tears-down, the new `_load_dataset` tears-down-then-clones-then-reopens; the loaded dataset's name shows in the title in place of the bench filename (`Ctrl+Shift+D` opens the screen). No schema change, no new dependency. **Verified** offscreen on a real Repository: save→library, load discards working-copy edits back to baseline, editing the loaded copy leaves the saved original pristine, a clone from a missing source leaves the bench byte-identical, plus dialog build / button-enable / signal-path and `sanitize_name`/`rename`.

### ADR-057 — Automatic rotating database snapshots + clean-close checkpoint
Closes the "save on close + auto-save" backlog item — but reframed by ADR-050 Tier-2, which had already made the default file a live, auto-committing `.mfl`, so "write the open file on close" was *already true*. Two real gaps remained: (1) we open in **WAL mode** but never checkpointed or closed on exit, so committed-but-uncheckpointed writes sat in the `.mfl-wal` sidecar — copying the bare `.mfl` silently dropped them; (2) auto-commit gives no protection against *logical* mistakes (a bad import persists just as faithfully). Fix: a `RegisterWindow.closeEvent` runs `Repository.checkpoint()` (`PRAGMA wal_checkpoint(TRUNCATE)`) + `close()` so the single file is self-contained; and **rotating timestamped snapshots** (`mfl_desktop/snapshots.py`) copied via `save_copy` into a `Snapshots/` folder beside the live DB on **launch + a 30-min in-session timer + clean close** (owner picked the most-coverage option), keeping the newest `SNAPSHOT_KEEP=10`. `maybe_snapshot` is best-effort (never blocks the UI) and **change-detects via `max(mtime(.mfl), mtime(.mfl-wal))` vs the newest snapshot** — the WAL mtime is the real signal since the main file's only moves on checkpoint — so the three triggers don't churn byte-identical copies. Restore reuses **File ▸ Open** (snapshots are ordinary, schema-upgradeable DBs); `_swap_repository` gives the file being *left* the same checkpoint+snapshot. Config is module constants (Preferences promotion deferred). **Verified** against a temp DB: snapshot written on change / skipped on no-change, rotation to `keep`, same-second collision suffixing, `wal_checkpoint(TRUNCATE)` zeroing the sidecar, and a snapshot opened back as a faithful populated copy; plus offscreen-Qt window construction confirming the launch snapshot, a live 30-min timer, and close.

### ADR-056 — Sankey report (income → total → expenses)
Builds the long-reserved `report.type='sankey'` (ADR-039): the owner's favourite view — income sources merge into a central Total that fans out to nested expense categories + a Savings node. A data reality shaped it: the owner's 206 Banktivity categories are **all `expense`/`transfer`, zero `income`**, and many transfers are recorded as account-name categories — so a `kind`-based Sankey is empty today and a sign-based one shows £96k of savings-transfers as top "income". The owner chose to fix category kinds manually (also unblocks the Budget), so the report is built **correct on `category.kind`** (income = inflows on income cats, expense = outflows on expense cats, transfers excluded) and comes alive as kinds are corrected. Rendering (owner picked nested-classic over flat-at-depth, threshold as % of total over % of parent): a paintEvent **tree-partition** chart (`sankey_chart.py`, no QtCharts per ADR-026) — every node has one parent on its side so ordering each column by its spine-ward neighbour means ribbons never cross; **spine height = max(income, expense)** with the shorter side balanced by a Savings or Deficit node; cubic-Bézier ribbons, hover tooltips. Controls are **inline** (not a modal, so toggling is quick): timeframe (YTD/MTD/Last-month/Custom), levels (depth), "hide below X%" (folds small nodes into "Other"), amounts/% switch; a summary panel shows income / expenditure / amount saved / saving %. New `Repository.sankey_category_totals` (period-scoped, reads `txn_category_line` for splits), `SankeyFilters` in `reports/filters.py`, made selectable in `NewReportDialog`, dispatched in `register_window` + a Reports-menu entry. Multi-currency is summed as bare pence (like the Spending report) — a display-currency pass is a follow-up. **Verified** offscreen on the live DB: filters round-trip; aggregate excludes transfers + scopes by period; depth 1→3 expands nested columns (19→27 painted nodes); threshold folds into "Other"; Savings/Deficit balance the short side; amounts + percent both paint; selectable + opens bare/saved.

### ADR-087 — Home budget card measures spend against envelope available
The Home dashboard's budget card flagged **"over"** while the Budget window showed the same month **under**. Both read the same `compute_matrix`, but the card compared spend to `cell.allocation` (this month's fresh assignment — the header's *Assigned* figure) while the Budget window compares to `cell.available` (`allocation + carry_in`, the rolled-over envelope balance — the ADR-058 model). The card now reads `cell.available`, so the two agree. One-field fix in `home_dashboard._budget_card`; amends ADR-075.

### ADR-088 — Income Over Time report + category filter on Income & Expense
A new saved-report type mirroring Spending Over Time for **income** (strict inflow: `kind='income'` AND `amount>0`). Rather than duplicate ~1,400 lines, `SpendingReportWindow` was generalised over a small frozen `_Direction` descriptor (kind / type / labels / repo-method / value-key); `IncomeReportWindow` is a one-attribute subclass, so the two variants share the chart, rollup, drill-down, filter dialog and save/load and can't drift. Adds `Repository.income_aggregates`, an `IncomeOverTimeFilters` subclass, a `kind` param on the shared filter dialog (hides the expense-only Uncategorised toggle), the `income_over_time` type (**migration 0028** widens the `report.type` CHECK), and menu/catalog/dispatch wiring. **Also amends ADR-064:** a Categories checklist + a `category_ids` clause on `income_expense_series`, with picked parents expanded to their descendants. **Verified** headless against a copy of the live DB.

### ADR-089 — Reinvested dividends (DRIP) as income
The owner's 401(k) records dividends as `ReinvDiv` — a single reinvest with **no cash leg** (`amount=0`; the dividend is held as `quantity × price`), so the cashflow income rule (`amount>0`) couldn't see them (143 rows, £80,299.13). Two changes: (1) reinvests become **user-categorisable** (amends ADR-086 — dialog Category field + inline register cell; safe because a reinvest is zero-cash, so its category never reaches the cash totals); (2) the Income Over Time report gains an *Include reinvested dividends* toggle (default on) that values them at `quantity × price` under their tagged category via a second `income_aggregates.include_reinvested` pass (no double count — the cash pass needs `amount>0`). New reinvests auto-tag on import: an Uncategorised reinvest falls back to a configured `reinvest_dividend_category_id`, which the dialog self-seeds when you file a reinvest under a category (no preferences screen — flat `setting` table). Units footnote: `price` is per-share **pounds** (a Buy's pence `amount` = `qty × price × 100`), so the valuation scales ×100. **Verified** headless (toggle adds exactly £80,299.13; import auto-tag end-to-end).

### ADR-090 — Exclude investment portfolio-move trades from the cashflow reports
The owner saw trades polluting the Payee report as a large **"(No payee)"** bucket — the tip of a deeper miscount: a Buy is `amount<0` on the Uncategorised (`kind='expense'`) category, so the strict-outflow rule counted **£1,852,934 of buys** as spending (≈36% of the raw expense total) across Spending, Payee, Category & Payee, and the expense side of Income & Expense + Sankey. A trade moves cash *within* the portfolio (cash ⇄ securities), so it's neither spending nor income. A shared `Repository._portfolio_move_exclusion` (buy/sell/share-move/reinvest/split = `affects_shares`, filtered by **txn id** since the split-unroll view lacks `action`) drops them from all five aggregates; **amended** the same day to the Home dashboard's Recent-activity feed (`list_recent_transactions`, by `action`). Cash distributions (Div/IntInc/cap-gain) and manual Cash in/out stay — they're real flows. `income_aggregates` is untouched (trades never reach its income side; reinvests are its deliberate, separately-toggled inclusion). **Verified**: Spending falls by exactly the trade total (£5,154,544 → £3,301,610); "(No payee)" drops from ~£1.85M to £5,696; income unchanged.

### ADR-091 — Surface auto-post failures, and guard category-kind changes that orphan schedules
The owner reported an auto-post expense schedule (Polestar 2 → "Asset Depreciation", −£450/mo) that sat overdue for *dozens* of launches and never posted. Root cause: its category had been switched expense→transfer (`change_category_kind`) after the schedule was created, leaving the schedule transfer-kind with `transfer_to_account_id = NULL`; `post_scheduled_txn` raised "Transfer schedule is missing a destination account." and the launch sweep `auto_post_due` **silently swallowed** it (`except Exception: break`) every single launch — the exact gap ADR-074 acknowledged and left open. Two fixes. **(1) Stop hiding failures:** `auto_post_due` now returns an `AutoPostResult` carrying both `posted` ids and `failures` (each an `AutoPostFailure` with `schedule_id`, a `"Account — Category (Payee)"` label, and the exception message); per-schedule failures are still caught (one bad schedule never aborts the launch) but recorded, not dropped. `RegisterWindow._run_auto_post_sweep` shows the posted count as before and now raises a `QMessageBox.warning` listing each skipped schedule + reason, pointing at Schedules → Post Now (ADR-074's repair path); a clean launch stays silent. **(2) Block the cause:** `change_category_kind`, when the new kind is `transfer`, refuses with a `ValueError` (surfaced by the Categories dialog) if any active schedule on the category or its descendants has no destination — naming the offenders and telling the user to set a destination or pick a non-transfer kind first. Refuse, not auto-repair: a destination is a user choice the system can't infer (same conclusion as ADR-074's post-time prompt). Return-type change to `auto_post_due` (only caller updated); no schema change, no migration. **Verified** offscreen on copies of the live file: the sweep returns `posted=[]` + a named failure for the broken schedule (previously a silent empty result); `change_category_kind(90, 'transfer')` is refused and names the schedule; an unrelated kind-change with no dependent schedules still succeeds.

### ADR-092 — Reopen the last-used file on launch
The owner's annoyance: quit + relaunch always reopened the **default** file in the default location, never the file they'd `File ▸ Open`'d and been working in. The launch resolver (`__main__.main`) kept no memory of the runtime open, and the obvious place to store it — the per-file `setting` table — is the wrong layer: it lives *inside* each `.mfl`, but the path has to be known *before* any file is open. So this is app-level, cross-file state, persisted in **`QSettings`** (the OS-standard per-user store: plist / registry / ini, one mechanism, no platform branch per ADR-050 rule 9). New `mfl_desktop/app_session.py` exposes `remember_last_db` / `last_db_path` (a no-arg `QSettings()` keys off the app's org + application names, so `main` now also sets `setOrganizationName(APP_NAME)`); the path is recorded whenever a file becomes the live file — at launch and on `File ▸ Open` (`_swap_repository`) — while a loaded dataset (`_load_dataset`) keeps the same working file and so is already remembered. Launch precedence is now `--db` → **last-opened (if it still exists)** → legacy cwd dev DB (`mfl_dev.mfl`/`.db`) → appdata default; last-opened sits above the cwd dev convenience so "reopen what I was working on" wins, yet a fresh checkout with nothing recorded still gets the dev file (and that first launch records it). A remembered file that exists but won't open (corrupt / not an MFL DB) falls back to the default instead of stranding the launch. No schema change, no migration, nothing written into any `.mfl`. **Verified** offscreen (isolated `QSettings`: round-trip; relative path stored absolute) + offscreen Qt (`_swap_repository` updates the remembered file from A to B; importing `__main__` raises no circular import). **Amended 2026-06-21 (transient-absence robustness):** an iCloud-Drive `.mfl` quit-then-relaunch opened the default instead — `last_db_path()` filtered on `exists()` so a not-yet-materialised iCloud file read as "unset", and the launch then re-recorded the fallback default, *clobbering* the pointer permanently (compounded by `Repository()` recreating any missing path). Now `last_db_path()` returns the recorded path without an existence check; the resolver checks existence itself and, on a remembered pointer it can't use this launch (absent or won't-open), opens the default **for the session only without overwriting the pointer** so the next launch retries once the file is back, and never hands a missing path to `Repository`. Verified offscreen: evict→fall back with pointer preserved; restore→reopen; missing file not recreated.

## Status values

| Status | Meaning |
|--------|---------|
| **Proposed** | Under discussion; not yet decided |
| **Accepted** | Decision made and adopted; the approach described is in effect |
| **Implemented** | Accepted and fully built; implementation notes may record divergences |
| **Superseded** | Replaced by a later ADR; kept for historical reference |
| **Deprecated** | No longer applicable but not replaced by a specific decision |
| **Parked** | Built and/or trialled, then set aside; kept as a record so a future attempt doesn't repeat it |

---

## Adding a new ADR

1. Copy the filename pattern: `ADR-NNN-short-description-of-decision.md`
2. Use the next available number in sequence
3. Fill in Context, Options considered, Decision, and Consequences
4. Set status to `Proposed` until the decision is agreed
5. Add a row to the index table and a summary paragraph above
6. Once agreed, update status to `Accepted`
